# 皇经集注

**The Collected Commentaries on the Original Acts of the Supreme Jade Emperor**

**Scripture Title:** *Collected Commentaries on the Original Acts of the Supreme Jade Emperor* (Abbreviated as *Collected Commentaries on the Jade Emperor Scripture*).

Compiled by Zhou Xuanzhen, a Daoist of the Quanzhen tradition during the Ming dynasty. This work gathers commentaries on the *Jade Emperor Scripture* from the Song, Jin, Yuan, and Ming dynasties, with an appended commentary on the *Jade Emperor’s Heart Seal Scripture*. Ten fascicles in total.

**Source of the Base Text:** *Wanli Continuation of the Daoist Canon*.

---

**Fascicle One of the Commentaries on the Jade Emperor Scripture**

**Preface to the Collected Commentaries on the Jade Emperor Scripture**

Composed by the Heavenly Marshal of Harmonious Response, the Heavenly Worthy of Concordant Virtue

The Great Dao is formless, yet it subtly initiates the myriad things;
The Perfect Truth is imageless, yet it gathers the hearts of all to return of their own accord.
Its mechanism is like a great bell—struck, it responds at once.
How vast is the Supreme Sage! Sincerity alone suffices to commune with it.

We reverently regard the *Original Acts Scripture* as the secret words of the Mysterious Emperor, the pivotal essence of the boundless heavens.
In the Floating Black True Realm, it records the first transmission of the Dao;
In the Purple Tenuity Upper Palace, it reveals the traces of its sealed mysteries.
Truly, it is the hidden melody of all heavens, the immortal verses of the Great Brahmā.
When the Eight Trigrams faced ruin, it was due to the imperial brush;
When the thousand perfected stood in guard, it universally delivered the numinous spirits of humanity.
Who can fathom its kalpas? Who can know its ages?
For the multitudes of the great earth, deluded and lost, have forsaken their true nature, destroyed their original forms, and indulged in sensual desires, unable to cleanse themselves—thus the sacred text remained hidden.

Today, as jade emerges from Kun Mountain and pearls divide from the vast sea, we have obtained this luminous scripture, prostrating in awe and wonder.
It is said: those imprisoned in darkness, yearning for its wondrous meaning, may be redeemed at the source;
Those afflicted with chronic illness, gazing upon its virtuous resonance, may be instantly cured.
It is a torch in the gloom, a vessel upon the abyss—preserving the state, pacifying the household, aiding the living, and delivering the dead.
Inscribed on golden tablets and jade scrolls, its vastness is beyond measure.
Without reverence for the true wind, how can one grasp this principle?
I humbly set forth its essentials to enlighten those yet unenlightened.

---

**Preface to the Collected Scripture on the Original Acts of the Supreme Jade Emperor**

The Dao is fundamentally wordless, yet all scriptures are the traces of true sages’ discourse. Words reveal the Dao, and even sages and worthies do not abandon them.
Since the division of the Three Powers and the establishment of the teachings of names, principle has remained unified—yet the deluded may diverge from it, and divergence is not the Way.

Before the kalpas began, the Primordial Beginning sat in illumination. When the time and destiny were ripe, the perfected ones inquired of the Jade Emperor regarding his causal acts, and thus he expounded this scripture.
It is the most venerable of dharma categories, the foremost of numinous texts—no scripture since has equaled it.
Its true words are profound and recondite, eschewing ornate embellishment. Though its Brahmā-verse is self-contained, its purport is inexhaustible; even the sages cannot speak of it, nor can thought or contemplation reach it. Yet this scripture encompasses all, as clear as the palm of one’s hand.

Your servant, Zhang Zhong, served in the civil administration of the Zhou dynasty, entrusted with affairs by the Supreme Emperor. Upon hearing this scripture, he vowed to treasure and uphold it to the end.
When the Emperor reviewed the merits and transgressions of humanity, he recorded that your servant Zhong walked the path of loyalty and filial piety, and commanded him to oversee the transformation of the Nine Heavens and compile this scripture.
Within its profound mysteries, he savored its richness to the fullest.

Alas! Those who study this scripture in the world fail to embody the sagely intent, to grasp the profound essence. Erroneous carvings and misguided transmissions have led to distortions in its verses, splitting it into two names—*Cavernous Mystery* and *Supreme*—each clinging to private interpretations in transmission, greatly deviating from the intent of the scripture’s exposition. Some even adhere rigidly like tuning pegs to a zither.
The reckless and absurd may disbelieve this scripture, or claim it borrows from other texts, or force interpretations in ignorance—all unaware of the scripture’s supremacy, and that the retributions of blessings and misfortunes cannot be escaped. How grievous is their error!

Your servant Zhong could not bear the loss of this magnificent canon, nor the folly of the vulgar world, which, in ignorance, offends without hearing the Great Dao.
He memorialized the Emperor’s command, enlisting immortal perfected ones to explicate the scripture’s meaning, disseminating it among the mortal realm as the key to exhaustive study and the ladder to the human Dao.
May this sacred canon serve as a vessel, rescuing those long drowned;
May this wondrous medicine of the Mysterious Tradition readily cure chronic ailments.
Those who hear the scripture and awaken to the Dao shall never speak recklessly;
Those who respond to the moment and recognize the true shall forever escape the wheel of rebirth.
Across the three thousand great thousand worlds, every realm shall become a domain of supreme harmony;
From kalpa to kalpa, every generation shall be a scene of joy and benefit.
Those who seek the Dao shall surely attain it; no wish shall go unfulfilled.
The merit of this scripture shall thus be without fail.

I respectfully inscribe this preface.

**Zhang Zhong, Minister of the Nine Heavens’ Civilizing Transformation and the Venerable Emperor of Literary Florescence, prostrates and bows a hundred times.**

---

**On the Original Dao**

Composed by the Venerable Immortal of the Southern Culmen, the Aged Recluse

The Venerable Immortal of the Southern Culmen says: Tracing the origins of Daoist teachings, we find that in the primordial chaos before separation, the human Dao was not yet complete. Heaven commanded our Dao Ancestor, the Yellow Emperor of Xuanyuan, to inherit the mandate of the Nine August Ones, to grasp the reins of the Six Dragons and ascend the heavens, to establish the celestial pole on behalf of Heaven, and to stabilize the Three Powers.

At that time, Heaven and Earth had not yet become distinct; there were no written characters, so knotted cords served in place of governance. There were no houses, so people dwelt in nests and caves. There were no garments, so they bound grasses to cover their bodies. There were no utensils, so they drank from cupped hands and hollowed vessels. Our Dao Ancestor, the Yellow Emperor of Xuanyuan, first created written characters, fashioned clothing, built palaces, and crafted utensils, thereby completing human affairs.

Among the Nine Schools and within the Three Teachings, the written characters in use, the clothing worn, the houses inhabited, and the vessels employed all originated with the Yellow Emperor—all derived from the teachings of our Daoist school and the Yellow Emperor. Moreover, Laozi said that what gives birth to Heaven, Earth, humanity, and the myriad things must itself have a source, which he did not know by name, so he provisionally called it the *Dao* and provisionally wrote it as *Great*, hence the *Great Dao*. Its teaching is called *Daoism*, and from this the world first acquired the term *Dao*.

Thus, all who speak of cultivating the Dao or studying the Dao are borrowing Laozi’s words and using *Dao* as their name. Are they not disciples of Laozi? Furthermore, Laozi’s phrase “mysterious and yet more mysterious, the gateway to all wonders” has also been borrowed and used in scriptures—all employing Laozi’s words. Likewise, the *Book of Zhuangzi* states: “Only after the Great Awakening does one know the sage.” These two characters, *Great Awakening*, were coined by Zhuangzi; Emperor Huizong of Song later adopted them to honor the Golden Immortal. All such terms in the scriptures derive from the writings of our Daoist school, from the teachings of the Yellow Emperor, Laozi, and Zhuangzi.

In the preface to the *Commentary on the August Scripture*, it is said: The character *Dao* is revered equally by the Three Teachings. Yet reckless and deluded fools regard the Dao as a lesser vehicle, showing their ignorance. The Jade Emperor is honored by all Three Teachings. Some blind followers call him the Heavenly Lord and criticize this as insufficiently reverent, failing to understand the root and origin of the Jade Emperor’s conduct. The Emperor’s virtue is boundless; his merits, once accomplished, are indestructible. His position is most exalted, his name most supreme; he governs the myriad heavens and encompasses the Three Teachings. Across the three thousand great thousand worlds, he moves through kalpas with effortless mastery. Confucians call him the Supreme Emperor; Buddhists name him Dipamkara; Daoists title him the Mysterious Lord—his dignity is peerless.

Whoever reads this scripture will understand the Emperor’s wondrous deeds and resolve millennia of doubts and myriad confusions. Yet those who remain ignorant, who do not grasp the scriptural text, continue to speak recklessly, failing to awaken and thereby deepening their transgressions. How can they recognize that human life originates from the Dao, is governed by the Supreme Emperor, and is enlightened by the sagely teachings? To slight the Emperor is to disrespect Heaven; to slander the scripture is to fail to comprehend the Great Dao—this is to turn one’s back on one’s roots and forget one’s origins, to misunderstand the source of life and creation.

I, Yan, have long lamented this and thus place this preface at the beginning of the commentary as a warning.

**Minister Lü Yan, the Pure Yang Admonishing and Transforming Protector Emperor, prostrates and bows a hundred times in reverence.**

---

**Preface to the Second Continuation of the *Collected Commentaries on the August Scripture***

The existence of scriptures for the Dao is like the sun and moon in the sky or the statutes and canons of a nation. Gazing upon the sun and moon prevents the folly of facing a wall; following the laws of former kings ensures no transgressions. Thus, venerating and believing in the true scriptures is surely the standard for entering the Dao.

Moreover, this scripture was personally transmitted by the Primordial Beginning, proclaimed by the Jade Emperor and the various deities—it is the highest rank among the Three Teachings, the secret words of the Great Sage, worthy of reverence in every place and esteemed in every kalpa. Yet the Dao is wordless; this scripture has already given it form through language. Why then is a commentary needed? The scripture, expressed in written words, is understood only by those who have attained the Dao. For those who have not yet entered the gate, it is deeply dependent upon this.

Otherwise, crossing a river without a raft—how can one reach the shore? Alas! To abandon the scripture in seeking the Dao is wrong; to cling to the scripture as the Dao is also wrong.

To contemplate the scripture with the heart, to verify the heart through the scripture—when heart and spirit merge in understanding, this Heavenly Treasure Divine Chapter is inherently within our nature. With true illumination, one does not cling to the written word, so how could the two errors arise?

Long Spring, Assistant to Transformation and Illuminated Responder, Perfected Lord Qiu Chujī, bows his head a hundred times in reverence.

**Preface to the First Four Chapters of the *Imperial Scripture Collected Commentaries***

The greatness of the Dao and the majesty of the Jade Emperor—the sacred profundity of the *Imperial Scripture*—your servant Zhen has long known. Yet the world, in its ignorance, raises reckless arguments, as if the Dao could be abandoned, Heaven profaned, and the sacred scripture treated lightly. How could this be so? Just as the Dao has its scripture, so the nature has this body; just as Heaven has its Emperor, so the body has its Heavenly Lord. Without the illusory body, the nature would have nothing to adhere to, and its wonders would not manifest; without the Heavenly Lord, the body would have no master, and its form would be empty. If body and heart cannot be without these, then how can one fail to repay the Emperor’s grace or believe in the scripture’s merit?

Yet belief in the scripture is not merely about the written word—it is through the heart’s spiritual communion. If one truly attains and does not forget, the wondrous fruit is achieved.

Minister Deng, Heavenly Lord and Marshal of Thunder, bows his head a hundred times in reverence to compose this preface.

**Three Praises**

Your servant, Heavenly Lord Deng, bows his head and speaks:

**Three Praises**

**Praise**
Vast is the Supreme Dao, without peer among the highest perfected.
**Dao**
Transcendent across the Three Teachings, this alone is revered.

**Praise**
August is the Jade Emperor, unmatched among the Three Teachings.
**Emperor**
Through kalpas vast as desert sands, ever does one return to the Most Honored.

**Praise**
August is the sacred canon, subtle and profoundly deep.
**Canon**
Encompassing the Three Teachings, its dharma-treasures stand supreme.

---

**Preface to the First Compilation of the *August Canon* with Collected Annotations**

The Sage of Propagation did not speak of the numinous, yet revered the service of the Supreme Emperor; Confucians shunned discourse on the mysterious, yet earnestly upheld the learning of the heart. The Supreme Emperor was indeed never treated lightly by the Confucians, yet none observed the Daoist scriptures, grasped the profound intent, or fused the Three into One. Was this due to sectarian exclusivity? Or was the practice of the Dao too pressing to allow for it? Alas, how narrow!

The matter does not lie in clinging to names; the Dao values only true benefit. If the profound scriptures were not so, how could they speak of the Dao? If they are so, how do they differ from the Confucians—why then should one be so rigidly bound?

Your servant Hongxian, from youth, studied the teachings of Confucius and once delved into the profound canon, glimpsing as if an attainment, though dared not presume it certain. Later, passing the imperial examinations and dwelling at Golden Phoenix Slope, I was able to peruse the books of the Three Teachings and came to know that none is more revered than the Dao, none deeper than the profound. Among the Three Teachings, no text surpasses the *August Canon*—as indispensable as beans, grain, cloth, and silk. Its profound meanings are difficult to fathom; the commentaries of the immortals must not go untransmitted. Thus, I took refuge beyond the worldly realm and piously compiled this volume. Yet my frail body daily weakened, and I had not the means to publish it. Later, I encountered a recluse from Jinan in Shandong, Zhou Yunqing, who lectured on the profound canon and edited the *Daoist Canon*. I entrusted my humble words to my friend, the Unskillful Daoist, to pass on to him.

In the winter of the thirteenth year of the Wanli reign, the former *zhuangyuan* Fang Yichen of Jiangxi, Luo Hongxian, bows in reverence to compose this preface.

**Preface to the Compilation of the *August Canon* with Collected Annotations**

The difficulty of speaking of the Dao has long been so.

Your humble servant, Xuan Zhen—a dull-witted rustic of the wilds, unworthy to speak of the Dao—how could I presume to compile the *Daoist Canon* and assemble the *Collected Annotations to the August Canon*? It is like an ant attempting to bear a mountain, revealing only my incapacity. Yet the Great Dao does not reject the lowly, and even humble study may yield understanding. Though the Jade Canon is profound, the immortals have elucidated its mysteries. When the late Grand Historian Luo entrusted this work to me, to omit it from the Canon would be to conceal a celestial treasure; to include it, however, left me uneasy. I feared my shallow insights might fail to harmonize with the immortals’ intent, forcing me to regurgitate half-digested interpretations that would provoke revulsion, distorting the sublime flavor of the Dao and compounding my offense.

Alas! True clarity in exposition is rare in this world. For this dull and unworthy servant to undertake such a task is to invite failure and guilt. Yet my resolve lies in practicing the Dao, and even Confucius did not shun criticism for such a cause. Who am I to evade blame and abandon this completed work? If those of noble spirit and deep understanding, upon reviewing my humble efforts, take pity and further illuminate the text to expound its meaning, then this compilation will not have been in vain.

Respectfully inscribed.
In the fifteenth year of the Wanli reign, your devoted servant Zhou Xuan Zhen of Shandong, compiler of the *Daoist Canon*, bows in reverence.

**Preface to the Transcription of the *Collected Annotations to the August Canon***

To practice the Dao and propagate one’s name is to honor one’s forebears. This is what the world calls “loyalty perfecting filial piety”—a principle upheld through the ages. Your servant Jingcui, having studied the Confucian classics in youth, knew of the Heavenly Emperor’s majesty but not that the practice of the Dao transcends worldly achievement—this I only later came to understand. After following my Daoist master, Zhou Yunqing, in compiling the *Daoist Canon* and attending to its transcription, I studied the *Annotations to the August Canon* and realized that the Three Teachings share a single principle, and the nature of the Dao is undivided. This canon directly points to the profound essentials; to awaken to it is to exhaust the Dao. Thus, I have presumptuously placed this preface at the head of the volume as self-admonition.

In the summer of the sixteenth year of the Wanli reign, your devoted servant Wang Jingcui, a Daoist practitioner in the capital, bows in reverence to inscribe this.

**Examination of Key Principles**
**Investigation of the Origins of the Dao**

**Investigation of the Origins of the Dao**

The Dao in its essence is formless and nameless—who could fathom its source, or from what would one begin to examine it? Yet since the Primordial Beginning divided and transformed, the Great Void conceived wondrous existence, and the Dao’s mysteries became manifest, names were thereby established. The True One embraces the Three, and the Three Teachings stand therein. Being and non-being, end and beginning—none lie beyond the Five Phases. Aeon after aeon they give rise to one another; sage after sage they transmit the lineage—all is the Dao. Even those who leap beyond the Three Realms and stand apart from the Five Phases cannot escape being counted among those who attain the Dao. Thus, the Dao’s revelation is the very origin of the term "Daoist school." Therefore, we first examine this in our search for the origins of the scriptures.

**Investigation of the Origins of the Scriptures**

Scriptures serve to convey the Dao, acting as the compassionate vessel for delivering the world. All scriptures are the sacred teachings of perfected beings, containing nothing but the supreme principle. Yet this scripture unfolds from the Primordial Beginning and takes its transformative source from the Jade Emperor. The Primordial Beginning is the foremost of the Three Teachings; the Jade Emperor is the origin of the myriad dharmas. This scripture is of the utmost mystery and wonder, uniquely crowning the Three Teachings; it is also the sovereign of all scriptures, enduring through infinite kalpas. Its revelation extends from the beginningless past, concealed in the Dark Heavens and treasured within the Jade Summit. Its characters are no ordinary script—each spans a full *zhang*, their radiance boundless. The Heavenly Perfected Sovereign, responding to the times, took up his brush and transcribed it for transmission to the world. Such is the origin of this scripture’s promulgation. Thus, we continue our investigation by tracing the lineage of the Dao’s transmission.

**Investigation of the Lineage and Manifestations of the Jade Emperor, Supreme Master of the Myriad Dharmas and Sacred Ancestor of the Mysterious Teachings**

Masters deliver the world, shattering delusion and rescuing beings from suffering. They transmit the Dao and bestow scriptures, opening the future and continuing the past. The Great Dao’s Mysterious Master unifies the Three Teachings, encompasses the myriad dharmas, dwells in the Heaven within Heaven, and stands as the Sage among Sages—without beginning or end, his origin transcends all inquiry, existing before the ten thousand forms. Yet the Dao’s wondrous manifestations divide into truth: he appears in the Radiant and Majestic Land of Joy, a manifestation from a past kalpa. The world observes the luminous yang of the celestial Dao—yang governs bestowal, its mechanism ever active—hence they honor the Emperor as the Great Emperor Zhang. The deluded, failing to grasp this principle, mistakenly claim that the Zhang clan of Xingtang in the former Northern Zhili (now Hebei) are descendants of the Jade Emperor. How could they know that the Xingtang Zhang clan are merely descendants of Zhang Guo and successors of Zhang the Immortal? How could these be conflated in discussion? This is but an investigation of surnames and worldly lineages.

If we discuss lineage, the Jade Emperor is the foremost emanation of the Great Dao, the primordial ancestor of kalpas vast—how could he have birth, death, or a mortal name? The Jade Emperor’s sacred consort, divine children, and retinue were all palace attendants from his time as Radiant and Majestic Crown Prince. When the Emperor ascended, his entire court attained the Dao. Essentially, the Empress and her attendants were not truly female in form; all were celestial perfected beings. To deliver the multitude of beings, they manifested as female bodies—this has already been explained. It is like the Buddha attaining the Way while his wife and children achieved sagehood. Regard the Jade Emperor as the progenitor of the Dao: the myriad beings of countless kalpas, all life born of heaven and earth, are but offshoots of the Dao’s lineage. Who among them is not part of the Jade Emperor’s retinue and system? Once the attendants of the Great Brahma Palace attain the Dao, they become celestial perfected beings. For example, Mañjuśrī presides over the Immaculate World, and the Dragon Girl attained the Way and transformed into a male body—this principle is the same. Yet today’s monks, Daoists, and laypeople, failing to grasp this truth, mistakenly believe the Jade Emperor has a mortal court, undergoes rebirth, and attains only the Two Vehicles’ fruition. How could they know that while the heavens may perish, the Three Clarities’ realm and the Great Brahma Heaven are imperishable? While the gods of the heavens undergo rebirth, the Jade Emperor does not. For the Jade Emperor is the embodiment of the Dao, and the Dao is boundless—how could the Jade Emperor be finite? Truly, he is the supreme teacher of all Buddhas of the One Vehicle, the King of the Myriad Heavens, and his court is but the wondrous transformation of the Dao. Such is the outline of the profound lineage. Scholars must not speak carelessly; let them examine this investigation in detail.

**Record of the Merits of Engraving Scriptures**
In the most ancient times, scriptures had no paper or brushes; they were recorded on bamboo and wooden slips. When Meng Tian and Cai Lun invented paper and brushes, scriptures were transcribed thereafter. Later, lofty scholars engraved printing blocks to reproduce them, doubling the merit. Yet deluded followers of heterodox paths, unaware that Meng and Cai received blessings in Tuṣita Heaven, claim these two men suffered karmic retribution in hell. In truth, the two descended into the underworld under the guidance of the Most High Lord of Salvation from Suffering and the Underworld Lord Kṣitigarbha Bodhisattva, bearing scriptures to deliver those condemned for heretical teachings. How could they have endured hell’s torments? Their merit was immense, for they advanced the propagation of scriptures and teachings.

**Record of the True Benefits of Recitation, Dissemination, and Exegesis**
Recitation and exegesis require utmost sincerity, free from defilement, attachment, or delusion—such merit accords with the scriptures’ words. Printing and distributing scriptures yield even greater merit, for they widely disseminate the Dharma’s treasures. To treat scriptures lightly, slander them, or defile them incurs grave transgressions. Be diligent, be warned, and do not betray the teachings of sages and worthies.

**Investigation of the Jade Emperor’s Sacred Titles and Their Variations**
The Jade Emperor’s sacred titles have been revered since before the kalpas vast; in the middle ancient era, they were further exalted and repeatedly praised. As worldly rulers embraced the Dao and received the mysterious grace, each honored what they witnessed and revered. Matters aligned with the times, and merits manifested in the world. As their manifestations became evident, all people saw and heard, venerating the titles of the various deities to establish proper appellations. There are four Jade Emperors: the first is the Great Tenuous Jade Emperor, the title bestowed by Emperor Wu of Han upon the ruler of the Great Tenuous Enclosure; the second is the Brahma Heaven Jade Emperor, the title bestowed by Emperor Xuan of Han upon the ruler of the Heavenly Market Enclosure; the third is the Fiery Splendor Lesser Tenuous Jade Emperor, the title bestowed by Emperor Ai of Han upon the precelestial fixed position; the fourth is the Purple Ultimate Jade Emperor, the title bestowed by Emperor Guangwu of Han upon the postcelestial Qian trigram. None of these are this Jade Emperor. This Jade Emperor’s titles are Supreme Sovereign of the Golden Portal of the Vast Heaven, the Most Honored, the Spontaneously Wondrous Existent, the Perfected of Miraculous Radiance, the Jade Sovereign Lord of Heaven, also called the Most High August Jade Emperor of the Mysterious Firmament. He governs all heavens, eternally indestructible and imperishable. Yet the world, failing to investigate thoroughly, erroneously equates him with Śakra, unaware that the Jade Emperor’s titles differ entirely. The four Jade Emperors are all under the dominion of the Most High Jade Emperor. Those who speak of the Four Heavenly Emperors as equals of this Jade Emperor are also mistaken. Those who comprehend heaven will understand this.

**Investigation of the Jade Emperor’s Governance and Supreme Authority**
Master Ge Xian said: The heavens of the world appear the same to all. Confucians speak of one heaven and earth, one Lord on High. Daoists speak of thirty billion myriad great Dharma realms, each with thirty-six heavens, each heaven with its own emperor—all under the dominion of the Most High Jade Emperor. Buddhists speak of three thousand great thousand-worlds, each with thirty-two heavens, each heaven with its own Jade Emperor. The three teachings’ discourses seem divergent. Yet when they speak of one heaven, they refer to the Great Void beyond, acknowledging its boundlessness, hence the thirty billion myriad. Beyond this, they also speak of the inconceivable. When they speak of three thousand great thousand-worlds, beyond this, they also speak of the immeasurable. Thus, Confucians speak of following the Lord’s decree and say the sage emulates heaven. Heaven’s essence is boundless; even through kalpas, epochs, and generations, this principle holds. Therefore, the Lord on High is unchanging. Daoists speak of the Most High’s formless void, the true Emperor as indestructible; Buddhists speak of true suchness and self-mastery, eternally unretrogressive. All affirm that the Jade Emperor is imperishable. Thus, to speak of one heaven is not to neglect the vast; it is to name the whole, which is nondual with the profound and the Buddhist. To speak of thirty billion myriad or three thousand great thousand-worlds is not a falsehood; it is to enumerate parts, which aligns with the Confucians. As for the Buddhist claim that each heaven has its own Jade Emperor, each realm has its own ultimate. The Daoist claim that all realms share this Jade Emperor means all realms are one and infinite. Whether called the Great Void, the inconceivable, or the immeasurable, all know the Dao is unchanging and the Jade Emperor eternally present. If one divides worlds and claims the Jade Emperors differ, does this mean the principle of infinity is dual? If one asserts that with the passage of kalpas the Lord on High perishes, does this mean the principle of infinity is destructible? Knowing the Dao is indestructible, the Jade Emperor is eternally present. This is certain; do not cling to demonic doctrines to slander the sacred.

**Investigation of the Jade Emperor’s Pure Tenuous Heavenly Realm**
Wang Chongyang said: The Pure Tenuous is the most profound and subtle realm of heaven, what Daoists call the Heaven of the Seeded People, Confucians call the Beyond of the Vast and Formless, the ever-indestructible azure expanse, and Buddhists call the unretrogressive realm.

Within the miscellaneous writings of Chan Buddhism, erroneous claims place the Jade Emperor atop Mount Sumeru, identifying Him with the Heaven of the Sun and Moon or the Heaven of the Four Kings—realms subject to destruction—while asserting that only Maitreya’s Inner Court remains an unretrogressive domain. Some further speak of the "Milo Enclosure" or "Mila Garden," three variant names derived from the Daoist scriptures’ Supreme Primordial Lord, referring to the same transcendent realm: the Pure Tenuous Heaven of the Jade Emperor’s abode in the Mysterious True Realm of Milo. The Heaven of the Sun and Moon and the Heaven of the Four Kings, however, are but the dwelling of the Supreme Tenuous Jade Emperor, not that of the Most High Heavenly Worthy, the Supreme Jade Emperor. Thus, the Daoist scriptures state: "Atop the Mysterious Valley Mountain resides the Imperial Lord, who pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy, the Most High Jade Emperor." The Mysterious Valley Mountain is none other than the Chan Buddhist Mount Sumeru, where the Lord of the Sun and Moon governs as the deity presiding over this heaven—akin to the present-day Prefect of the Imperial Capital. Hence, the Buddhist sutras describe the scene of the Tathāgata expounding the Dharma while Śakra, Lord of the Devas, holds an umbrella overhead, much like a newly minted *zhuangyuan* ascending the golden hall, where the Ministry of Rites raises a toast, and the Prefect of the Capital unfurls an umbrella to signify the court’s honor for the worthy. Yet heretical currents have mistaken Śakra, who merely holds the umbrella, for the Most High Jade Emperor, as if equating the Prefect of the Capital with the Emperor himself. Such errors are egregious, and distortions of this kind abound.

Within these miscellaneous writings, it is further claimed that Mount Kunlun has eight distinct locations. Though the eight directions may be spoken of, they ultimately converge in the northwest—the Qian trigram’s head, the Kunlun of the northwest. What the Confucians call the "Pillar of Heaven and the Web of Earth" is none other than the Daoist Mysterious Valley Mountain and the Buddhist Mount Sumeru. How could there be eight such mountains? Yet the world has long perpetuated this misconception, and thus, in examining the Pure Tenuous Heavenly Realm, these errors are addressed to caution those who propagate such fallacies.

**Investigation of the Jade Emperor’s Rank of Honor**
Liu Haichan said: Within Daoism, the Jade Emperor is the transformation of the Three Pure Ones. The Daoist tradition first speaks of the Three Pure Ones as preceding the Void and Nothingness before the Wondrous Existence, referring to the Wuji and Taiji—realms without distinction of honor or inferiority. In Buddhism, He is Dipamkara Buddha, manifesting as the body of Śākyamuni Buddha. Chan Buddhists prioritize the Buddha over the Jade Emperor, reflecting the foreign custom of revering their own sovereign before the Emperor of China. Yet when examining the Dao’s hierarchy of honor, *The Golden Wheel Sutra* states: "The Jade Dipper’s Mysterious Mandate rides forth, as the spirit soars to the Supreme Ultimate. The Five Planets lead as envoys, while Śakra and Brahmā serve as attendants." Śakra and Brahmā here represent the immortals, Buddhas, and bodhisattvas. The Emperor’s trust in the Three Pure Ones and the Buddha is but a manifestation to guide sentient beings toward the Dao. Yet worldly currents, failing to trace the source, arbitrarily assign ranks, demoting the Jade Emperor to a secondary honor—as if there were beings in the world greater than the Emperor. Some even compare the Three Pure Ones and the Buddha to retired emperors, distorting the sequence of the Jade Emperor’s prior and subsequent manifestations. To liken those of different surnames and titles to father and son is an even graver transgression.

Alas! Just as the world cannot exist without the Jade Emperor, so too must all life have ancestors and parents. To slander the Supreme Emperor and establish rival sects is to abandon one’s ancestors and parents in pursuit of self-exaltation. How can this be permitted?

**Investigation of the Jade Emperor’s Beneficent Titles**
Lan Caihe said: People know to revere the Supreme Emperor but do not invoke His sacred titles. Some Confucians claim that reciting them is improper, unaware that Mencius spoke of "the great filial son who cherishes his parents all his life." To cherish one’s parents with a sincere heart is to be a filial child; to invoke the Emperor’s titles with a sincere heart, ensuring no transgressions, is this not to be a true child of Heaven and Earth? To embody the form perfectly is to align with Heaven and Earth, and the benefits shall be boundless.

**Investigation of the Benefits of the *August Emperor’s Scripture***
Zhang Ziyang said: Where there is the rise of an emperor, there must be the establishment of imperial institutions. Those who adhere to these institutions do not err. How much more so with the *August Emperor’s Scripture*, the heart-seal of the Dao’s essential teaching? To embody it is to become a sage—how could it merely prevent transgressions? Yet people today doubt its benefits, for they have not sincerely practiced its recitation and upholding. Let the wise reflect on this.

**Investigation of the Merits and Transgressions in Collating the Emperor’s Scripture**
Zhongli Zi said: All beings arise from the Dao, their true nature derived from the Heavenly Emperor. Thus, virtue moves Heaven, and blessings naturally follow. Even in poverty and lowliness, one’s peace and joy surpass others—this is the true Hall of Blessings. Evil, however, is self-inflicted calamity, as Heaven sends down misfortune. Even in wealth and nobility, one’s misfortune and woe become a living hell. Fortune and misfortune are fixed, following one’s goodness or evil; the resonance between Heaven and humanity is swifter than an echo. Yet deluded beings do not believe, and thus the merit-recorded adage states: "To truly recite one volume of the *August Emperor’s Scripture* is to accumulate a thousand virtues, ascending to the Heavenly Hall." True recitation unifies inner and outer, aligning speech and conduct with the Dao—not merely chanting the scripture with the mouth, but embodying goodness in every thought. How excellent!

Wang Lingguan said: "Why trouble skilled hands to depict my image? I only wish your heart aligns with mine." To align one’s heart with the Supreme Emperor is to cultivate virtue and blessings in tandem—this is true recitation and meritorious goodness. All else—reciting scriptures, restraining speech, and disciplining the mind; venerating the prescribed years and months—though blessed, yields results commensurate with the magnitude of one’s goodness, and thus ranks secondary.

The transgression-recorded adage states: "To disbelieve this scripture is to fall into heretical paths, for a heart misaligned with the Dao becomes a heretic." It further warns: "To slander the true scripture is to descend into hell." Disbelief merely limits one’s awareness of the scripture’s merits, a minor transgression. Slander, however, abolishes Heaven’s sacred text. The mind commits grave deeds, inviting boundless misfortune and sinking into the darkness of yin, where the sins are inescapable, leading straight to hell’s path. It further states: "To revile the Emperor and slander the sages, to abolish the abodes of the gods and rend the true scriptures—such unrepentant wickedness incurs eternal karmic bonds, and the calamity extends to seven generations." Slander is to malign the sacred text with the mouth, defying Heaven’s majesty, and thus the sin rests upon oneself. To revile the Emperor and rend the scriptures is to persist in evil without remorse, embodying unvirtuousness and leaving an eternal stench. It dishonors the body and shames one’s kin, such that even a hundred generations of filial sons and compassionate descendants cannot undo it.

The sins of one’s own person—when shall they ever end? The transgressions of ancestors and kin—how could they ever be absolved? If not so, then when a state enacts laws to punish the guilty, why are there cases of exterminating three clans or eradicating nine lineages? It is because the crime is so grave that it extends to one’s kin. Thus, though the net of law may stretch wide, there are still those who cast perverse glances upon the scriptures, recite them without reverence, chant them with errors and disdain, or recklessly interpret and judge them, favoring one while disparaging another. According to the severity of their transgressions, there are corresponding retributions awaiting them.

Alas! The Emperor’s scriptures are the law of the present age. To defy the royal law is clearly stipulated in the statutes; to disregard the sacred canon—how could there be no heavenly decrees? How lamentable that the human form is so hard to attain, the supreme Dao so hard to encounter! Parents give birth to us, their toil and suffering the same. Those of virtue bring blessings to their ancestors, just as in this world, passing the imperial examinations and receiving noble titles honors one’s kin. Those of transgression bring calamity to their ancestors, just as in this world, when descendants commit crimes, the household head is held accountable. Though human forms are the same, good and evil differ; though parental kindness is the same, blessings and karma diverge. Why then do people not do good but willingly commit evil, needlessly burdening their ancestors and clans?

The scriptures’ system of merits and demerits states this clearly: the true scriptures reside in the human heart. When one is purely good, the scriptures’ power naturally manifests. The supremely wise act in accordance with the scriptures without reciting them aloud. Those of middling wisdom perceive the Dao through the scriptures, while the utterly foolish refuse to believe even when told. The supremely wise are rare, and the utterly foolish are not many; the majority are of middling capacity, so the work of teaching and transformation must not be neglected. How can those who study these scriptures fail to embody the Jade Emperor’s compassionate intent to deliver the world, treating them as mere common texts?

*An Examination of the Collected Commentaries on the August Scripture*
Master Shi Xinglin says: The *August Scripture* speaks the truth of the Dao, which is inherently present in our nature and thus requires no explanation. Yet people’s capacities vary, and partial views abound. Even the explanations of the immortals cannot fully convey its profound essence; they merely serve as a reference for later generations to reconcile differing interpretations.

*An Examination of the Similarities and Differences in the August Scripture*
Zhang Zifang says: Originally, this scripture had no alternate names or distinctions such as *Highest Numinous Treasure*. Later generations, through arbitrary judgments, added or removed words and phrases, forcing connections in the text and severely distorting its original meaning. Now, upon examination, *Highest Numinous Treasure* derives from the praises of various perfected immortals, but later people mistakenly took it as a separate title. Here, following the definitive judgment of the Mystic Capital, we record and transmit it to the world. Later scholars should bear this in mind, silently embodying its truth. If they encounter errors in transcription, transmission, or exposition, they should collectively verify and correct them. Any extraneous additions to the text or characters are all erroneous. Those of understanding should not cling rigidly to them.

*Preface to the Collected Commentaries and Transmission of the August Scripture*
Your disciple Zhou Xuanzhen, a humble cultivator of the Dao and successor of the Complete Perfection lineage from Xiaozhao in Shandong, prostrates with utmost reverence, bowing a hundred times in purification, and respectfully submits:

The Dao is wondrous and non-actional, yet it manifests according to the times; the human heart possesses awareness, and one should accumulate merit wherever one is. Though I, Xuanzhen, am but a lowly being, the least among the three realms, I aspire to return to the mysterious through the wondrous Dharma, merging Confucian conduct with the Dao. Upon glimpsing the Emperor’s scripture, I treasured it more than rare jewels. I studied it word by word, hoping to attain enlightenment through its text. Yet the sacred canon lacked annotations, making comprehension difficult. Thus, I humbly gathered explanations from various sources, compiling the sayings of immortals and sages into the Daoist Canon. For the three fascicles of true text, I arranged them in order; for the five ranks of secret discourses, I assigned chapter titles. The work spans ten fascicles, totaling six hundred pages, comprising one hundred and eight chapters and over one hundred thousand words. The heart-essence of a thousand sages is now clearly visible in these volumes; the profound principles of countless kalpas lie open before the eyes. Though I have not yet fully penetrated the mysteries of the supreme sages, I have at least made the most splendid true texts accessible to all. Having contributed this small effort, I trust that good affinities remain. Choosing an auspicious morning, I reverently carve the text, relying on the support of virtuous patrons to bring it to completion.

I submit this memorial in advance, hoping it may reach the mysterious gaze of the celestial realm, augmenting the pure blessings of ruler and people, and pardoning my humble presumption. May all realms and directions be fully illuminated by the seventeen radiant lights; may all ages, past and present, be molded by the thirty great vows. May all beings ascend to the profound mystery, and may both the living and the dead forever partake in the blessings of the Dharma. If even a fraction of my sincerity is realized, it will be more than enough.

Respectfully submitted.

*An Examination of the Sequence and Meaning of the Scripture’s Commentaries*
The original text of the scripture was sometimes presented as a single fascicle, following its original transmission, symbolizing the Supreme Ultimate. When divided into three fascicles, it symbolizes the Three Powers. The present commentary is arranged in ten fascicles, symbolizing the ten poles, for the Dao’s numbers are fulfilled in ten. The five ranks symbolize the five phases; combining the five phases, four images, and eight trigrams yields seventeen, all divisions of the Supreme Ultimate. Thus, the Emperor’s seventeen radiant lights enable Heaven to generate and Earth to complete. This scripture of the Jade Emperor is Earth’s way of nurturing the myriad things to perfection. The number of Earth is thirty, so the Emperor demonstrates thirty kinds of merit. The Emperor’s virtue surpasses the ten poles, hence his ten titles. Through eons of cultivation, his virtues are boundless. The present commentary’s six hundred pages symbolize the six hundred chapters of the *Fire Records*; its one hundred and eight chapters follow the Emperor’s one thousand eight hundred precepts. Its over one hundred thousand words symbolize the Emperor’s one hundred thousand wondrous acts and mysterious radiance.

As for the so-called *August Scripture Compendium*, it was compiled for those of lesser capacity who cannot fully grasp the sacred text, summarizing its essentials to instruct them. Knowing this principle, how could there be any conflicting interpretations?

*Precepts on Reading, Reciting, Expounding, and Transmitting the Scriptures*
When reading or reciting any scripture, or when expounding or transmitting it, one should first purify oneself, dress neatly, and arrange one’s countenance with solemnity before placing the scripture on a clean table. Sit upright, compose the mind, forget both good and evil, relinquish all views, and abide in serene emptiness. Only then should one calmly open the scroll—whether to silently read, recite aloud, elucidate, or teach—engaging with the Emperor as if in direct audience, maintaining utmost sincerity without interruption. This is how one upholds the precepts.

**On Copying Scriptures and Precepts**
When copying any scripture, the rules and rituals are the same as for reading or reciting. The mind must be upright, the brush held straight—not for the sake of fine calligraphy, but because this itself is the Dao.

**Distinguishing Variant Scripture Titles**
According to the *Baopuzi*: "Highest" (*Gaoshang*) refers to those above the seed-people, who have fulfilled heaven’s utmost limit, their elevation unmatched—what Buddhists call the "stage of non-retrogression."

The Jade Emperor is the most revered among sages, the most noble among spirits. All buddhas, sacred masters, and lords of the myriad heavens thus honor him as the Jade Emperor.

As Lü Chunyang said: "The Dao is peerless in its loftiness, hence ‘Emperor.’"

The Supreme Lord’s benevolence spans kalpas, his merits surpass all sages, perfectly good and perfectly beautiful—his praises are inexhaustible. Dwelling in the Jade Clarity Heaven, he proclaims the transformations of the Primordial Beginning, and so is titled the Jade Emperor.

Han Xiang said: *The Original Conduct* recounts the Jade Emperor’s foundational path to sagehood, his wondrous practices through eons. *The Collected Scriptures* gathers the five sublime discourses of the Primordial Beginning into one scripture, revealing the true path of cultivation for later generations.

Guangjian said: "Only heaven is supremely high." The heaven where the Jade Emperor dwells borders the Jade Clarity, yet transcends all heavens—hence "Highest." People, seeing the Jade Emperor’s exaltation, assume his virtue is unattainable, never realizing the sagely Dao is undivided: I stand shoulder to shoulder with the utmost sage. The Emperor’s loftiness, his wondrousness, are the fruits of his practice. Thus, the Heavenly Pivot Minister Zhang transmitted this scripture to inspire people to emulate the sage and attain perfection. The imperial decree states: *The Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct Collected Scriptures* aims to enlighten readers, enabling them to trace the noble causes of the past and follow the footsteps of the utmost sage, thereby becoming a perfected one.

Later, it is also titled *The Supreme Cavernous Mysterious Treasure Scripture*. "Supreme" (*Taishang*) signifies that which is immeasurably great and boundlessly high. It reveals the secrets of precelestial virtue, serving as the origin of all written teachings. "Cavernous Mysterious" (*Dongxuan*) denotes its illumination of the Three Luminaries and the manifestation of profound mysteries. The treasury of the mysterious and numinous is the dharma-treasure for countless generations of heaven-dwellers and humans—hence "Treasure" (*Lingbao*). In essence, scriptures elucidate the Dao, and the Dao resides within oneself. If one can fully realize their nature and destiny, awakening to this Dao, and practice it with wholehearted devotion, they may enter sagehood.

**On Believing in Scriptures and Discerning the Rise and Fall of Virtuous Karma**
Humans originate from the Supreme Ultimate. Heaven and hell are described in detail in the scriptures, yet the world remains skeptical—how could this be mere fabrication? Though death returns one to emptiness, those whose destinies are not exhausted possess souls bound by karmic deeds. Bo You became a malevolent spirit, and Zichan believed it; Confucius did not dismiss it. How could there be no hell? Those who purify themselves and return to the transformations of the old creation may ascend to heaven. Yet blessings cannot be seized by chance, nor can karma be evaded by luck. Heaven and hell are created by the human heart. To merely believe in their names without cultivating virtue is to invite disaster. Even if one speaks daily of karmic retribution, what benefit is there?

When reciting scriptures, there are purificatory incantations for the mind and the like, but they are not recorded here. Since earlier instructions taught that the mind should unite with the Dao, reciting with sincerity is itself the true incantation—thus their texts are not included.

The original version of *The Imperial Scripture* begins with the thirty-six sacred titles, corresponding to the thirty-six heavens. Why does the present scripture only include ten proclamations? The ten titles align with the ten supreme attributes of the Emperor’s appellation, not chosen for brevity or complexity. Readers should consider this carefully.

**Commentary on the *Highest Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct Collected Scriptures***
This commentary is a direct annotation of the *Cavernous Mysterious Treasure Scripture*; later readers should not doubt it.

**Prostrating in Reverence**
This scripture expounds the wondrous practices of the Jade Emperor as revealed by the Primordial Beginning. Thus, those who recite it should prostrate themselves in utmost reverence, sincerely offering their devotion.

Gazing upward, I invoke the Three Clarities’ realm,
The supreme and peerless lords of the Three Realms.
Knowing the loftiness of the Great Dao and the exaltation of the Three Clarities,
I aspire with earnest longing,
Returning body, spirit, and life,
To convey my true heart upward.

**Gazing in Reverence**
I invoke the Jade Clarity, High Clarity, and Supreme Clarity.
The Three Clarities’ realms are supremely exalted and peerless.
The Jade Clarity’s sacred realm is the Primordial Beginning,
The High Clarity’s true realm is the Numinous Treasure,
The Supreme Clarity’s immortal realm is the Dao and its Virtue—
The Three Realms’ ancestral Great Heavenly Worthies.

Gazing upward, I invoke the Great Canopy Heaven,
The supreme and mysterious vault of creation.
Lü Chunyang said: The Jade Emperor’s dwelling is the heavenly origin of the three-thousand-great-thousand worlds, forever beyond retrogression. Unmatched in height, it is called the Great Canopy. The Mysterious Vault Lord governs the boundless azure, sovereign of all heavens.

Gazing upward, I invoke the Three Clarities’ realms,
Where the assembled hosts of perfected beings attend the Celestial Throne.
Zhang Ziyang said: "Attend" means to stand in array. The Celestial Throne is the unfathomably profound realm, beyond sight or hearing. "Hosts" refers to the multitude. The assembled hosts of perfected beings include the precelestial Nine Celestial Thrones, the postcelestial immortals and sages, all gods, buddhas, bodhisattvas, arhats, and vajras—all are present therein.

The wondrous Dao is beyond thought and discourse,
The utmost and singular vehicle cannot be grasped by mind or speech,
Difficult to fathom through contemplation.

**Entering to Cultivate the Mysterious Gate**
Zhang Zifang said: "Entering" means to progress through true knowledge and practice. The "Mysterious Gate" is the gateway of the Dao. The manifold wonders of the mysterious are profound and impenetrable; gradual advancement leads to awakening and entry into the Mysterious. This aligns with Mencius’ "abiding in stability deepens one’s resources" and the Buddhist "progressing through hearing, reflection, and cultivation, ultimately attaining liberation."

**The Wondrous Scripture Reveals the Profound Mysteries**
"Reveals" means to uncover, to extract. "Profound mysteries" are the unfathomable and obscure. This wondrous scripture extracts the divine mechanisms from the true realm—this is the revelation of profound mysteries.

**Guiding the Deluded in the Dust**
The Primordial Beginning expounds the wondrous scripture, revealing profound mysteries to guide those lost in the mundane, delivering them from the sea of suffering and liberating them from karmic destinies.

**Now I Purify My Three Karmas**
"I" refers to the one reciting the scripture. The "Three Karmas" are the karmas of body, speech, and mind. "Purify" means to devote oneself sincerely and forever sever these karmas.

**Reciting with the Mouth and Upholding with the Heart.**

The reciter declares their sincerity in reciting this scripture.
With the mouth they chant, with the true heart they uphold and receive it.
Only hoping for great compassion,
to accept this servant’s plea.

*Compassion* is written in one version as *venerable*—*compassion* is correct.
In reciting and upholding this scripture, one only hopes that the Primordial Jade Emperor and all Perfected Ones will bestow great compassion,
open their merciful countenance,
and accept this servant’s prayer.
If written as *venerable*, it cannot carry the intent of the preceding three invocations.

The compassionate light illumines the lowly,
the divine hearing attends to the recited sounds.
May the great compassionate light of all sages illumine this servant’s humble and sincere heart.
May the divine hearing listen to the sounds of prayer and recitation.

Hoping that when this servant chants the scripture,
its Dharma-sound resounds through the ten directions.
May the recitation of this scripture cause its Dharma-sound to reverberate through the ten directions,
so that all in the ten directions may hear and believe in the great Dharma—this is the resounding.

May all aspirations be fulfilled,
as proclaimed in the scripture.
May this servant, through awakening to the scripture and cultivating the Dao,
fulfill all good aspirations,
just as the scripture describes the Jade Emperor’s wondrous practices through kalpas past.

From this, may one gradually advance in cultivation,
attain the great Dao,
and serve all immortals and sages.
With utmost sincerity, one takes refuge and bows in reverence.

If sincerity is not complete, it is not *utmost sincerity*;
if there is the slightest regret, it is not *taking refuge*.
In chanting this scripture, one maintains unwavering devotion and steadfast practice—
thus it is called *taking refuge with utmost sincerity and reverence*.

The sacred realm of Jade Purity,
where the Primordial One, peerless and supreme,
the Dharma King among heavens,
whose rank surpasses all immortals and buddhas,
dwells in a realm that is eternally indestructible—
this is the sacred realm of Jade Purity.

The Palace of the Clear and Subtle Heaven.

Within the Hall of Lush Radiance and Verdant Terrace,
the supreme height of luminous realms,
the Heaven above all heavens—
divine light fragrant and luxuriant,
serene in true purity.
Thus it is called the Hall of Lush Radiance and Verdant Terrace.

Above the vast expanse of pure, resounding echoes,
where the profound and mysterious depths cannot be fathomed—
the heavens array myriad forms in boundless profundity,
yet Jade Purity stands above all heavens.
Thus it is called above the vast expanse of pure, resounding echoes.

Manifesting the wondrous forms of conditioned existence,
the Primordial Heavenly Worthy, as the origin of the Three Teachings,
reveals transformations to instruct humanity—
their marvels beyond measure,
these are the myriad sublime forms of conditioned existence.
Possessing limitless divine power,
endowed with boundless, immeasurable spiritual penetration.
(One tradition holds that the Primordial One is the boundless great Dao, hence the saying—yet the former explanation is correct.)

Expounding and disseminating the true and mysterious,
shattering the obstructions of non-being, being, form, and emptiness—
broadly proclaiming and elucidating the most profound and wondrous teachings.
Breaking through the worldly barriers of non-being, being, form, and emptiness:
Non-being takes non-action as its essence;
being follows arising;
form clings to existence;
emptiness does not transcend the cycle of nihility.
The Primordial One, in expounding this scripture,
reveals the true and mysterious,
unconfined by the three contemplations,
unbound by the two extremes.
Through direct pointing in clear words,
the thusness is immediately realized—
thus shattering the stagnant obstructions of non-being, being, form, and emptiness,
guiding one to the wondrous refuge of the Dao.

Delivering and uplifting all sentient beings,
eradicating distinctions of wisdom and folly, high and low—
rescuing and elevating all beings of karmic destinies from the dust,
unrestricted by past or present, sage or fool,
all may cultivate the Dao.
This is the eradication of all distinctions between wisdom and folly, high and low—
the wondrous Dharma of true oneness, undivided.

Its sublime function is unfathomable,
its numinous mechanism beyond measure—
the peerless sagely efficacy knows no bounds,
difficult to perceive;
the mysterious, divine Dao-movement cannot be gauged.

With great compassion, great vows,
great sageliness, great mercy—
boundless deliverance of humanity—
the Primordial Heavenly Worthy.

Great compassion: deep empathy for the world;
great vows: limitless transformation;
great sageliness: the sagest among sages;
great mercy: inexhaustible salvation.
Boundless deliverance of humanity: without limit.
(Explanation of the Primordial One follows later.)

With utmost sincerity, one takes refuge and bows in reverence—
this refers to those who recite and contemplate the scripture,
offering their true hearts in reverence to the Most Venerable.
It is not merely the recitation of these words by the mouth.

The sacred realm of Supreme Purity,
the luminous height of mysterious purity,
the most true and wondrous realm.

The Palace of Yu-Yu Heaven.
From the First Azure to the Great White,
a wondrous realm of divine radiance and numinous transformation,
eternally indestructible, boundlessly vast,
its divine workings without end.
The scriptures speak of the Primordial White Palace of Yu-Yu Heaven.

Within the Purple Tenuity’s Jasper Terrace,
a realm of ineffable mystery, forever unshaken and imperishable—
thus called the Purple Tenuity.
(Not the Purple Tenuity Enclosure of the Northern Asterism.)

The radiance of the Jasper Terrace’s Supreme Purity Palace,
adorned with myriad treasures,
dwells within the Jasper Terrace.
Above the Jade Capital of the Mysterious Metropolis.

Supreme Purity lies above the White Jade Capital of the Great Mysterious Metropolis.
(Alternatively, it may be said to lie above the Jade Capital Mountain of the Highest Heaven—both interpretations are valid.)

It connects to the lineage of the Primordial Celestial August,
*Xi* (系): to continue, to inherit.
It is the thread of succession.
As the Numinous Treasure embodies the origin and enacts transformation,
it thus ascends to join the Dao-lineage of the Primordial Celestial August.

It surpasses the root and sprout of the Western Na Jade Realm.
(According to scriptural investigation, the Western Na Jade Realm lies in Shaanxi,
the birthplace of the White Emperor of the West.
The Numinous Treasure precedes the birth and transformation of all sages,
hence it is said to surpass the root and sprout of the Western Na Jade Realm.
*Yu-bai* [Primordial White] should not be conflated with the White Emperor.
Another interpretation reads *chao* [超, "surpass"] as *shao* [绍, "continue"],
suggesting the Heavenly Worthy as the root and sprout of the Western Na Jade Realm—this is incorrect.)

Entering the pearl within a grain of millet,
drawing forth the essence of the true and mysterious;
the Heavenly Worthy enters the Mysterious Pearl within a millet grain.
(This is akin to the Confucian "ninefold play of the Great Ultimate"
or the Buddhist "treasury of the true Dharma-eye."
*Yi* [挹]: to grasp this Dao as one would a rare treasure,
satiating the deepest flavors—thus the phrase.
It means to fully draw forth the essence and purity of the true and mysterious.)

Within the Fragrant Grove Park,
repeatedly expounding the subtle expedients of secret essentials.
The Heavenly Worthy, in the wondrous Fragrant Treasure Grove of Supreme Purity,
often discourses on the subtle expedients—the *quanti* and *titi*—of the mysterious and essential.
(The Dao itself is ineffable; scriptures serve as the path of practice.
Like the *quan* for catching fish or the *ti* for snaring rabbits,
they are not to be clung to—hence scriptures are called *quanti*.)

Its wondrous virtue defies thought,
its divine transformations elude comparison.

The Great Compassion, the Great Vows,
the Great Sage, the Great Mercy—
boundlessly delivering beings,
(as previously explained).
The Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy.

From the Azure of Beginnings to the Great White,
the Primordial Beginning once more reveals its wondrous transformations.
Dwelling in Supreme Purity,
its numinous workings boundless,
the great Dao’s dharma-treasures are transmitted without end.
Thus is he called the Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy.

With utmost sincerity, we take refuge and bow in reverence
to the Great Clarity’s immortal realm, the Palace of Great Crimson Heaven.
The Three Clarities’ celestial palaces are originally one,
yet through the vast radiance of the mysterious,
wondrous and inexhaustible,
it is called the Great Clarity’s immortal realm.
Primal White scatters its misty glow,
crimson auspices blanket all,
eternally indestructible—
hence the Palace of Great Crimson Heaven.
(This does not refer merely to the color red.)

Lofty, the golden towers rise,
vast, beyond the layered heavens.
The Most High’s abode stands unshaken,
supreme and boundless,
peerless, its golden light imperishable.
The mysterious towers reach so high,
so distant they defy measure,
forever dwelling above the ninefold heavens,
the ninefold layers, the ninefold skies.
(Another tradition holds it crowns the thirty-six heavens.)

Born through measureless kalpas,
the Most High has traversed kalpas of transformation,
boundless and unfathomable—
the great Dao’s mysterious teaching
is born through measureless kalpas.
Expounding the Dharma across twelve thousand heavens,
the Most High has, through the ages, transformed the triple-thousand great-thousand worlds.
Here it speaks of teaching in twelve thousand heavens—
the Most High’s Dharma courts extend through twelve thousand celestial realms.

Five thousand secret words
fuse the wondrous Dao of the Three Powers;
eighty-one transformations
uplift the beings of the Six Realms.
(Or: uplift the beings of the six senses—eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, mind—mired in the Six Desires.
Or: uplift the beings of the six realms—existence, non-existence, form, emptiness, potential, and object.
Or: from *zheng* [拯], meaning to rescue—awakening beings to the Dao and guiding them to perfection, the meaning remains the same.
The Six Realms are hard to escape;
the Most High extends compassionate teachings,
aiding gods, humans, ghosts, and creatures to transcend the dust—
hence it is also written as *zheng*.)

His sagely virtue is lofty,
his mysterious merit vast and profound.
The Most High’s sagely virtue,
exalted and majestic,
his mysterious merit broad and boundless,
deep and unfathomable—
thus it is called *xuangong* [玄功].

The Great Compassion, the Great Vows,
the Great Sage, the Great Mercy—
boundlessly delivering beings,
(as previously explained).
The Heavenly Worthy of Descended Birth.
The Most High’s manifestations are measureless,
his merciful blessings inexhaustible,
unceasing through all lives—
hence he is called the Heavenly Worthy of Descended Birth.

With utmost sincerity, we take refuge and bow in reverence
to the Realm of Wondrous Existence, the Upper Palace of Miro.
(The Upper Palace is the name of the Jade Emperor’s sagely father’s abode.
In the past, in former kalpas, he manifested as a king’s body.)

Long ago, he manifested as the body of the King of Miaole in the land of Guangyan—this was the very substance of the Root Emperor, the very essence of the Most Merciful Venerable Lord of the Myriad Heavenly Saints. In the primal phase, his appearance was profoundly still and serene: the sagely father, the origin of Dao and its transformations, his wondrous form abiding in tranquil purity, motionless and unchanging. Truly most profound and most wondrous, beyond all description—this primal stillness of his appearance is indeed most mysterious and remote, most divine and subtle, defying all discourse.

He succeeded to the throne and inherited the transmission, his virtue peerless and unmatched, one following upon the other. He inherited the kingship of Guangyan, continuing the royal lineage, his power and virtue unrivaled, without equal or parallel. Following in the footsteps of his predecessors, his virtue and fortune flourished ever more abundantly—thus it is said his virtue is peerless and unmatched, one following upon the other.

The sagely father’s compassionate father, the Most High’s supreme venerable one. The Jade Emperor is called the compassionate father of all beings, occupying the most exalted position. The sagely father refers to the Jade Emperor. The King of Guangyan gave birth to the Jade Emperor—speaking of the sagely father’s compassionate father, the supreme venerable one. His praises are inexhaustible, devotion to him knows no end. The Jade Emperor’s merits are eternally manifest, thus his praises are inexhaustible, and devotion to him knows no end.

The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Great Vows, the Father. The Great Sage, the Great Mercy—the Heavenly Worthy of the Sagely Father of the King of Miaole in the land of Guangyan. This sagely father refers to the King of Guangyan, for he gave birth to the Most Sagely.

With utmost sincerity, we take refuge and bow in reverence
to the Realm of Wondrous Existence, the Inner Palace of Miro.
(The Inner Palace is the most secluded abode of the Jade Emperor, where the sagely mother resides—hence it is called the Inner Palace.)

Her compassionate countenance shines with the warmth of spring’s sun,
the sagely mother’s kind and virtuous face radiant with luminous brightness, like the gentle harmony of the sun in spring.
Her noble demeanor is as stern as autumn’s frost,
her virtuous and reverent beauty, her bearing majestic and awe-inspiring, like the solemn severity of autumn’s frost.

Pure and complete in primordial qi, existing before heaven and earth;
her wondrous body, replete with the void and boundless qi of Brahman, predated the existence of heaven and earth.
Manifesting her wondrous form, she appeared through successive queens and consorts.
Her sag

Renouncing the exalted glory of a ruler of ten thousand chariots—
*(A state of ten thousand chariots signifies a great kingdom; the Jade Emperor abandoned the throne, forsaking the honor and splendor of a sovereign’s reign.)*
Enduring humiliation with benevolent gentleness, undaunted by the accumulation of eons in cultivation.
*(Bearing shame with great forbearance, embracing kindness and meekness, he feared not the arduous accumulation of virtue and deeds across countless kalpas. "Dread" denotes aversion to difficulty; ten myriad make an *eon*, explained below.)*
His merits peerless, his virtue too profound to surpass.
*(His deeds transcended all comparison, hence peerless; his boundless grace and virtue defied measure, hence too profound to surpass.)*
Great compassion, great vows, great sagehood, great mercy—manifesting a body of boundless merit:
**The Most High Jade Sovereign of Heaven.**

With utmost sincerity, we prostrate in reverence:
Enthroned in imperial majesty, dwelling high in the celestial palace.
*(Enthroned as the Jade Emperor, he resides in the Great Heavenly Palace of Pure Subtlety.)*
Roaming through all the White Jade Capitals,
*(Traversing all the White Jade Capitals of the worlds’ great heavenly palaces.)*
Universally manifest within the ten directions’ Golden Towers.
*(Omnipresent within the Golden Towers of all ten directions’ great heavenly palaces.)*
Steadfast yet responsive, coming and going with unconstrained freedom;
*(Abiding in great stillness yet perfectly responsive; moving or resting with natural ease, attaining boundless liberation, never confined.)*
Expanding and contracting, gathering and dispersing—ever thus from beginning to end.
*(Whether extending or withdrawing, uniting or parting, his transformations remain unfathomably fluid.)*
Unified yet divisible, his transformations harmoniously fluid and inscrutable.
*(Whole yet capable of infinite division, his divine metamorphoses flow with perfect spontaneity, beyond all measure or prediction—like the Buddha’s "effortless grasp of the Dao" or the Confucian ideal of "meeting opportunity at every turn.")*
Expounding the Dao of purity and liberation,
*(Revealing the truth of perfect clarity and emancipation.)*
Delivering those sunk in delusion, sorrow, and suffering.
*(Rescuing beings lost in ignorance, grief, and karmic affliction.)*
Naturally so, beyond the grasp of mortal understanding.
*(His wondrous transformations arise spontaneously, defying all worldly cognition. The character *识* here denotes perception, not aspiration or interpretation.)*

Great compassion, great vows, great sagehood, great mercy—manifesting a body of purity and spontaneity:
**The Most High Jade Sovereign of Heaven.**
*(This title extols the immaculate virtue of the Jade Emperor.)*

With utmost sincerity, we prostrate in reverence:
Once a royal heir, his mysterious merits now resound through the ages.
*(In a former kalpa, he was the heir of Guangyan; his boundless, profound transformations remain ever evident.)*
Three thousand kalpas of cultivation passed as a single day;
*(Three thousand two hundred kalpas of spiritual practice unfolded like a single day.)*
The salvation of countless beings extended across the ten directions.
*(His deliverance of myriad souls reached every realm of the ten directions.)*
Though his dharmakāya arose from the womb’s sacred vessel,
*(The Jade Emperor’s manifested form, born of the Sagely Mother, emerged from the embryo of the dharmakāya—yet his sacred body was no mere mortal vessel.)*
His true essence sprang from the primal transformations of the Dao.
*(The character *腪* (yùn) signifies the process of formative metamorphosis; his sacred body truly arose from the primordial transformations of the Dao’s origin.)*
Indestructible and imperishable, vanishing yet ever-present.
*(Never destroyed, never extinguished; seemingly absent, yet wondrously real; seemingly present, yet utterly transcendent.)*

Great compassion, great vows, great sagehood, great mercy—manifesting a body of divine luminosity, indestructible and unshakable, the supreme dharmakāya of true emptiness:
**The Most High Jade Sovereign of Heaven.**
*(This title praises the Jade Emperor’s sacred fruition, eternally real and immutable.)*

**Prostration and Repentance:**
*(Prostration: kneeling in profound reverence, body pressed to the ground in utmost devotion. Some mistakenly define it as prolonged kneeling, but this is incorrect.)*
*(Repentance: confessing one’s transgressions, vowing to eradicate them forever; remorse: lamenting past wrongs, resolving to reform—akin to a sinner’s self-surrender.)*

We, your humble servants—
*(We, the reciters of this scripture, together with all virtuous beings, speak as one.)*
From time immemorial,
*(Since the beginningless kalpas—kalpas without origin, their inception beyond all reckoning.)*
Have allowed ignorance and afflictions to obscure our true hearts.
*(Our nature is inherently luminous, yet stirred by external phenomena, we veil our inner radiance, giving rise to delusion. Ignorance clouds the mind, breeding turmoil and vexation, drowning our innate goodness—like a covering that obscures what lies beneath. Yet the true heart remains, ever-present; only through ignorance and affliction does it seem lost, as if shrouded in darkness.)*
Now, we reveal our original truth.
*(Having cast off these veils, our true nature is laid bare.)*

We have persistently engaged in killing, theft, and licentiousness—
*(Not merely committing these acts, but harboring the intent to kill, steal, or lust, unable to extinguish such thoughts—this is the persistence in evil. These constitute the three bodily karmic transgressions.)*
Slander, deceit, and seductive speech—
*(Spreading discord with duplicitous words; fabricating falsehoods without basis; weaving deceptive rhetoric to mislead—these are the four verbal karmic transgressions.)*
Defaming the true teachings of the Great Vehicle,
*(Ignorant of the Dao, they spew slanderous lies against the authentic Mahāyāna teachings of Confucianism, Daoism, and Buddhism.)*
Sowing strife among kin and friends, severing bonds of harmony.
*(Not through physical violence, but by stirring conflict with reckless words, rupturing the affection between loved ones, and fracturing the peace among others.)*

Greed, wrath, and delusion—letting these three poisons run rampant,
*(Insatiable desire, unending resentment, and stubborn ignorance—allowing these three poisons to dominate the mind. Some misinterpret *暗* as a single affliction, or *三心* as the three temporal states of past, present, and future, but these are incorrect.)*

Excessive joy, anger, attachment, and aversion amplify the seven forms of arrogance.
*(Liu Langran states: Fulfillment breeds joy, provocation stirs anger, affinity fosters attachment, and opposition sparks aversion—these, combined with the three poisons above, swell into seven kinds of arrogance.)*

First, chasing fleeting vanities while neglecting the Great Dao—this is reckless arrogance.
Second, indulging wicked thoughts and scorning karmic retribution—this is defiant arrogance.
Third, drowning in illusions and refusing to return to the true Dharma—this is profane arrogance.
Fourth, reveling in worldly passions and shunning the virtuous—this is haughty arrogance.
Fifth, harboring resentment and envy while defying sacred laws—this is negligent arrogance.
Sixth, surrendering to desire and neglecting the body’s well-being—this is slothful arrogance.
Seventh, persisting in aversion, failing to ascend to goodness, and disrespecting the divine—this is contemptuous arrogance.
*(Some equate the seven emotions—joy, anger, sorrow, fear, love, aversion, and desire—with the seven forms of arrogance, but these arise from the amplification of the three poisons and cannot be classified as such. This interpretation is incorrect; Liu Langran’s explanation is sound. Let the reader discern carefully.)*

The roots of sins accumulated across kalpas defy recollection—
*(The karmic roots of evil deeds committed through countless kalpas resist remembrance or reckoning.)*
The stains of misdeeds across lifetimes are immeasurable.
*(The defilements of transgressions across myriad existences are beyond measure, their weight unknown.)*

Take refuge in the boundless compassion of the Most High Sages—
*(Sincerely and perpetually turn toward the supreme, relying on the power of their great compassion to silently aid in the eternal dissolution of transgressions. *(Note: "Compassion" should not be rigidly interpreted as "venerable.")*)*
Bare the true heart and prostrate in repentance.
*(Expose the genuine heart and humbly offer repentance for past sins.)*

May all the karmic stains of ten thousand kalpas and a thousand lives—
*(The accumulated defilements of countless kalpas and existences, briefly enumerated here—)*
Be wholly purged through this act of repentance.
*(May all past transgressions vanish after this repentance, never to be repeated.)*

Offer this body and mind to the Perfected Ones above—
*(Surrender this present body and mind in eternal devotion to the Most High Perfected Sages.)*
And pray that all sinful roots be pardoned.
*(May all past sins be absolved by the grace of the Perfected, who forgive without inquiry.)*

With utmost sincerity, make this vow:
May my eyes forever behold the radiance of the Jade Mark,
*(May my eyes always witness the luminous, wondrous form of the Perfected, as if they were present.)*
May my ears forever hear the sound of the Dharma,
*(May my ears always perceive the sublime voice of the Perfected teaching, attuned to truth.)*
May my nose forever inhale the fragrance of myriad wonders,
*(May my nose forever breathe the sacred, wondrous scents of the Perfected’s Dharma-body, suffused with celestial essence.)*
May my tongue forever praise the Supreme Dao,
*(May my tongue forever extol the peerless Dao, uttering no words but those of the Perfected’s Dharma.)*
May my body never be tainted by impurity,
*(May my body remain pure across all lives, unstained by defilement, enacting only the deeds of the Perfected’s Dharma.)*
May my mind forever abide in right faith.
*(May my heart and thoughts forever dwell in perfect sincerity, free from deceit or wayward desires.)*

Vow to repay the Four Profound Debts above—
*(The debts to heaven and earth for their shelter, to sun and moon for their light, to sovereign and land for their sustenance, and to parents for giving life.)*
Vow to relieve the Three Paths of suffering below—
*(The sufferings of the celestial path bound by form, the terrestrial path bound by attachment, and the aquatic path bound by greed—afflictions of mind, spirit, and body.)*

Extend boundless compassion to all beings,
*(May I widely manifest the compassion innate to my nature, embracing all with mercy. *(Alternatively: "May the Emperor’s compassion be universally extended.")*)*
And practice skillful means to liberate all sentient life.
*(May I perform such meritorious deeds, employing great skillful means to transform and deliver all beings in the world.)*

Imploring the great compassion of the Jade Emperor,
*(As previously explained.)*
May all vows be protected and fulfilled.
*(May the Jade Emperor’s grace ensure the realization of all my aspirations.)*

The vow now complete,
Take refuge in the Three Treasures:
*(The Dao, the Scriptures, and the Masters.)*

**Mysterious Essence Mantra**
*(The profoundly hidden, secret essence of the Great Brahmā Immortal’s Mantra.)*

O Boundless Primordial Beginning,
*(Boundless—vast beyond measure. Primordial Beginning: explained later.)*
Deliverer of Countless Beings,
