*(As previously explained.)*
Expounding the Teachings of Purity,
*(Explained later.)*
Guiding the Celestial Perfected to ascend.
*(Guiding the Celestial Perfected upward. *(Alternatively: "Ascending the throne to guide," but this is overly restrictive.)*)*

From the Mystic Throne, the Dharma is proclaimed—
*(The Dao-body abides eternally, its light pervading the ten directions; the throne transcends the mundane, suspended in the void. The turning of the Dharma-wheel in empty space is the Mystic Throne’s discourse.)*
Silent and soundless.
*(Profound and formless, silent and soundless.)*

The Jade Emperor radiates light,
*(As explained later.)*

Joy and celebration defy expression.
*(Joy and celebration beyond the reach of words.)*

This is the transmission of the heart-mind,
This true scripture is the essential canon of the Teaching Master, the Most Sagely One, transmitted through the heart-mind.
It is also called the Celestial Root.
*(This scripture is the mysterious root of the Celestial Dao, not the "return of thunder" in earthly hexagrams.)*

The Great Perfection Mantra,
*(Explained later.)*
The Jade Chapters of the Cavernous Writ,
*(The Azure Jade Celestial Chapters, the Numinous Writ of the Great Cavern.)*

Compiled into a book,
*(Assembling the esoteric words of the Primordial Beginning and the luminous petitions of the Perfected, to form the scripture of the Jade Emperor.)*

Disseminating among the divine Perfected.
*(Spreading and bestowing universally among the divine Perfected, to propagate the sagely teachings—this is the meaning of "disseminating the canonical writ.")*

Now I face east and recite,
*(Sitting facing east to recite this scripture.)*

May I stand equal with Heaven,
*(May I, through eternal true recitation of this scripture, stand equal with Heaven.)*

Both in life and death attaining fruition,
*(Both in life and death, all attain the fruit of the Dao.)*

Forever crossing the ford of the River of Love.
*(Forever transcending the River of Love. The bonds of love among sentient beings are the hardest to sever—this is the ford of true suffering. Reciting this scripture enables all to forever cross the River of Love.)*

Visualizing the august countenance,
*(Visualizing the august countenance of the Jade Emperor.)*

Proclaiming the precious title,
*(Proclaiming the precious title of the Jade Emperor.)*

With utmost sincerity, I bow in reverence to the Most High,
*(As previously noted, with utmost sincerity, I bow in reverence to the Most High.)*

The Heaven of Infinite Vastness,
*(The boundless expanse of the Great Void, the supreme and infinite Heaven of Miro.)*

The wondrous realm of mysterious truth,
*(The celestial palace of the Jade Emperor, where numinous radiance and auspicious light abide—no illusory or transient phenomena.)*

Eternally indestructible, subtly unfathomable,
*(The wondrous realm of mysterious truth, eternally unchanging, its subtleties beyond measure.)*

The distant Purple-Golden Towers,
*(The distant Purple-Golden Towers, where auspicious light and mysterious signs manifest.)*

The Supreme Tenuity of Jade Purity.
*(The Supreme Tenuity—no mere celestial realm of sun and moon, but the Palace of Jade Purity in the Great Subtlety, the abode of the Jade Emperor. Here, mysterious purple qi and golden light extend forty billion myriad leagues, towering and immutable, forever untainted by dust, beyond the reach of all heavens—thus is it called the Palace of Supreme Tenuity and Jade Purity.)*

The Sagely One of the Infinite and Most High,
*(The Dao transcends all bounds, the position is most exalted, the virtue and power of the Great Sage are supreme.)*

Vast and luminous, radiating brilliance,
*(Boundless and expansive, the azure depths of the double mystery emit boundless, measureless light.)*

Silent and vast, without origin,
*(Though suffused with great light, its depths are inscrutable, soundless and still—profound beyond comprehension, vast beyond all source.)*

The mysterious model encompassing the ten directions,
*(The body of the Dao, the dharmakāya, majestic and boundless, is the origin of all spirits, the lord of myriad heavens, the ancestral sage of kalpas—this mysterious model governs the ten directions.)*

The profound and tranquil true and constant Way,
*(Serene and still, ever pure and ever stable, the great Way of true constancy, unchanging.)*

The expansive and boundless great spiritual power,
*(Vast beyond measure, formless and traceless, the greatest spiritual power.)*

The Jade Emperor, Great Heavenly Venerable, Supreme Sovereign of the Mysterious Vault.
*(The Jade Emperor is not merely the lord of one heaven but the sovereign of all heavens, the origin of the Three Teachings, the Most High and Infinite Great Heavenly Venerable, the Supreme Sovereign of the Mysterious Vault and Lofty Firmament.)*

Upon reciting these ten sacred lines, one should bow once for each.
*(If unable to bow for each line, first bow once while reciting all ten, then perform nine additional bows while reciting only "The Jade Emperor, Great Heavenly Venerable, Supreme Sovereign of the Mysterious Vault" is also permissible.)*

After completing the rites, sit upright and recite the scripture.

The Great Marshal Ma Lingguan states: *This scripture is the king among all methods. For gods, humans, ghosts, and beings, none fail to benefit. Whether man or woman, regardless of poverty or wealth, nobility or humility, or even illiteracy—whoever reveres this scripture and hears its words shall transform from woman to man and attain blessings and longevity. Printing and distributing it, or exhorting others to recite it, yields boundless merit. Yet one must be utterly sincere, without doubt or negligence. Wherever this scripture resides, all spirits protect it. Those who heed my words shall forever enjoy divine favor. Strive on, and do not squander this auspicious opportunity.*

*End of Volume One of the Imperial Scripture Collected Commentaries*
*Beginning of Volume Two of the Imperial Scripture Annotations*

**Catalogue of the *Collected Commentaries on the Imperial Scripture***

**The Scripture Itself** – Three scrolls, totaling 12,036 characters.
- **Upper Scroll**
- **Middle Scroll**
- **Lower Scroll**

**Five Chapters:**
1. *The Divine Transformations of the Celestial Palace of Qingwei* – First Chapter (Upper Scroll)
2. *The Great Luminous Perfect and Complete Divine Mantra of the Most High* – Second Chapter
3. *The Virtues and Powers of the Jade Emperor* – Third Chapter (Both in Middle Scroll)
4. *The Protection of Heavenly Perfected Ones* – Fourth Chapter
5. *Divine Responses and Verified Miracles* – Fifth Chapter (Both in Lower Scroll)

**Collected Commentaries on the Scripture** – Ten scrolls, over one hundred thousand words.
- **First Scroll:** Prefaces by Various Perfected Ones; Foreword; appended *Investigation of Meaning* and *Prefatory Insights*
- **Second, Third, and Fourth Scrolls:** Commentaries on the Upper Scroll
- **Fifth, Sixth, and Seventh Scrolls:** Commentaries on the Middle Scroll
- **Eighth, Ninth, and Tenth Scrolls:** Commentaries on the Lower Scroll

**Upper Scroll of the *Highest Scripture of the Jade Emperor’s Fundamental Conduct***

**First Chapter: The Divine Transformations of the Celestial Palace of Qingwei**

The Ancestral Celestial Master states: *The Celestial Palace of Qingwei transcends the Three Realms. All dust and defilement are purified; its emptiness is luminous and wondrous, its subtlety unfathomable. Dwelling within the Three Clarities, it is the great celestial palace where the Jade Emperor resides. When the Primordial Beginning expounded the scriptures, he presided over this wondrous realm. His sagely and marvelous efficacy operates and transforms without limit, beyond all measure or comprehension. The scripture expounds this meaning as the supreme chapter—only those with divine wisdom and wondrous insight can fully comprehend it. Thus, it is called the First Chapter of Divine Transformations.*

This humble commentator, reflecting on ancient exegesis, observes: *That which transforms wondrously beyond measure is called "divine"; that which pervades universally without omission is called "transformations." It crowns the five chapters and serves as the origin of the three scrolls. Those who grasp this at the Vermilion Terrace will understand the entire scripture.*

**Chapter One: The Divine Transformations**

**At that time, the Heavenly Venerable of Primordial Beginning—**

*"At that time"* refers to the initial differentiation of the Boundless, the inception of the Great Mystery’s flourishing transformation, the wondrous juncture of the myriad sages’ karmic affinity—when this scripture was about to be expounded.

*"Primordial"* means great and primary.
*"Beginning"* means origin.
The flourishing transformation of the myriad sages originates with the Primordial Beginning.
Thus, he is called the *Heavenly Venerable of Primordial Beginning.*

**In the Celestial Palace of Qingwei—**

*For an explanation of the Celestial Palace of Qingwei, see above.*

**Within the Jade Capital and Golden Gates—**

The Perfected One of Purple Clarity and White Purity states: *The Jade Emperor’s abode is the Jade Capital, its gates forged of gold—not the gold and jade of the mortal world, but wondrous transformations of divine power, where azure heavens and luminous jasper adorn the majestic palace-city. Hence it is called the Jade Capital and Golden Gates.*

**The Mystic Garden of Seven Treasures—**

The White Perfected One states: *The Seven Treasures are: azure jade, jasper terraces, lapis lazuli halls, dragon-veined walls, white jade ramparts, cinnabar gates, and golden radiance suffusing all—thus named the Seven Treasures.* Another account lists them as: glass, crystal, pearls, agate, coral, amber, and giant clam. *The Mystic Garden* refers to the profound and recondite paradise.

**The Jade Emperor’s palaces, ascending the Throne of Luminous Brilliance—**

Master Zhang Zifang states: *When the Primordial Beginning descended to the Jade Emperor’s hall, he ascended the sacred Throne of Great Luminous Brilliance.*

**With an immeasurable host, he expounded the Dharma-gate of the Numinous Treasure, the Pure and Undivided True One.**

Zifang states: *As the Primordial Beginning ascended the throne, boundless perfected sages gathered. Thus it is said: with an immeasurable host, he proclaimed the wondrous, numinous, and precious Dharma—pure, unstained, and utterly true—the secret and marvelous essence of the Undivided True One, seamless and unadulterated, the Dharma-gate of Non-Duality.*

The *Collected Explanations of the Ten Directions* states: *The primordial spirit of humanity is the origin of nature and life. This is inherent to the Great Heavenly Venerable within the realm of Qingwei Heaven. The Jade Capital and Golden Gates, adorned with the Seven Treasures, are fundamentally possessed by all. The seven treasures of the human body—nature, life, yin, yang, spirit, qi, and essence—correspond to the luminous courts and mystic gardens, uniting heaven and humanity as one. When the Celestial Monarch is at peace, the Throne of the Jade Emperor’s radiance may be ascended. As the hundred constituents obey the command, concentrating the spirit and aligning with the Dao, one attains the Heavenly Venerable’s throne, joining the immeasurable perfected beings in proclaiming the Dharma-gate of the Numinous Treasure, the Pure and Undivided True One. Yet the Dao leaves no trace; only through luminous realization does one enter its secret and wondrous realm—as if upon a great road, with a path of entry. Hence it is called the Dharma-gate.*

**Chapter Two of the Divine Transformations**

**At that time—**

*This refers to the moment when the Primordial Beginning ascended the throne.*

**The Venerable Jade Emperor—**

*Venerable Emperor* denotes his incomparable majesty.

**With the various Celestial Perfected Ones, Flying Celestial Great Sages, Boundless Divine Kings, and jade maidens and numinous youths numbering ninety million, all observing a pure fast and bearing ritual regalia, stood in attendance beside him.**

Zifang states: *With* means together; *various* means many. *The Jade Emperor, together with the host of celestial immortals and perfected beings, wondrously assisted in transformation, ascending and delivering through divine power—the Great Sages of the Flying Celestials, the Divine Kings of the three thousand great realms and the boundless heavens beyond, the numinous youths of the Lesser Yang’s mystic qi who respond and attend, and the jade maidens of the Lesser Yin’s mystic qi who proclaim and transmit—altogether ninety million divine beings. Concealing their divine radiance and returning to the primordial origin, they observed a pure fast, held the jeweled regalia, and stood in attendance beside the Primordial Beginning’s Throne of Luminous Brilliance.*

Marshal Tian You, Vice-Commander of the Primordial, states: *The human body possesses a true sovereign, the primordial spirit, whose numinous power is unrestrained. It also harbors Flying Celestial Great Sages, whose spirit and qi guard and support the entire body. In every interstice, there are Boundless Divine Kings, the mystic radiance of the Lesser Yang, and the numinous workings of the Lesser Yin—likewise possessing numinous youths and jade maidens. When the heart aligns with the Dao, the great tally of Yang’s vigor also becomes ninety million, as the body’s spirits pay homage to the origin. A pure fast means an unwavering heart; bearing regalia means the body is free from indolence.*

A humble observation states: *Humanity and heaven-and-earth are of one kind; one should remain clear and unadulterated. When the primordial spirit governs the supreme pole, it is like Master Yan’s heart-fast or a ritualist’s bearing of the banner—singing reverence without duality. Then one follows the command of the Celestial Monarch and attains the Dao.*

**Chapter Three of the Divine Transformations**

**Thereupon—**

At this very convergence, the Jade Emperor, knowing the appointed time was nigh, exercised the power of the Six Penetrations before the assembly, releasing a radiance of great luminosity that suffused all heavens and boundless Brahma-kṣetra. Every realm trembled and quaked; the ten directions and all worlds without limit became as lapis lazuli and crystal, utterly transparent, without obstruction or hindrance.

The Divine Consort proclaimed: The Jade Emperor, discerning the moment when the mysterious light would unfold and the civil brilliance would commence—the time for expounding the Dharma and transmitting the scriptures—manifested the might of the Six Penetrations before the grand convocation. He emitted a light of supreme illumination, pervading the measureless heavens and the infinite celestial palaces of the divine emperors and perfected beings, all realms of the spirit’s dominion. Every domain shuddered and stirred. The worlds of all immortals and buddhas in the ten directions, without limit, became as precious lapis lazuli and crystal, their brilliance pure and resplendent, revealing all without concealment, leaving no place unseen or obstructed.

Master Zhang Ziyang said: The Six Penetrations are the penetration of sight, the penetration of hearing, the penetration of spirit-touch, the penetration of spirit-meeting, the penetration of past lives, and the penetration of foreknowledge—these correspond to the six penetrations of the Buddhist tradition, such as the divine eye. *Brahma-kṣetra* refers to the celestial abodes of the divine emperors, wondrous and resplendent in the heavens, untouched by the dust of the world, never decaying, towering and unshakable, invisible to mortal eyes—hence called *Brahma-kṣetra*. "All realms" denotes the domains where each spirit dwells. The boundaries of these realms encompass all worlds, not merely the human realm but also the celestial realms. Though lapis lazuli possesses form and light, it reveals all things within; the precious crystal, without flaw or leakage, leaves nothing unseen. The Jade Emperor’s radiance pierces all realms, illuminating even the hidden and obscure—how could there be any obstruction? The comparison is made lest one fail to grasp the meaning.

A humble observation states: The luminosity of human nature is inherently unobstructed, but when the primordial spirit loses its mastery, barriers arise. One may hear but not see, or see but not hear; know but not speak, or speak but not know; obscure self and others, or confuse past and future—thus failing to attain the Six Penetrations. If one thoroughly comprehends nature and destiny, with the primordial spirit ever in command, then the light pervades heaven and humanity, penetrating within and without. The Purple Palace and the Cinnabar Terrace, the Yellow Court and the Mystic Realm—the original abodes of the body’s spirits, inherently celestial—all shine with radiance, unobstructed and fully illumined. Is this not like lapis lazuli and crystal, revealing all without concealment?

Yet while the Dao is inherently luminous, attaining clarity is no easy matter. One must not feign ignorance nor be misled by false knowledge. To grasp the truth neither too soon nor too late is a profound awakening. If one can emulate the Jade Emperor, perceiving the appointed time and manifesting light, ever renewing and abiding in constancy, then the great luminosity shall never dim, and the Dao shall forever shine forth.

**Chapter Four of the Divine Transformations**

The sacred hosts of the ten directions all rode upon five-colored jade wheels, jade-like chariots, azure-green carriages drawn by nine-colored dark dragons, and ten peerless feathered canopies.

The Thunder Patriarch said: The ten directions are the four cardinal points, the four intermediate directions, and above and below. The sacred hosts are the divine and perfected beings of the ten directions. Beholding the light emitted by the Jade Emperor, they all rode upon wheels of five-hued patterned jade, resplendent chariots of jade-like splendor, azure-green treasure carriages, nine-colored dark dragons of radiant glory, and feathered canopies of unmatched excellence.

Bai Yuchan said: The five colors are blue, yellow, red, white, and black. The *wheel* refers to the two wheels of a chariot; the *chariot* is the vehicle itself. The *carriage* is the general term for the imperial conveyance. The nine colors are blue, red, yellow, white, black, purple, azure-green, profound dark, and golden luminosity. The *dark dragon* possesses the semblance of dragon-light but no visible form. The *ten peerless* are those without equal in the ten directions, canopies of phoenix and luan feathers, wondrous and divine. The Daoist scriptures state: The *feathered canopy* is a high-handled feathered fan. Another account says that when the divine emperors and perfected beings travel, auspicious feathered regalia serve as their canopy—this latter explanation is even more sublime.

A humble observation states: Humans, endowed with the primordial numen of the Five Agents—Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth—each possess dharma treasures. When immortals and perfected beings attain the Dao, these treasures accompany their divine conveyances. If one can silently pay homage to the Supreme Emperor, emulating heaven, the spirits within the body gather, and the upright qi manifests its splendor. The jade wheel, the jade-like chariot, the azure-green treasure carriage, the nine-colored dark dragons of spiritual transformation, and the ten peerless feathered canopies—all once resided within the body. How could these be exclusive to the divine beings of heaven and earth? Alas, only those who have truly attained the Dao understand this.

**Chapter Five of the Divine Transformations**

Unicorns danced and phoenixes sang, solemn hymns resounded; divine consorts scattered flowers, golden youths wafted incense, chanting the profound verses of the Cavernous Chapters as they floated through the air.

Master Xu Jingtian said: As the sacred hosts journeyed, unicorns led the dance and singing phoenixes harmonized, their melodies refined and resonant, their songs clear and bright. Celestial consorts scattered blossoms of jade; attendant golden youths diffused auspicious incense, praising and chanting the sacred verses of the Cavernous Chapters, escorting the divine procession as it soared through the void toward the imperial capital.

A voice from the ten directions proclaimed: When the divine emperor travels, divine youths and jade maidens follow in song, unicorns dance and phoenixes sing, with attendant maidens performing the dance of the unicorn and the song of the phoenix. Hence the saying: "Their songs resound clearly." This interpretation is overly contrived. The unicorns and phoenixes accompanying the divine procession are akin to the imperial mounts of today. Moreover, the Daoist scriptures state: When the Celestial Emperor travels, dragons soar and phoenixes dance—such is the harmony of the celestial realm. It is also said that when dragons and leopards roar in the mountains and forests, their calls resound clearly. These are undoubtedly true unicorns and phoenixes. Otherwise, when Emperor Shun performed music on Mount Qi, why did the phoenixes appear in formation and the hundred beasts dance? Reflecting on the scriptures, one should adhere to the former explanation.

Those of limited insight say: When one cultivates the Dao, silently aligning with the celestial principles, revering the Primordial Sovereign, and embodying supreme harmony within, the celestial pipes resound in song, the subtle meridians settle into tranquility—elegant as the dance of the unicorn, the cry of the simurgh and phoenix, their harmonious calls a joy to hear. The radiance of yang essence shines forth, the splendor of yin blossoms manifests, and one seems to glimpse divine maidens scattering flowers and golden youths wafting incense. The esoteric music and mysterious tones become the celestial hymns of praise sung by immortals, resonating with the primordial spirit. As if riding the wind through empty space, this is akin to the sacred assembly floating through the heavens to the imperial abode. Such potential lies within all, yet only those of resolve may witness its truth.

*Chapter Six of the Divine Powers*

At that moment, Brahmā Heaven’s assembly of golden immortals, the great bodhisattvas of the Mahāyāna, and the fourfold hosts of the eight divisions—all bathed in this radiant illumination—rode upon golden and azure cloud-borne jade chariots. Clad in ninefold radiant garments, they streamed forth wondrous visions, celebrating the auspicious celestial assembly. The Three Luminaries emitted their fragrance, rare perfumes wafted from the eight directions, and the sacred throng circled and wove before the Dao. A rain of marvelous blossoms descended like clouds, blanketing the gathering.

Zifang remarks: At this time, all the Brahmās of the heavens, every awakened golden immortal, the great beings who have realized the Mahāyāna’s true path, the fourfold hosts of celestial spirits, demons, and ghosts, and the eight divisions of devas and dragons—all, illumined by this light, rode upon chariots of jade and gold, borne by flying clouds of golden and azure hues. Adorned in ninefold radiant raiment, they scattered wondrous visions to celebrate the propitious celestial occasion. The fourfold assembly gathered, and the Three Luminaries—sun, moon, and stars—emitted their fragrant splendor. Exotic perfumes drifted from the eight directions, and the sacred multitude presented these esoteric marvels, circling and weaving before the Great Dao. A rain of celestial flowers descended like clouds, covering the grand assembly.

Magū explains: Brahmā Heaven is the most exalted jeweled forest and jade palace, unseen by the mortal world and hidden in ineffable mystery—hence its name. The golden immortals are those whose bodies are indestructible as vajra. The great bodhisattvas include holy beings such as Avalokiteśvara. The fourfold hosts comprise immortals, generals, male and female spirits—or, alternatively, celestial spirits, demons, and ghosts, all of which are valid. To speak of monastics and laity would be incorrect, for such beings rarely ascend to the celestial realms. The eight divisions are the spirit hosts, the general hosts, the deva and celestial soldier hosts, the vajra hosts, the dragon king hosts, the night-luminous handmaid hosts, the asura hosts, and the yakṣa hosts. The nine radiant garments are azure, multicolored, purple, cinnabar, cloud, mist, auspicious light, luminous, and universal treasure radiance. The ninefold mysterious light streams forth these wondrous visions, for they are the radiance of raiment—or rather, the marvelous adornments that follow the form of the spirit, not merely the garments themselves. The *Qingxiao* refers to an auspicious day, or the celebration of an audience with the Divine Empyrean. The four assemblies are the gathering of celestial goodness, the auspicious gathering of spirits, the gathering of timely conjunctions, and the gathering of karmic convergence—not merely the assembly of the fourfold hosts. The circling before the Dao refers to the fragrant wafting from the eight directions, or the sacred multitude’s encircling. The descent like clouds, covering the assembly, describes the marvelous blossoms falling as clouds to blanket the gathering—not merely the sacred throng descending like clouds, which would be overly contrived.

Those of limited insight say: The human body contains myriad spirits, yet if the primordial spirit does not preside, the host of spirits will not manifest their numinosity. Only the true cultivator, silently paying homage to the true sovereign, may summon the myriad spirits to reverent audience. The mysterious light of the spirit palace and the hundred marvels all converge and appear. When the primordial spirit presides over the assembly, auspicious signs array themselves like propitious clouds covering all—then I and the celestial realm are no longer two.

*Chapter Seven of the Divine Powers*

At that time, the Emperor’s light suffused all heavens, illuminating downward to the ten directions and boundless worlds, making them equal to the realm of the Mysterious Capital. All mortal realms, reaching upward to the Nine Heavens, were connected and intertwined, intimately near. The boundless worlds below—mountains and ridges, slopes and hills, ravines and valleys—all lay as level as the palm of a hand. The six directions were brought near, and the Three Realms were no longer distant. The jeweled terraces and palaces of heaven were scattered like stars among mortals. Rare jades and precious stones were arrayed in brilliance, illuminating the cloud-borne thoroughfares. Seven-jeweled balustrades demarcated the roads. Jade trees and immortal blossoms, resplendent with pearls and treasures, adorned the radiant Cinnabar Field. Lingzhi and sacred grasses spread in lush profusion.

The Perfected of the Celestial Realms remarks: At that time, the Jade Emperor’s light, from the thirty-six heavens of this world to the heavens of the three thousand great realms, shone downward to illumine all the boundless worlds of the ten directions, making them as luminous as the realm of the Mysterious Capital where the Jade Emperor dwells. All the worlds of the Dharma realms, bathed in this light, were without obstruction, reaching upward to the Nine Heavens of wondrous yang transformation. Heaven and earth, the mortal and celestial realms, were connected in luminous union, intertwined in utmost intimacy. All the boundless worlds below—lofty mountains and ridges, rugged slopes and hills, lowly ravines and valleys—lay as level and smooth as the palm of a hand. The six directions of above and below, the four quarters, were brought into closest proximity, and the Three Pure Realms were no longer distant. The jeweled terraces and palaces of heaven were scattered like stars among the mortal realm. Rare jades and precious stones were arrayed in brilliance, illuminating the cloud-borne thoroughfares. Balustrades of seven treasures marked the roads. Jade trees and immortal blossoms, resplendent with pearls and treasures, adorned the radiant Cinnabar Field. Sacred lingzhi and immortal grasses spread in lush profusion.

Shixinglin’s *Examination of Meanings* states: The dwelling of mortal kings is called the imperial capital; the Jade Emperor’s abode surpasses all heavens, unseen by the world—hence it is called the Mysterious Capital. Ordinarily, heaven is pure and earth is turbid; spirits are numinous and mortals are dull. Without connection, they are not intimately near. Yet when the Emperor’s light shines through, the numinous mechanism wondrously links them, so above and below are united, and spirits and mortals draw near. The Nine Heavens refer to the nine upper realms of the thirty-six heavens, not merely nine in number.

Mountains refer to those of great height and grandeur. A *ling* is a large mound or hill. A *po* is uneven terrain. A *ban* is the ruggedness of mountain ridges. Deep and long channels are called *gou*. Where mountains flank water is called a *jian*. Where water flows and gathers is called a *xi*. The great hollows of mountains are called *gu*. *Mian* signifies vast and level expanses. Though land naturally possesses mountains, waters, valleys, and ravines—thus being inherently uneven—when the Emperor’s light suffuses and illumines it, wondrous intent overflows, and all the lands of every world become level.

*Qiong* denotes fine stone; *gui*, jade-like gems. *Fenran bingchen* describes their profuse and splendid array. *Yunqu* are the celestial roads at heaven’s summit. Horizontal barriers are called *lan*, vertical ones *shun*—what the world terms railings. *Qian* signifies the radiant brilliance of blossoms. *Zhubao* are the true treasures of pearls and gems. *Dantian* refers to the cinnabar field of the Mysterious Capital’s cinnabar steps.

As the *Guanshi* observes: The human body contains heaven and earth. When the primal mysteries of yin and yang fail to unite, above and below become distant and estranged. Yet when the original spirit commands the light and celestial radiance blazes forth, earth and heaven harmonize in supreme balance, above and below merge, and all unevenness and curvature become intimately and wondrously conjoined. The treasures innate within the body, when marvelously manifested and spiritually reflected, differ in no way from those of heaven. The *dantian*, the domain where spirit is mastered, reveals extraordinary scenes and luminous visions: numinous *lingzhi* are nurtured, their lush profusion presenting auspicious omens, while railings and balustrades are adorned with immortal blossoms—no need for distant seeking.

In the *Eighth Chapter on Spiritual Penetrations*, at that time, all below in the lower realms beheld the wondrous music of the celestial spheres resounding from the various heavens, revolving and swirling in harmony with the Emperor’s light, their sounds naturally resonant and harmonious. Again, all saw *luan* birds singing in melodious cries and phoenixes joining in song, their airborne voices attuned to rhythm; dragons frolicking and *lin* beasts circling in dance, soaring and wheeling at heaven’s summit. Precious blossoms from the heavens scattered and drifted down in profusion, covering every road in every realm.

At that moment, mortals and sages alike were awestruck and amazed; darkness and obscurity dissolved into light. Heavenly beings and mortals rejoiced and exulted, leaping and dancing in jubilation. Ordinary folk and scholars of the Dao all attained flight and ascension, gazing upward at the towering jeweled terraces of kalpas’ height, looking downward upon the purple clouds suffusing the vast expanse of the *Miluo* realm. In all these worlds, every person and people attained the wondrous transformation of the Dao’s *qi*. Those with white hair and wrinkled faces were all transformed and delivered, their locks becoming dark and lustrous, their complexions ruddy and youthful. The young and strong, the tender and small, saw their forms and features enhanced, their appearance radiant and resplendent, smooth and refined in exquisite beauty. All suffering and affliction were healed and pacified. Across the three thousand great worlds, the old and young alike universally awakened to liberation, enjoying peace and bliss, their hearts and minds filled with joy. In every land beneath heaven, songs and hymns celebrated the great peace of the realm.

The *Celestial Venerable of Longevity* states: When the Emperor’s light pervades all at that time, the people of every world below behold the secret and wondrous music of the celestial spheres in each heaven, revolving and swirling in accord with the Emperor’s light, their sounds naturally resonant and harmonious. Again, all witness auspicious *luan* birds singing in melodious cries and divine phoenixes joining in song, their airborne voices attuned to rhythm; dark dragons dancing in play and auspicious *lin* beasts circling in spirals, soaring and dancing at heaven’s summit. Precious blossoms from the heavens scatter and drift down in profusion, covering every road in every realm.

At that time, mortals and sages alike were awestruck and amazed; hidden darkness dissolved into light. Heavenly beings and mortals all rejoiced and exulted, leaping and dancing in jubilation. Ignorant mortals and scholars of the Dao all attained divine ascent to the Jade Capital, flying upward to heaven, gazing upward at the towering jeweled terraces of kalpas’ height, looking downward upon the purple clouds suffusing the vast expanse of the *Miluo* realm. In all these worlds, every person and people universally attained the wondrous transformation of the Dao’s *qi*. The aged with white hair and wrinkled faces were all transformed and delivered, their locks becoming dark and lustrous, their complexions ruddy and youthful. The young and strong, the tender and small, saw their forms and features enhanced, their appearance radiant and resplendent, smooth and refined in exquisite beauty. All suffering and affliction were healed and pacified. Across the three thousand great worlds, the old and young alike universally awakened to liberation, enjoying peace and bliss, their hearts and minds filled with joy. In every land beneath heaven, songs and hymns celebrated the great peace of the realm.

The *Thunder Gate Messenger* states: The wondrous music of the celestial spheres takes gold as the chief of the eight sounds. The primordial tones of the supreme *Brahmā* realm are the indestructible essence of gold. All tones harmonize without discord or corruption—this is the origin of musical harmony. Some say that it is naturally balanced without need for tuning, a sound rarely heard in the world, hence it is called the music of the celestial spheres. Others say that the great creation is the vast *hongjun*, and the wondrous workings of the Dao’s transformation naturally embody supreme harmony; the marvel of celestial music is the transformation of great creation, hence it is called the music of the celestial spheres. *Yongyue huanxin* describes leaping and dancing for joy, hands and feet moving in delight. Eight *chi* make a *ren*. The jeweled terraces of heaven endure through countless kalpas without decay or destruction, hence they are called *jieren*. *Yangguan* means to raise one’s gaze; *fumian* means to lower one’s glance. *Ziyun Milo* refers to the precious realm of the Yellow and the Old, not merely the terraces below—thus there is a sense of both upward and downward contemplation.

*Gan* is a deep blue with a reddish hue; *ganfa* refers to what is now called "green locks." As the *Guanshi* observes: Humans possess yin and yang, their bodies divided into upper and lower. The *qi* above is always pure, while the *qi* below is always turbid. Only when *qi* intermingles without harmony do the upper and the wondrous become unseen and unheard, leading to decline, weakness, and depletion. Yet when one aligns with the great Dao, unites with the primal mystery, and radiates wondrous light, one truly hears the secret sounds and truly sees the mysterious transformations: the elegant strains of the celestial spheres, the *lin* and phoenix, dragon and *luan*, all manifesting their marvels. Auspicious blossoms drift and scatter, suffusing all with beauty; yin and yang’s *qi* bears fine fragrance, and the spirit is stirred in awe. All hidden recesses become luminous, above and below harmonize and flow freely—this is the leaping and dancing joy of heaven and humanity. When yin dissolves and wondrous intent ascends to the mysterious, even ordinary folk and scholars of the Dao ascend. Gazing upward at the azure-jeweled terraces, looking downward upon the pervasively mysterious realm, the land is prosperous and the people at peace, *qi* harmonious and spirit serene. The aged become strong, the pacified attain supreme balance, the deficient become abundant, sinews are renewed and marrow transformed, and one perpetually preserves supreme harmony, the body in perfect accord, delighting in this wondrous transformation.

Not only do the aged regain youth and the young grow ever more radiant, but the world erupts in song, rejoicing in the great peace of the realm. Ah, this is indeed the truth! Those who comprehend savor it deeply.

**Ninefold Manifestations of Spirit-Power**
At that time, the divine wind spreads far and wide, the myriad *qi* raise the life-giving essence; heaven quakes and earth splits, withered bones revive, sunken corpses and wandering souls all regain their forms. The iron-walled Fengdu, the eternal night of the Nine Dark Realms, instantly shatter—hell’s suffering souls are transformed and reborn in the heavens, and the torments of the Three Evil Paths are all at once released. Then, by the power of this radiance, all sin-laden multitudes are reborn in the great celestial palaces of the ten directions.

Wei Boyang said:
When the world sings in joy of great peace,
The Emperor’s virtue and divine wind resound afar,
The wondrous myriad *qi* raise the tide of supreme harmony.
Qian’s creative impulse stirs, yang’s vigor moves in strength—
heaven quakes with the mysterious chariot;
Kun unfolds its destiny, yin’s softness yields in compliance—
earth splits to reveal the numinous depths.
Long-withered bones revive anew,
sunken corpses and scattered souls all regain their forms,
unbound and undispersed.
The underworld’s Fengdu, the great Iron Enclosure,
eternally shrouded in darkness, the Nine Dark Prisons,
instantly collapse—no more gloom, no more dungeon bonds.
All suffering souls in the hells are transformed and reborn in the heavens.
The torments of the Three Evil Paths—hell, hungry ghosts, and beasts—
are all at once released, their karmic debts forever dissolved.
Then, by the power of the Jade Emperor’s mysterious auspice,
the illumination of the Dao’s light,
all sin-laden multitudes are reborn in the great celestial palaces
beyond the ten directions, above the ethereal clouds, in the boundless void.

**My humble observation:**
Nothing quickens the ten thousand things like the wind.
The Emperor’s transformation is profoundly subtle, its spirit inexhaustible,
pervading the entire dharma-realm.
Those who receive it remain unaware—hence it is called the *divine wind*.
*Qi* may manifest in colors, yet it has no fixed form—
how then can one speak of "raising the essence"?
Where *qi* flows, the Emperor’s virtue operates in silence,
supreme harmony overflows, saturating and moistening all—
thus it is called *raising the essence*.
The "quaking of heaven" does not refer to thunder,
but to yang’s virtue flourishing in abundance,
emerging from *Zhen* to bestow life.
The "splitting of earth" is not a violent rupture,
but the earth’s way rising from humility,
yin settling and yang reviving,
revealing the marvel of nurturing growth.
No longer sealed, the earth’s hidden treasures are released—
hence it is called *splitting*.
"Withered bones reviving" does not mean decayed bones rising again,
but those whose hearts have died and forms withered.
Awakening to the Dao and knowing truth,
they return yang and transform their bones—
immortals among men, withered bones reborn.
The *po* soul dwells in the body, delighting in death,
feasting on offerings.
Those who live without understanding the Dao,
tainted by worldly dust and defiled by attachments,
lose their spirit at death, their *hun* dispersing and *po* scattering.
Some cling stubbornly, others fall into sinful prisons,
their *po* essence dissolving and drifting,
phantasmal and adrift in karmic suffering—
the *flying po* of evil deeds.
"Regaining form" means *hun* and *po* reuniting,
no longer adrift or submerged,
freed from the terrors of sin and all underworld karma.
Fengdu’s iron walls, so rigid and unyielding,
are all self-imposed barriers of sinful souls.
The Emperor’s radiance illumines the profound—
with a single gleam, sins vanish.
The prisons of eternal night, where no sky or sun is seen,
the Nine Dark Realms, all open to light;
Fengdu’s iron walls instantly crumble to dust,
and the suffering multitudes of hell are reborn in heaven.
The torments of the Three Evil Paths are likewise released.
At that time, by the grace of this light,
the sin-laden multitudes are reborn in the great celestial palaces of the ten directions.

What is a human life?
Spirit complete, form whole, modeled on heaven and earth;
yin and yang, the Five Phases—
no aspect of nature is lacking.
Originally pervaded by supreme harmony,
pure and unstained,
yet deluded by worldly enticements,
mistaking the false for the real,
clinging to dust and defilement,
grasping at illusions,
once attachments take hold, they become unbreakable.
Deception deepens over time, leaving no room for enlightenment.
Joy, anger, sorrow, thought, grief, fear, and shock—
sudden terrors strike, the heart lacks constancy,
restless and ceaseless.
Selfish desires torment the mind and burden the body,
unheeding of warnings—
this is the "sunken corpse and flying *po*,"
Fengdu’s iron walls, the dark prison’s confinement.
Yet if one severs desire and forgets the self,
letting the celestial ruler remain at peace,
supreme harmony becomes clear and penetrating,
stirring the wind of *Xun*, circulating the great harmony,
preserving the vast and pure,
harmonizing the Dao’s pulse—
then the divine wind spreads far and wide,
the myriad *qi* raise the essence,
yang bestows and yin receives,
their interaction restores yang,
dissolving boundless suffering,
eradicating endless dust,
shattering eons of delusion and attachment,
freeing one from the karmic paths of darkness.
Thus heaven quakes and earth splits,
withered bones revive,
sunken corpses and flying *po* regain their forms,
Fengdu’s iron walls and the Nine Dark Realms instantly collapse.
Yin dissolves and yang grows,
desire fades and principle returns,
the turbid is transformed into the pure,
essence and *qi* refine into spirit.
Freed from the Five Sufferings and merging the Five *Qi*,
one silently ascends to the primordial palace;
purifying the Three Karmas and realizing the Three Origins,
one ascends to the Purple Palace.
Thus the suffering souls of hell are transformed and reborn in the heavens,
the torments of the Three Evil Paths are all at once released,
and the sin-laden multitudes, by the power of this light,
are reborn in the celestial palaces.
Those born into this world—ponder this, treasure this.

**Tenth Manifestation of Spirit-Power**
At that time, the Jade Emperor divided his body, pervading all the great celestial palaces, causing each to naturally manifest: white jade became their capitals, yellow gold their towers, with seven-jeweled numinous gardens and Great Radiance Halls, radiant thrones, banners, canopies, and parasols, rare treasures and wondrous flowers spread throughout. Then the Jade Emperor, with his divided body, filled all these places—within the white jade capitals, the yellow gold towers, the seven-jeweled numinous gardens, and the Great Radiance Halls upon their radiant thrones—universally expounding the pure and liberating Dao to the ten directions.

Master Zhongli Quan said:
When that great radiance was released,
the Jade Emperor divided his dharma-body,
pervading all the great celestial palaces,
causing each to naturally manifest.
White jade capitals, yellow gold towers,
seven-jeweled adornments in the numinous gardens—
all were like the Jade Emperor’s own abode.

The Great Radiance Mysterious Hall was fully arrayed with the Great Radiance Precious Throne, the Mysterious Banner of the Dao, ritual pennants, floral canopies, rare and wondrous treasures, and exquisite celestial flowers, spread throughout all the great celestial palaces. At that time, the Jade Emperor, with his wondrously divided body, pervaded each of the great celestial palaces, spiritually transforming the Jade Capital, Golden Towers, and Mysterious Gardens. Ascending the Great Radiance Hall, he mounted the Radiance Throne, where every divine seat shone with light. The Dharma Throne of the Primordial Jade Emperor radiated a light most wondrous, so vast it could not be measured, so divine it could not be described—surpassing even the Dharma King’s throne of the Buddha’s realm. Thus, the Emperor’s transformed bodies ascended these thrones, universally expounding to the ten directions the true, pure, and utterly pristine Dao of awakening and liberation. To expound is to illuminate and clarify its meaning.

Master Guan’s Humble Insight says: The primordial spirit of humans is numinous and unconfined, reaching everywhere without obstruction, fundamentally identical to the Jade Emperor’s wondrous transformations. The Purple Palace and Cinnabar Terrace are inherently no different from the celestial divine palaces; auspicious mushrooms and divine medicines are no different from the treasures and flowers of heaven. Yet people, ensnared by worldly profit, lose mastery of their primordial spirit, and so cannot circulate freely or penetrate all things, nor manifest numinous power at every turn. They forfeit their true purity and fail to attain the Dao of liberation. If one preserves truth and harmonizes with the Dao, silently revering the Spirit King, then numinous movement becomes universal, filling the entire body—just as the Jade Emperor’s divided bodies pervade all celestial palaces. The mortal form attains the wondrous, rare treasures manifest marvels, and pearl towers, jeweled halls, jade palaces, and jasper terraces become the golden and jade capitals and seven-jeweled mysterious gardens of heaven. The divine palace and cinnabar terrace are the Great Radiance Hall and its Radiance Throne. Qi harmonized and pulses flowing, light stirs and rosy clouds rise—these are the banners, pennants, and canopies. The flourishing of divine mushrooms is like the rare flowers of heaven. When the primordial spirit governs and presides over the cinnabar terrace, unfolding the numinous and revealing the mysterious, it is as when the Jade Emperor, with his divided bodies, simultaneously ascends each throne to expound the Dao. Our true nature endures through kalpas unharmed, without duality or admixture, unbound and unobstructed, fundamentally pure and unstained, naturally liberated. Its great luminosity is never dimmed. If one can spiritually govern and unfold the numinous, then the entire body becomes mysteriously transformed. Unconfined by the three thousand worlds, clearly understanding causes and conditions, never deluded about reality, inwardly and outwardly radiant and transparent, penetrating the divine and attaining transformation—this is the Jade Emperor universally expounding, clarifying, and teaching the pure and liberating Dao to all worlds. Those who comprehend may savor this meaning for themselves.

In the eleventh chapter on the Jade Emperor’s spiritual transformations, each of his manifestations was attended on left and right by immeasurable Celestial Perfected, Great Sages, Wondrously Accomplished Realized Ones, and Numinous Consorts and Jade Maidens. These Jade Maidens possessed countenances of exquisite beauty, refined and wondrously unique. Their forms were adorned with celestial treasures rare and divine, their voices clear and penetrating, delighting all who heard them. From their bodies emanated a subtle, wondrous, and naturally liberating fragrance, its fragrance rich and pervasive, filling all the celestial palaces, the most wondrous and blissful pure lands, and every blessed place across all worlds.

The Queen Mother said: At that time, each of the Jade Emperor’s transformed bodies throughout the celestial palaces was attended on left and right by boundless Celestial Perfected, spiritually potent and transformative Great Sages, Wondrously Accomplished and majestically adorned Realized Ones, numinous and transcendent Immortal Consorts, and Guardian Jade Maidens. These Jade Maidens possessed countenances and forms of exquisite beauty and wondrous uniqueness, dignified, splendid, and radiant, surpassing all others in divine marvel. Their bodies were adorned with celestial treasures rare and divine, their speech and voices clear and resonant, delighting all who heard them. From their persons emanated a profound, subtle, and divinely wondrous fragrance of great liberation and natural purity, its fragrance rich and pervasive, filling all celestial palaces, the most divinely blissful pure lands, and every blessed gathering across all worlds.

The Exegesis says: The Wondrously Accomplished are those in whom all virtues arise without forced effort, their merit and power inexhaustible, naturally perfected as Realized Ones. Their spiritual powers are immeasurable, hence they are called Wondrously Accomplished. The Numinous Consorts and Jade Maidens are deities transformed from the wondrous qi of the Yin and Brahman, guarding and serving the Perfected Emperor. All celestial maidens are so named. Free from desire and encumbrance, they differ from demonic women. Their virtue and merit complete, noble, beautiful, and revered, they remain purely unsullied and unadulterated—hence they are called Numinous Consorts and Jade Maidens, not referring solely to the Empress. These Jade Maidens are as described: their countenances exquisitely beautiful—*shu* means beauty; *duan*, dignified and upright; *li*, splendid and radiant; *qi*, divinely wondrous and rare; *te*, surpassing all beauty, unmatched in the world. Their forms adorned with celestial treasures—celestial consorts, transformed by divine light and spiritual power, adorned with wondrous treasures, their bodies and countenances unseen in the mortal realm. Their voices clear and resonant—*yan* refers to speech, *yin* to sound.

Clear—voices and words distinct. Penetrating—pervading and universally heard.

The subtle and wondrous, liberated and spontaneous fragrance: the consorts, having attained profound awakening and great liberation, their mysterious mechanism unfathomable, their divine wonder immeasurable, require no artificial crafting—naturally exuding a fragrant aroma. Yet none know whence this fragrance arises, hence it is called subtle and wondrous. This scent is rich and pervasive—*fen* denotes the diffusion of a fine and beautiful aroma; *fu*, the dense and luxuriant fragrance that clings and lingers.

Pervading all heavens and the most wondrous Pure Lands—*zhou* means to reach all; *bian*, to extend broadly; *ji*, utmost. In each of the great celestial palaces, the Jade Maidens who attend and guard the transformed emanations of the Jade Emperor—this fragrance does not linger in one place alone but suffuses every world and all heavens, the most wondrous lands free from suffering. The great earth encompasses all worlds of mountains and rivers. Blessed realms—where worlds exist, there is generation and transformation, hence they are called blessed realms. Alternatively, it is said that only through reverence, sincerity, and faith may one perceive this rare fragrance. In every world touched by the Jade Emperor’s light, all beings awaken faith and encounter the wondrous scent of the Numinous Consorts and Jade Maidens, hence they are called blessed realms. This interpretation also holds.

All sentient beings of the Six Paths who perceive this fragrance universally receive deliverance. These are the heavenly path, human path, demonic path, hell path, hungry ghost path, and animal path. Among the heavenly path, all celestial beings who can perceive this fragrance will have the Five Decays and Four Signs forever dissolved, their heavenly blessings ever-increasing. Among the human path, kings, ministers, and the multitudes who can perceive this fragrance will attain the joys of long life in the human and heavenly realms; should their bodies pass away, they will achieve the Way of liberation through *shijie*—the shedding of the mortal husk. Among the demonic path, all demons who can perceive this fragrance will dwell peacefully in celestial palaces, their struggles and battles at rest. Among the hell path, all sinful souls who can perceive this fragrance will escape the torments of hell and attain the bliss of Pure Lands. Among the hungry ghost path, all hungry ghosts who can perceive this fragrance will be sated, free from the torments of hunger and thirst. Among the animal path, all beasts who can perceive this fragrance will escape the sufferings of the animal realm and attain the joy of wisdom.

The Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering states: All sentient beings within the Six Paths who perceive the spontaneous fragrance of the Numinous Consorts and Jade Maidens universally receive the grace of transformation and deliverance. The beings of the Six Paths—namely, the celestial beings of all heavens, the human and heavenly beings of all worlds, the demons of all demonic paths, the sinful souls of the hell path, the destitute spirits of the hungry ghost path, and the karmically bound beasts of the animal path—if any among the celestial beings of the four kinds of heavenly realms can perceive the spontaneous fragrance of the Numinous Consorts and Jade Maidens, the sufferings of the Five Decays and Four Signs will be forever eradicated, and their heavenly blessings will increase. Among all the human realms of the great earth, if emperors, ministers, and the multitudes can perceive this spontaneous fragrance, they will retain their forms and abide in the world, enjoying the long life of humans and heavens. Should their bodies pass into extinction, they will achieve the Way of *shijie*—unfettered liberation through the shedding of the mortal husk. Among all the heavens and demonic paths of the worlds, if any among the demon kings, demon folk, demon women, or demonic spirits can perceive this spontaneous fragrance, they will peacefully dwell in separate celestial palaces, their conflicts and battles at rest. Among all the underworlds and hell paths of the worlds, if any sinful souls can perceive this spontaneous fragrance, they will escape the torments of hell and be reborn in the bliss of Pure Lands. Among all the destitute spirits of the hungry ghost path, if any hungry ghosts can perceive this spontaneous fragrance, they will be filled and sated, free from the torments of hunger and thirst. Among all the karmically bound beasts of the animal path, if any beasts can perceive this spontaneous fragrance, they will escape the sufferings of the animal realm and attain the joy of wisdom and clarity.

The Perfected Immortal Sa states: The Six Paths are like roads, wherein beings undergo cyclic rebirth across six kinds of destinies, hence they are called the Six Paths. First is the heavenly path: heaven has thirty-six designations. The highest four heavens are called the Seed People, where the immortals of the Nine Mystic Palaces and Seven Treasures reside—what Buddhists call the stage of non-retrogression. Below the Seed People are the Four Revered and Mystic Heavens, which Buddhists call the Four Dhyāna Heavens of Form. Below the Revered and Mystic Heavens are the Four Heavens of Forgotten Images, which Buddhists call the Four Dhyāna Heavens of the Formless Realm. Below the Heavens of Forgotten Images are the eighteen heavens of the Form Realm. Below the eighteen heavens of the Form Realm are the six heavens of the Desire Realm. Each world contains thirty-six heavens, and all worlds are alike.

The four heavens of the Seed People are realms of wondrous emptiness and subtle existence, where divine transformations and mysterious spirits abide eternally without decay. Only the highest perfected immortals dwell there, with no celestial beings—thus they are not counted among the paths of celestial beings. The Four Revered and Mystic Heavens are realms where worldly defilements have only just been purified, their transformations still incomplete and not yet divine, not yet attaining the Great Vehicle. Though they surpass the human path, even they cannot escape the great kalpas. There are the Formless Realm, the Form Realm, and the Desire Realm. The celestial beings of these heavens are tall and majestic, their forms like gleaming silver. They do not rely on the illumination of the sun and moon, for they possess their own radiance. The celestial beings of the Sun and Moon Heaven stand five *li* tall, with their height increasing progressively to hundreds of *yojanas*—a *yojana* being forty *li*. The Daoist scriptures say: a *yushe* is a measure of distance. They wear celestial robes weighing six *zhu* and two *qian* and five *fen*. Their heads bear natural pearl crowns. Their eyes do not blink, their heads do not bow, they stand without leaning, their eyes shed no tears, and their bodies know no weariness. Yet if they do not awaken to the Great Vehicle, when their heavenly blessings are exhausted, their pearl crowns shatter, their eyes blink and shed tears, their bodies stoop and grow weary—then the Five Decays and Four Unlovely Signs appear.

If one receives the fragrance of nature with utmost sincerity and reverence, awakening to the wondrous origin of this scent, one suddenly realizes the Great Dao—without relying on external teachings to perceive this fragrance—and thus attains enlightenment. This is called "the power to perceive." The Five Decays and Four Unlovely Signs are forever dispelled.

"Forever" means "eternal." Eternally freed from the suffering of decay, one’s heavenly blessings instead increase. With each turn, blessings grow boundlessly, never diminishing.

The paths of humanity differ: there are yin and yang, old and young, noble and base, rich and poor, sages and fools. Without attaining the Great Dao, one’s lifespan is short, death is arduous, and the corpse does not decompose. Across all worlds, whether emperors, ministers, high and low officials, or the countless masses—*zhao* meaning ten million, *shu* meaning multitude—the term *zhaoshu* encompasses all people, emphasizing their vast number. If they receive the natural fragrance and awaken to the Great Dao, perceiving its subtle and wondrous scent, they attain unhindered, long-lived joy in the human or heavenly realms. Even if they pass away, they may secretly shed their mortal form through *shijie* or transcendence: casting off the shell through seated or standing liberation, or seizing another’s body in rebirth. *Shijie* may manifest as apparent death followed by reappearance in the world, with both corpse and spirit departing, or as feigned death leading to ascension.

Among the demonic paths, their kinds vary. Some, like the *Gusiluo*, contend with the Heavenly Emperor, disrupting celestial order—such as the asuras and rebels. All demonic realms are either fond of war or create illusions and plagues, dwelling in constant unrest. If these demons perceive the natural wondrous fragrance and awaken to the true Dao, they turn from evil to righteousness, their dwellings become peaceful, and they remain in their proper stations. In the heavens, they occupy separate domains, no longer delighting in strife, conflict, or the suffering of war. Each finds respite and rest.

The suffering of battle arises from conflict, which brings injury, and war, which brings slaughter—victory and defeat alternate, enemies become foes. Thus, it is called suffering. Each attains rest, for though spirits do not invade demons, demons disturb them, and one must respond by subduing them. Now, having perceived the fragrance and awakened to the wondrous, demons dwell in peace without contention, and spirits are likewise undisturbed. Thus, both spirits and demons find rest.

In all worlds, hells bear many names: Fengdu, Blood Lake, Blood Gorge, Icy Hell, Fire Chariot, Knife Mountain, Sword Tree, River of Desire, Mind-Restraint, Iron Bed, Wind Blades, Iron Dogs, Bronze Serpents, Cauldrons of Boiling Oil, Sawing, Grinding, Flaying, Naraka, Tongue-Pulling, and the Thirty-Six Hells. All souls enduring punishment find it difficult to escape the suffering of hell’s imprisonment. Yet if they perceive this natural fragrance, they awaken and transcend, leaving behind the torments of hell to be reborn in a pure and blissful land.

Hungry ghosts, bound for kalpas in the ghostly register, may have slender necks and bloated bellies, or massive heads and emaciated frames; their throats may be blocked, or they may consume burning coals and smoke, molten copper, or iron pellets. For generations, they never taste water or food, enduring hunger, thirst, and pain, their suffering ceaseless. Yet if all hungry ghosts in these worlds perceive this natural fragrance and awaken to the Dao, the flavor of the Dao fills their bellies, sating their hunger and quenching their thirst. Their throats open, and the torment of starvation vanishes forever.

In the animal realm, all creatures born from eggs, moisture, or transformation—whether soft or wriggling—are included, not merely birds and beasts. Though nurtured within heaven and earth, animals lack wisdom and endure much suffering, from which escape is difficult. If all animals across the worlds perceive the natural wondrous fragrance and awaken to the Dao, they attain liberation, their karmic retribution ends, and they escape the suffering of the animal realm, gaining the joy of wisdom and understanding.

Animals are not without awareness, yet they cannot speak of the Dao or embody it; their forms differ, and their spirits are distinct. Some are domesticated for riding or labor, others hunted and slaughtered, trapped in pits, or butchered for kitchens—consuming fur and blood, their flesh and bones utterly devoured. Their suffering is beyond words. Yet upon perceiving the fragrance, they gain wisdom, for this is the power of the Emperor’s light.

A humble observation: the two preceding passages share a single intent. The original spirit of the human body governs yin and yang; true sages, wondrous practices, and divine maidens all arise from it. Within the harmony of spirit, qi, essence, and blood, the subtle fragrance of liberation exists naturally—profound and ineffable. The balance or imbalance of qi, unless one is mad or foolish, also pertains to the Six Paths. If the Heavenly Lord is not at peace, one is bound by the Five Agents; if thoughts are not severed, one is disturbed by the ceaseless tumult of yin and yang. Thus, one is also subject to the turning of the Six Paths. Perceiving the beauty of the Six Ding Jade Maidens within oneself, smelling the natural fragrance of harmony and liberation, and illuminating the Great Dao—so that the original spirit ever shines—one beholds the Emperor’s light and attains transcendence. Forever freed from the dust of the mundane, unbound by the body, one is thus eternally released from the suffering of the Six Paths. Those who understand will savor this and grasp the meaning of these two passages.

**Chapter Twelve: Divine Powers**

At that time, the multitudes of beings born into the celestial heavens as retribution for their sins, having attained rebirth in these sublime celestial palaces, by virtue of the compassionate light’s embrace, awakened and each clearly understood the causes of sin and blessing. Together with their retinues, they performed celestial music, their melodies harmonious and resonant. Some texts render *ji* as "art," while others use the character *ji*. Pronounced *zhīqiè* or *qújì*, it means "with." The character *ji* is correct. Joyfully, they came before the Emperor.

These multitudes, each harboring sorrow, together raised their voices and said: "We, your servants, have passed through countless kalpas, great and small, never beholding the Three Lights of sun, moon, and stars, ever dwelling in darkness and gloom. Cast into the Three Evil Paths of hell, hungry ghosts, and beasts, we have endured much suffering and affliction. By Your boundless grace, O Supreme Emperor, You extended Your skillful means and radiated Your compassionate light, taking pity and delivering us, so that we might all be reborn in the heavens. All our evil karmic retributions have been utterly extinguished, with no bonds or entanglements remaining. We have all attained rebirth in the celestial realms, gazing up in reverence to the Jade Emperor, each arriving before the primordial and most venerable Dao.

When these reborn celestial multitudes of sinful beings had finished speaking, they bowed their heads and returned to their original positions.

Master Ge the Immortal states: When the time comes for the transformation through fragrant liberation, all the sinful multitudes of hell, hungry ghosts, and other paths who are reborn in the most sublime heavens—having been embraced by the wondrous, spontaneous fragrance—by virtue of the Jade Emperor’s great compassionate light’s embrace, are thus received. *She* (摄) means to guide, uphold, and preserve. *Shou* (受) means to receive and guide the hun and shen, summoning them to return to the true. The Emperor radiates His compassionate light, wondrously transforming true fragrance, embracing all sinful multitudes, who then awaken to the great Dao. *Jue* (觉) means to know the reason why. *Wu* (悟) means thorough comprehension. The sinful multitudes, awakened, escape the destinies of the Three Evil Paths, each clearly and penetratingly understanding the causes of sin and blessing. *Gen* (根) is called *yin* (因, cause). Where there is cause, there is effect. *You lai* (由来) is called *yuan* (缘, condition). Where there is condition, there is karma. Having clearly understood the causes and conditions of sinful karma and blessed virtue, together with their kin and affiliated kindred—*yu* (与) means "together." The sinful multitudes, whether demons, ghosts, or karmic beasts, each have their own kin and affiliated groups—once reborn in heaven and enlightened to the Dao, they join with their kin to perform celestial arts and wondrous music. *Tian ji* (天伎), when interpreted as *yi* (艺, art), signifies that their mastery is all-encompassing. Coming before the Emperor—*yi* (诣) means "to arrive." These reborn celestial multitudes of sinful beings, each containing sorrow within, together raised their voices and said: 'We, your servants, have passed through countless kalpas, great and small, never beholding the Three Lights of sun, moon, and stars, ever dwelling in the dark and gloomy depths, cast into the Three Evil Paths of hell, hungry ghosts, and beasts, enduring much karmic suffering and sorrow. By Your boundless grace, O Supreme Emperor—*fu* (伏) means to bow the body low to the ground; *meng* (蒙) means to receive and be graced by. The phrase *fu meng* expresses the humility of the inferior receiving the favor of the superior. Henceforth, all instances of *fu meng* should be understood thus—we have been graced by Your universally applied skillful means, radiating great light. *Fangbian* (方便) refers to the wondrousness of the Dao, which universally benefits beings, hence called *fangbian*. With the radiance of Your compassionate light, You took pity and delivered us, so that we might all be reborn in the heavens. All our evil karmic retributions have been utterly extinguished, with no bonds or entanglements remaining. We have all attained rebirth in the celestial realms, gazing up in reverence to the Jade Emperor, each arriving before the primordial and most venerable Dao.'

When these reborn celestial multitudes of sinful beings had finished speaking, they bowed their heads and returned to their original positions of attendance.

This humble commentator observes: Humans, endowed with yin and yang, are originally of the same essence as Heaven and Earth. Yet, deluded by profit and desire, they defile their true hearts, persisting in evil without repentance, dismissing the workings of karmic retribution and rebirth as nonexistent. Thus, they fail to recognize the causes and conditions of sin and blessing. The wondrous harmony of true intent is lost, obscured by the snares of worldly dust. Greed, anger, ignorance, and jealousy arise; madness, sorrow, and joy alternate; cravings and the pursuit of fame know no end. They abide in darkness, like the denizens of hell, hungry ghosts, and beasts in the Three Evil Paths, enduring ceaseless torment, suffering as the sinful multitudes do. This is the state of those whose evil karma is not exhausted, who remain bound and unable to be reborn in heaven. When the primordial spirit governs and the light of Heaven shines forth, the yin qi of the body, along with杂念 and evil destinies, are all restored to true qi, ascending to the realm of the Nine Yangs. The threshold between good and evil, the ordinary and the sacred, becomes swift as an echo, with karmic retribution manifestly clear. Thus, the rhythm of Great Harmony is released, revealing the numinous and secret, paying homage to the Primordial Emperor. This is how the sinful multitudes, embraced by the Emperor’s compassionate light, each clearly understand the causes of sin and blessing, joining with their kin to perform celestial arts and music, coming before the Emperor. As yin qi dissipates,杂念 are forgotten, evil destinies are purified, evil is transformed into good, and the spirit and life are returned to the Dao. Through repentance and awakening, they come to know the inauspiciousness of their past evil deeds. Those who fail to awaken to the great Dao are like those facing a wall or sitting at the bottom of a well—truly, they see nothing. Obscured by the paths of duality and multiplicity, they are beset by many fears. Only when the primordial spirit governs the Jade Terrace, descending the true and guiding the numinous, wondrously radiating the mysterious splendor, transforming the yin and completing the field, are they liberated from the dust of the mundane, forever free from entanglements. Their hearts become one with the Dao, silently paying homage to the Emperor. This is how the sinful multitudes, harboring sorrow, spoke of their suffering in the dark kalpas, having been graced by the Emperor’s light, which took pity and delivered them, extinguishing their evil karma, freeing them from bonds, enabling their rebirth, and allowing them to pay homage to the Emperor and arrive before the Dao. This is the most wondrous transformation of the celestial realms. To draw near is to take from one’s own body, for the Dao originally resides within. It urges people to turn inward and practice in reality. Thus, the four lines above—'bowed their heads and returned to their original positions'—require no further elaboration. Those who understand will ponder this deeply.

The second volume of the *Commentary on the Imperial Scripture* concludes.
The third volume of the *Commentary on the Imperial Scripture* begins.

The Fifty-Fifth Celestial Master of the Han Succession, Great Perfected Zhang Guoxiang, collated
Examined by Retired Scholar Fangwai of Jishui, Jiangxi, Luo Hongxian
Compiled by Zhou Xuanzhen of Xiaozhaochen, Jinan, Shandong
*Chapter on Divine Penetrations*, Thirteenth Section

At that time, the Jade Emperor emitted a wondrous voice, universally addressing the sacred assemblies of the ten directions: "All of you, listen carefully. These multitudes of sinful beings, across vast kalpas, have indulged their unenlightened nature, committing the ten evil deeds, polluting the six defilements, and entangling the three karmic actions. Recklessly following their desires, they have never awakened, accumulating hidden sins and manifest transgressions day by day, month by month. Turning their backs on the Dao and deviating from truth, they follow perversity and abandon rectitude. With every thought and intention, they bind themselves to faults and errors. Thus, after the end of their lives, they fall into the three evil destinies, unable to attain liberation. Had they not encountered this Dharma assembly today, by what means could they escape?

The Great Emperor of Purple Tenuity stated: At the time of luminous embrace, the Jade Emperor emitted a wondrous voice. This wondrous voice is pure, resonant, and radiant, pervading the three thousand great worlds so that all may hear—peerless in its marvel. Hence, it is called the wondrous voice. It universally proclaimed to the celestial emperors, sacred perfected beings, and divine assemblies of the ten directions and all worlds: 'All of you, listen carefully.' *You* refers to *these*. *Listen carefully* means to listen with focused and true attention. The Jade Emperor instructed the sacred assemblies to listen carefully to his teaching, then spoke of these multitudes of sinful beings in the three evil destinies across vast kalpas. *Vast* means boundless and remote. From past kalpas until now, these sinful beings have indulged their unenlightened nature. Though their nature is originally numinous and bright, they give free rein to their desires, acting with madness, confusion, and disorder, following their impulses without returning to their original numinous and awakened essence. Thus, it is called the unenlightened nature. They commit the ten evil karmic obstructions. The *ten evils* are: three bodily evils—killing, stealing, and sexual misconduct; three mental evils—greed, hatred, and delusion; and four verbal evils—divisive speech, harsh speech, frivolous speech, and false speech. The accumulation of these ten evils leads to karmic retribution, hence called *evil deeds*. The six defilements thoroughly pollute. The *six defilements* refer to the impurities of the six senses—eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind. Alternatively, they may be understood as wealth, sensuality, fame, food, sleep, and self-serving desires—these six defilements are also valid. Both inner and outer aspects of the body are tainted by defilements, with no purity remaining; thus, it is called *thorough pollution*. The three karmic actions entangle. The *three karmic actions* are the three poisonous evils of body, speech, and mind. Alternatively, they may refer to past karmic causes, present transgressions, and future karmic consequences—this interpretation is also valid. *Entangle* means to coil, and *bind* means to constrain. Accumulated karma is as heavy as a rope binding a person, preventing liberation; thus, it is called *entanglement*. Recklessly indulging their thoughts without restraint, they act according to their whims, unaware of self-examination, giving free rein to evil without any period of awareness or repentance. Sins unseen and unheard by others, known only to oneself, are *hidden sins*. Transgressions witnessed by all, which cannot be concealed or corrected, are *manifest errors*. Day by day, they accumulate; month by month, they deepen. Turning their backs on the great Dao, they defy truth, follow perverse paths, and abandon the correct Way. With every thought and intention, they lack sincerity and rectitude. Following the impulses of delusion, they bind themselves to faults and errors. Thus, after the end of their lives, they fall into the three evil destinies—hell, hungry ghosts, and animals—unable to awaken or transcend. Had they not encountered this wondrous Dharma assembly today, by what means could they escape their karmic suffering?

I, the foolish one, observe: The spirit and qi of the human body are divided into yin and yang, pure and turbid. Indulging yin tendencies, following turbid and evil impulses, submitting to perverse thoughts, and abandoning true intention—these brew transgressions and make it difficult to escape karmic suffering. The longer evil accumulates, the less one understands the origin of karmic retribution, and thus they remain unawakened. When the original spirit is firmly settled, the wondrous intention spreads forth, the entire body receives its numinous influence, and one silently aligns with the profound mystery. Yang grows while yin diminishes; transgressions are dissolved, and sins are extinguished. Merging with the Dao and uniting with truth—all arises from the great awakening of wondrous enlightenment, recognizing the causes and conditions of faults and sins. The ancients regarded the pursuit of knowledge as the gateway to entry, and indeed, they saw clearly. Moreover, human nature admits no duality; good and evil both arise from the mind. The unenlightened nature is none other than the Dharma-nature. Thus, when it is obscured, one becomes an ordinary being; when it is awakened, one becomes a sage. The distinction between sage and madman is as thin as a hair’s breadth. If one can gather their emotions and return to their nature, stabilize their destiny and refine their spirit, grasp the subtleties of principle and desire, and understand the origin of defilements and evil, they will suddenly transcend karmic suffering, silently align with the profound mystery, and realize the Jade Emperor’s emission of the wondrous voice to proclaim the causes of indulging one’s nature and committing evil to the ten directions. Through encountering the Dharma assembly, beings of karmic types escape the three evil destinies. If one regards the unenlightened nature as a burden and seeks truth apart from it, dividing into two paths, one will fail to unite and attain the wondrous. Scholars should ponder this and naturally understand the essentials of transcending the ordinary.

*Chapter on Divine Penetrations*, Fourteenth Section

At that time, the Jade Emperor, in the transformed bodies of the various heavens, employed divine penetrations. Without moving from his place, he transported and received the celestial beings, enabling all to arrive at the Jade Clarity Sacred Realm of the Clear and Subtle Heaven, beneath the assembly of the Primordial Beginning. These multitudes were unaware and unknowing. At that time, the Heavenly Worthy and the assembly beheld the transformed bodies of the Jade Emperors from the ten directions, all gathering before the Heavenly Worthy’s assembly, like an infinite bright mirror reflecting all images, mutually containing and entering one another. Then, the great assembly bowed their heads, gazing reverently upon the transformed bodies of the Jade Emperor—the most venerable among the sacred—deepening their pure faith and increasing their joyful aspiration. Their minds were unwavering, arising in great steadfastness.

The Heavenly Emperor of the Celestial Sovereign stated: At the time of the great compassionate light universally embracing and receiving, the Jade Emperors in their transformed bodies within the various celestial palaces employed their great divine penetrations, majestically unmoving.
