Through the wondrous transport of their embracing and receiving divine light, they moved and guided the celestial beings of the various heavens, enabling all to arrive at the Clear and Subtle Heavenly Palace, the most supreme Jade Clarity Sacred Realm, beneath the assembly of the Primordial Beginning, the Ancestor of the Dao.

The Jade Clarity is incomparably revered, the great, pure, tranquil, and profoundly subtle heaven. The sacred □ realm is where the Most Real presides, the wondrous existence within the Void—where no ordinary spirits may easily arrive, the land of unwavering resolve. Beneath the assembly of the Primordial Beginning, none but the greatly divine and sagely, those of exceptional karmic affinity, may behold and gaze upon it. When the scripture was expounded, all the celestial beings arrived, for the Jade Emperor’s divine and compassionate reception enabled them to reach it. Thus, the great assembly of celestial beings, unaware and unknowing of how they came to be there, were blessed to arrive beneath the assembly of the Primordial Beginning. At this time, the Heavenly Venerable was none other than the Primordial Beginning Heavenly Venerable. Some mistakenly believe these to be the various Heavenly Emperors, but this is not so. At this moment, beneath the assembly of the Primordial Beginning, the entire assembly beheld the transformed bodies of the Jade Emperors from all ten directions universally gathering, arrayed without obstruction before the grand assembly of the Primordial Beginning, like an immeasurable host of great luminous mirrors reflecting the forms and images of all beings, mutually containing and interpenetrating without hindrance, drawn in without omission.

At this time, the great assembly prostrated themselves, touching their foreheads to the ground in reverence, gazing with joyful admiration upon the divine transformed bodies of the Jade Emperors—the most exalted among the sacred and true. The Jade Emperor is the sagely teacher of all buddhas, the sovereign of the myriad heavens, and thus is called the most venerable. Their pure and sincere faith deepened, their joyful aspiration grew ever more steadfast, their devotion to the Dao and return to the Real unwavering. Only with unchanging resolve is there true sincerity; only with genuine delight in the Great Dao is there true return and offering. The great assembly, overjoyed at beholding the wondrous transformations of the Jade Emperor, were filled with heartfelt reverence, thus their joyful aspiration increased, and they turned wholeheartedly in devotion. Without thoughts of retreat or wavering, they arose in great steadfastness and unwavering faith. A mind that retreats is not steadfast; a mind that wavers is not firm. Without steadfastness and firmness, there is no pure faith or joyful aspiration. Only in gazing upon the Jade Emperor with a mind free from retreat do they arouse the greatest, unchanging, and indestructible true resolve, forever returning to the Great Dao.

I humbly observe: the spirit and qi of humans share a common origin, whether pure or turbid, their wondrous transformations are without duality. If the mind does not align with the Dao, even with guiding and directing, it remains not the true path. Thus, the spirit does not congeal, the numinous is not revealed, and the secret transformations cannot manifest their marvels. If the primordial spirit congeals in truth, wondrously gathering all existence, silently paying homage to the True Emperor and assembling in the mysterious palace, true suchness is naturally at ease, without need for contrivance. This is like the Jade Emperor’s transformed bodies, their divine penetrations unmoving, yet transporting and receiving celestial beings to the assembly beneath the Primordial Beginning in the Clear and Subtle Heaven. When qi and essence mysteriously unite, silently following the Emperor’s decree, unknowing and unaware, the primordial spirit moves with numinosity, illuminating the body’s myriad wonders without constraint or leakage—thus the great assembly, unknowing and unaware, ascends in spirit to the upper realms. The Primordial Beginning and the assembly beheld the gathered transformed bodies of the Emperors, like great luminous mirrors, their radiant lights shining forth, all images mutually containing and interpenetrating.

When qi and essence merge with the spirit, returning to the secret and the true, free from defilement and falsity, joy and ease arise naturally. Once attained, it is forever attained, never destroyed nor lost—just as the great assembly, gazing upon the transformed bodies of the Jade Emperor, recognized their supreme venerability, deepened their pure faith, increased their joyful aspiration, and without thoughts of retreat, arose in great steadfastness. Scholars should inwardly embody this to perceive its wonder.

At the time of the fifteenth chapter on divine penetrations, the celestial beings who had recently ascended to heaven suddenly beheld the Heavenly Venerable’s victorious assembly and the site of the Dao’s practice—the foremost in purity, adorned with the merits of non-action. Overwhelmed with exultation and joy, they all prostrated themselves in reverence, marveling at what they had never before witnessed. At that moment, the transformed Jade Emperors from all ten directions merged into a single body, seated upon the Dharma throne. The pure assembly within the Dharma banquet, wishing to hear of the Jade Emperor’s original practices and realizations, dared not yet inquire.

Zhang Guo stated: When the transformed bodies of the Jade Emperor universally gathered, the celestial beings who had recently drawn near to the Emperor’s compassionate light ascended to the Great Mystery and were born in the Clear and Subtle Heaven. Suddenly, they beheld the Jade Emperor, the Great Heavenly Venerable, in the most victorious and beneficial assembly. An assembly is where ordinary people gather to see one another. If the benefits of the gathering are limited, it cannot be called a victorious assembly. When the Primordial Beginning expounded the Jade Scripture and the Jade Emperor manifested his compassionate light, all beings across the Dharma realms universally gathered, and gods, humans, and all beings eternally received great benefit. Opening the flourishing fortune of the Three Teachings, propagating the mysterious essence of the myriad Dharmas—this was the most excellent and finest of Dharma banquets. No assembly across the kalpas could compare, its merits supreme and eternally indestructible, thus it is called a victorious assembly. Within this assembly, the Primordial Beginning praised the virtues of the Jade Emperor and transmitted the Dharma of the Most Real—the supreme vehicle—universally liberating the world to awakening, thus it is called the site of the Dao’s practice.

This victorious assembly and site of the Dao’s practice were utterly free from worldly defilement, wondrously pure and luminous—the foremost in purity. The Jade Emperor’s wondrous transformations arise naturally, universally bestowing eternal benefit through his mysterious merit, without need for contrivance. The sands of the world receive his grace, eternally bathed in his blessings. The Jade Emperor never acts with intention, nor does the Primordial Beginning act with deliberation. The myriad heavens yield their merits, all buddhas yield their virtues. Through excellent karmic affinity and wondrous assembly, merits and transformations universally manifest—truly adorned with the merits of non-action. The celestial beings, beholding this, were filled with boundless joy, truly not knowing whether to dance with their hands or leap with their feet, so exultant and overjoyed were they. The entire assembly prostrated themselves, touching their foreheads to the ground in reverence, exclaiming that never in all the kalpas had they witnessed such a wondrous, victorious assembly and site of the Dao’s practice.

At this time, the transformed Jade Emperors from all worlds merged into a single body, seated upon the great luminous Dharma throne. The pure assembly within the Dharma banquet—those called the pure assembly—had ascended by the Emperor’s light, their long-accumulated dust instantly dissolved, utterly free from defilement, thus they were called the pure assembly. The great assembly beheld the transformed bodies of the Jade Emperor manifesting in the various celestial palaces across all worlds, all bathed in radiant light.

At this moment before the Primordial Beginning’s assembly, they once more became a single body—neither did their manifold manifestations reveal any lack, nor did their unity show any excess. In an instant they divided, in an instant they merged, their divine subtlety beyond comprehension, their cause unknown. Possessing such divine penetrations, the assembly all thought as one, desiring to hear the Jade Emperor’s fundamental practices, his cultivation of truth and verification of sagehood, yet none dared presume to pose the question.

I observe: Within the human body, spirit and qi nourish and protect, meridians and vessels interpenetrate, exterior and interior mutually adhere, emptiness and numinous responsiveness intermingle, movement and stillness mutually root one another—originally one part yet manifesting as ten thousand, the ten thousand all returning to a single source. Yet when humans are constrained by qi, obscured by things, ensnared by craving and delusion, then the bright becomes dim, the numinous stagnates. Some may study the Dao to aid the world, yet with petty wisdom and private benevolence, feigning merit and virtue, their kindness and favor finite—how could this be called the Dao? If one begins well but ends poorly, acts well but achieves ill, or forces oneself to sustain partial efforts, straining to grasp a handle, then whether gathering or dispersing, though appearing spiritually efficacious, this is not the subtlety of the Dao.

If one can truly awaken and comprehend, universally illuminate and penetrate, stillness and response all settled, without the disturbance of grasping or rejecting; if the numinous operates in silent accord, without the labor of forced effort—then the mechanism of the Dao subtly abides. The human heart retreats to listen, the turbid returns to clarity, the stagnant returns to the numinous. Alone, one awakens to true attainment, joyful and at ease, freed from constraints and obscurations, wondrously renewed each day. Thus do the gods and humans of the heavens, upon beholding the Heavenly Worthy’s pure and transcendent Dao-site, its effortless merit and adornments of virtue, leap for joy and prostrate themselves, exclaiming that never before has such a thing been seen. Gathering the ten thousand into one, the Celestial Lord ascends the throne—this is the ten directions’ transformed Jade Emperors once more seated as a single body upon the Dharma throne. If the pure assembly wishes to hear the Emperor’s practices yet dares not ask, then the root cause for expounding the scripture certainly cannot be spoken as one’s own experience. Those who study the Dao must secretly comprehend this, and the wondrous principle will naturally appear.

**Chapter Sixteen: Divine Penetrations**

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the four assemblies, saying: In a past age, there was a kingdom named Radiant Severity and Wondrous Joy. Its king was named Pure Virtue. At that time, the king had a queen named Treasure Moonlight. The king had no heir. One day, he reflected thus: *I* or *We*—which should I use? The king said to himself: I must not use *Emperor*. In past kalpas, I have never presumed to call myself *We*. It is proper to use *I*. Now I grow old, yet have no crown prince. If this body should collapse and perish—*bengmo*, meaning death—then to whom shall I entrust the altars of soil and grain and the nine ancestral temples?

Having thus reflected, he immediately issued an edict, summoning all Daoist assemblies to the various palaces and halls. Following the ritual codes, they hung banners and canopies, purified and adorned the space, and abundantly arrayed offerings. Throughout the six periods of the day, they performed the Dao, circumambulating the halls and praying to the perfected sages. Half a year passed, yet the king did not waver from his initial resolve.

I observe: Human life in this body receives the principle of Heaven and Earth in its nature, the qi of Heaven and Earth in its form, and is born of father’s essence and mother’s blood. It is illumined by the light of sun and moon, sustained by the ruler’s governance and the land’s bounty, preserved by the sagely institutions, and advanced by teachers and friends of prior wisdom. With the Dao, one positions Heaven and Earth, nurtures the myriad beings, enters sagehood and transcends the mundane, unbound by birth and death. Without the Dao, all affairs shatter, one’s stench endures without cease, transgressions accumulate, and retribution continues unending. As a sage, though the body perishes, principle endures, co-eternal with the Dao—thus descendants continue the lineage, and ancestral sacrifices never cease. As a commoner, without heirs, the ancestral sacrifices are cut off. The distinction between sage and commoner is thus vast.

The threshold between commoner and sage—how vast is the distance? Should one recognize the weight of this bodily existence, knowing that birth is no mere coincidence and must not be squandered; comprehend the four debts of gratitude to be repaid and the five constants as no trifling matter; fulfill human relationships and illuminate all things; cultivate reverence through self-nurturance and advance learning through knowledge; embody steadfast solidity; and upon hearing goodness, act without fail—then, by day and night examining oneself, preserving integrity from beginning to end, feeling no shame even in the hidden recesses of one’s chamber, and sustaining utmost sincerity without pause, one’s virtue merges with Heaven and Earth, one’s clarity aligns with the sun and moon, one’s order harmonizes with the four seasons, and one’s fortune accords with ghosts and spirits. Awaiting sagehood without doubt, never slackening even for a moment, one lives in accord and dies in peace, returning to the original endowment of creation. The legacy of one’s name after death grows ever more radiant—such was the unyielding resolve of Prince Qi of the Kingdom of Guangyan in cultivating the Dao.

**Chapter Seventeen: Marvels of Spiritual Penetration**

One night, Queen Baoyueguang dreamed that the Most High Lord of the Dao, accompanied by a host of perfected transcendents, appeared with golden countenances and voices of jade-like purity. They rode a five-colored dragon chariot, surrounded by luminous banners, shaded by canopies of radiant rosy clouds. At that moment, the Most High Lord of the Dao sat serenely in the dragon chariot, cradling an infant. The child’s every pore emitted billions of rays of light, illuminating the palace halls in hues of a hundred treasures. Preceded by ritual standards and floating through the void, they arrived. Overjoyed, the queen reverently received them, prostrating before the Lord of the Dao and addressing him: "Our king has no heir. I beseech you to grant this child to rule our kingdom. I humbly pray for your compassion and mercy, that you may heed my plea." Then the Lord of the Dao replied to the queen: "I willingly bestow this child upon you." The queen bowed in gratitude, receiving the child. Upon awakening, she found herself with child. After a year’s gestation, on the ninth day of the first month in the *bingwu* year, at the hour of noon, she gave birth in the royal palace.

The August Emperor of Vast Life declared: Prince Qi of the Kingdom of Guangyan never wavered in his resolve. In a single night, Queen Baoyueguang dreamed that the Most High Numinous Treasure Lord of the Great Dao, accompanied by a company of perfected saints, appeared with golden radiance and jade-like purity, their assembly suffused with immaculate divine light. They rode a five-colored dragon chariot, surrounded by resplendent banners, shaded by canopies of luminous rosy clouds. The Most High Lord of the Great Dao sat calmly in the chariot, holding a divine infant. From every pore of the child’s body emanated billions of auspicious rays, illuminating the palace halls in a spectacle of a hundred treasures. Ritual standards led the way as they floated through the void. Seeing the Lord of the Dao cradling the child, the queen rejoiced, receiving them with reverence and prostrating before him. She addressed the Lord of the Dao: "Our king has no heir. I beseech you to grant this sacred child to rule our kingdom. I humbly pray for your great compassion, that you may take pity on our king’s lack of an heir and grant my request." The Lord of the Dao replied: "I willingly bestow this child upon you." The queen bowed in gratitude and received the child. Upon awakening, she found herself with child. After a year’s gestation, on the ninth day of the first month in the *bingwu* year, at the hour of noon, the Jade Emperor was born in the palace of the Kingdom of Guangyan.

I humbly observe: In human birth, with form and substance, there comes the responsibility of human relationships and the mandate of life. The body bears the weight of the fundamental principles, and life carries the duty of dual cultivation. Vast, luminous, spiritually penetrating, and free—this body is no mere vessel, nor is life a trivial matter. It is originally of golden essence and jade-like purity, unstained and immaculate. Yet through ignorance and delusion, one may slight the celestial treasure, failing to unite with the wondrous and divine, to conceive the mysterious and numinous. Thus, one squanders the most precious gift of one’s household, rendering this body useless. Even if one possesses some self-regard, without clarity in the Dao and genuine effort, one may feign goodness while harboring evil—golden without, yet rotten within. Such a person cannot even preserve their own being, let alone manifest the celestial nobility and inherent excellence. How then can one fulfill one’s form and perfect one’s nature, ensuring that one’s true master does not decline?

If one awakens to the profound root of life and death, grasps the secret essentials of Heaven and humanity, thoroughly understands yin and yang, and deeply comprehends the workings of creation; if one recognizes one’s ancestral lineage, knows one’s parents, sees that one’s birth arises from the earth and one’s origin from Heaven; if one fuses the golden elixir, refines the pure jade, attains the wondrous in the indistinct, and unites with the mysterious in the obscure; if one’s spirit of emptiness and non-being nurtures the true reality of wondrous being, forming the sacred embryo and giving birth to the divine child—then those who gave me life do not do so in vain, and those who nurture me do not do so idly. With sinews of gold and bones of jade, one transcends form and spirit, reviving what was withered and flourishing eternally—just as Queen Baoyueguang dreamed of the Most High Lord of the Dao and the company of perfected transcendents, who bestowed the sacred child upon her to rule the kingdom.

A single person—awakened, one becomes an immortal; unawakened, one perishes. To understand the meaning of Queen Baoyueguang’s prayer for a child is to awaken to the Dao.

**Chapter Eighteen: Marvels of Spiritual Penetration**

At the moment of his birth, his body radiated a brilliant light that filled the kingdom. His countenance was wondrously fine, and all who beheld him were never sated. As a child, he was keen and wise; as he grew, he was kind and benevolent. Throughout his kingdom, he distributed all the treasures from the royal storehouses to the poor, the destitute, the widowed, the orphaned, the childless, the solitary, the starving, the infirm, and all suffering beings.

The prince was benevolent, kind, and yielding; his governance was guided by the Dao, and his songs and odes spread far. The distant lands were transformed by his virtue, and all under heaven looked up to him in admiration, turning to the Benevolent Prince. His father, the king, rejoiced even more.

The Supreme Primordial Sovereign said: When the Jade Emperor descended to be born, his body radiated a hundred treasures’ brilliance, filling the entire Kingdom of Resplendent Light. His countenance and form were wondrously fine, and all who beheld him never grew weary. In his tender youth, he was keen and wise; as he matured, he was compassionate and virtuous. From all the storehouses and treasuries of his kingdom, he distributed every treasure and possession without restraint, as if scattering them all without hesitation or regret. Yet one might ask: if he were to give away all wealth, would he not forsake his sovereign, his parents, and his kingdom? The Jade Emperor, born with innate wisdom and perfect conduct, would never commit such excess. Let the reader consider this carefully.

The emperor’s distribution of the treasuries was not to perpetuate wealth and nobility but to aid those without means—the destitute and impoverished, the helpless and distressed, the widowed without husbands, the widows without wives, the fatherless orphans, the childless and solitary, those without mothers or any support, those without fathers or anyone to rely upon; those suffering in years of famine when grain did not ripen, or in times of hardship when even vegetables failed; those afflicted by illness, frailty, injury, or disability—all such suffering beings received the Jade Emperor’s relief and benevolent aid. His kindness arose from utmost sincerity, not mere outward display. His benevolence and compassion, warmth and humility, spread across the land, and all who benefited from his virtue sang his praises in odes and ballads, extolling his Dao. From the royal domains to the distant frontiers, his transformative influence reached the farthest corners. All under heaven gazed upon him in reverence and followed his example, turning to the Benevolent Prince. To "turn" is to align with him, as the *Analects* says: "For one day to master oneself and return to ritual propriety, all under heaven will turn to benevolence." Seeking the Dao brings swift and great attainment. The Jade Emperor, born with divine marvels and growing in compassion, how could the world not turn to him in devotion?

Thus, as his virtue became manifest, the four quarters rejoiced and submitted. Even in his youth as prince, the signs of sagely and enlightened governance were already evident. Therefore, his father the king not only rejoiced at his birth but, seeing the prince’s Dao today, felt even greater joy and celebration.

I humbly observe: When one is born between heaven and earth, possessing this body, one possesses the true vital qi of life. Only with this true vital qi can one be human. This true qi, when in heaven and earth, is the wondrous principle; when in the human body, it is the vast and unyielding. The true qi is mysterious and numinous, luminous and free, illuminating past and present, pervading the dharma realm. Endowed with this principle, one inherently knows no hardship, suffering, peril, or aversion. Yet when it descends from heaven, it is cast aside by humanity. The true nature of inheriting goodness and perfecting one’s character is treated as a trivial, non-urgent matter. Unable to fully embody the correct principle to nurture the true numen or cultivate the wondrous mechanism to achieve spiritual transformation, one remains obscured and unenlightened, given to anger, jealousy, and immorality; greedy for profit and fame, endlessly hoarding; unmoved by virtue, indifferent to the poor and suffering; arrogant and self-righteous, inviting slander and defamation. Such conduct harms the true qi, weakens the vast and unyielding, and casts oneself into the realm of the ordinary and foolish, unable to enter sagehood.

If one preserves the Great Harmony, congealing and merging the secret intent, the sacred embryo reveals its treasure light, and the divine infant emits wondrous radiance. Gradually unfolding the mysterious spirit, one achieves effortless spiritual transformation, viewing the mire of power and profit, the dust of honor and glory, as mere illusions. With one’s abundance, one aids others’ lack, relieving people and benefiting beings, extending kindness to all. Though the kalpas rise and fall, one’s merit and virtue remain inexhaustible. One’s盛德 and spiritual transformation become eternally renowned as an immortal, and the boundless kalpas of the dharma realm are all embraced by one’s compassion. Heavenly spirits and humans rejoice, revering and submitting to one’s supreme virtue. Such a one is the heaven-and-earth’s filial child, a rare being in the world, bringing glory and joy to parents. This is the divine marvel of the Jade Emperor’s birth and growth—his compassion and benevolence leading all under heaven to turn to benevolence, and his father the king to rejoice even more.

**Chapter Nineteen: Marvels of Spiritual Penetration**

After this, the king suddenly passed away. The prince, now governing, reflected upon the fleeting nature of life and instructed his ministers to ensure a virtuous succession. He then relinquished his kingdom and retired to the Fragrant and Resplendent Mountain to cultivate the Dao, where he perfected his practice and transcended the mundane.

The Dipper Mother said: After the Benevolent Prince of the Kingdom of Wondrous Joy had won the hearts of all under heaven, the king suddenly passed away. The prince ascended the throne, governing the kingdom’s affairs, and reflected upon the fleeting nature of life. To "reflect" is to look down upon one’s own existence and contemplate it. "Fleeting life" refers to human existence in the world, like floating clouds in the sky or duckweed upon the water, impermanent and uncertain—hence "fleeting." The emperor, pondering this, issued decrees to his kingdom’s ministers and officials, entrusting the great treasure of rulership to a worthy successor, ensuring the virtuous continuation of the royal line. Another interpretation suggests he instructed the ministers to inherit the throne and practice virtue, which also makes sense. Having entrusted the throne to a worthy person, he abandoned his kingdom and secluded himself on Fragrant and Resplendent Mountain to cultivate the Great Dao. According to ancient records, Fragrant and Resplendent Mountain is the Stone Mountain in the Eastern Sea. Other mountains where the Jade Emperor left traces of his teachings are not the original site of Fragrant and Resplendent Mountain. After entering the mountain to cultivate the Dao, he completed his practice, transcended the mortal world, and ascended to the heavens to deliver beings.

I humbly observe: Human life in this world is like a white colt passing a gap, like thunder and lightning in the void—suddenly appearing, suddenly vanishing, unable to preserve itself. Even one who is honored as the Son of Heaven, possessing all within the four seas, clad in dragon robes and feasting on delicacies from every land, upon death, all becomes an empty dream. Those of lesser rank, even the highest ministers with fields stretching across a thousand *li*, are not worth mentioning.

Moreover, wealth and nobility are rarely shared with kin, while poverty and hardship are common. Yet people remain drunk in life, dreaming in death, deeply deluded and unenlightened. Thus, those who practice the Dao are seldom heard of—how much rarer still are those who become immortals! If one could awaken to the truth that the body is but a temporary lodging, life as fleeting as the mayfly, and suddenly break free from the dusty snares of the world, earnestly seeking the profound mystery, clearly perceiving and steadfastly practicing, without craving swift results, then when the time is ripe, transformation will naturally occur, and one will achieve the rank of immortal. Though one’s ancestors may have passed, they too are preserved by the sacred descendant’s arrival in Luoyang—thus, they do not perish. Was it not Prince Miaole, who relinquished his father’s throne to cultivate the Dao, achieving perfection and transcending the mortal realm?

Alas! Within the human body lies Kunlun Mountain. When old yang is exhausted, a single yang is reborn. Detached from all extremes, one secretly cultivates the utmost truth, and over time, ascends through immortal transformation. The rarity of such an aspiration mirrors the Emperor’s own path—ponder this deeply.

**Chapter Twenty of the Divine Powers:**
After passing through this kalpa, spanning eight hundred kalpas, he frequently relinquished his kingdom for the sake of all beings, severing love to study the Dao. Thereafter, through another eight hundred kalpas, he practiced medicine to heal the sick, rescuing and delivering sentient beings, granting them peace and joy. When this kalpa ended, he passed through yet another eight hundred kalpas, widely performing expedient means, unlocking the treasures of the Daoist canon, expounding sacred scriptures, magnifying the true teachings, proclaiming divine works, aiding the nation and saving the people—from the hidden to the manifest.

After this, through another eight hundred kalpas, he sacrificed his body and life, practicing forbearance and relinquishing his own flesh and blood. Through such cultivation over three thousand two hundred kalpas, he first attained the rank of Golden Immortal, known as the Tathāgata of Pure and Natural Enlightenment, teaching bodhisattvas to suddenly awaken to the true essence of the Great Vehicle and gradually enter the wondrous Dao of emptiness.

Through such cultivation, after another hundred million kalpas, he finally attained the position of Jade Emperor. When these words were spoken, the assembly of pure disciples unanimously exclaimed in wonder, declaring they had never before witnessed such sacred and wondrous conduct.

Master Xu Zhenjun said: After the Jade Emperor first relinquished his royal throne to cultivate the Dao, passing through these kalpas, he endured eight hundred kalpas as a crown prince. Each time he abandoned his kingdom, it was to deliver all beings—severing the bonds of the six relations to study the true Dao. Kalpas vary in duration: sixty years form a "dust kalpa," five hundred years a "cycle of flourishing destiny," three thousand years a "leap kalpa"; eighteen thousand eighty years a "lesser kalpa," one hundred twenty-nine thousand six hundred years a "wheel-turning kalpa." Countless kalpas accumulate to form a great kalpa. Here, "eight hundred kalpas" is not confined to size but signifies vast duration—roughly eight hundred kalpas in all.

During this time of severing love to study the Dao, after many kalpas, he endured another eight hundred kalpas, administering medicines to treat illnesses, rescuing and aiding suffering beings, granting them health and happiness. When this kalpa ended, he passed through another eight hundred kalpas, widely performing great expedient means, unlocking the scriptures of the Daoist canon, expounding the mysterious and numinous chapters, expanding and magnifying the great orthodox teachings, proclaiming and propagating divine scriptures, assisting the nation and delivering the people—from the hidden to the manifest, from darkness to light, extending blessings throughout heaven, earth, and the human realm.

After these kalpas, he endured another eight hundred kalpas, unafraid to sacrifice his body, unconcerned for his life, practicing forbearance and enduring humiliation without resentment. He joyfully relinquished his own flesh and blood—just as one who gives away wealth feels as though parting with their own flesh. In a past kalpa, the Jade Emperor practiced forbearance and relinquishment, giving away his family’s wealth until reduced to poverty and peril. Though insults assailed him and others could not bear the suffering, he remained unmoved, never wavering or regretting. This was truly sacrificing his body and life, practicing forbearance, and relinquishing his flesh and blood.

The sage endures what others find unbearable to achieve what others cannot. The Emperor’s attainment of supreme sageliness required such sacrifices. Yet, as a sage transforming and delivering the foolish, he could manifest in any form, his true body never truly destroyed. Those who comprehend this spiritually should not cling to the literal words—then they will grasp the truth.

From the eight hundred kalpas of severing love to study the Dao, through healing the sick, expounding scriptures to deliver beings, and practicing forbearance and relinquishment—such wondrous and arduous cultivation over three thousand two hundred kalpas finally allowed him to attain the rank of Golden Immortal, achieving the indestructible fruit, known as the Tathāgata of Pure, Natural, and Wondrous Enlightenment, the Dharma King. He taught bodhisattvas and great beings to suddenly awaken to the true essence of the Great Vehicle and gradually enter the profound, empty, and wondrous Dao.

The term *Tathāgata* signifies that all beings possess inherent nature, replete with myriad virtues. Its coming is equal to that of immortals and buddhas, fundamentally vast and luminous. Those who recklessly abandon it fail to preserve the endowment of heaven, obscuring their original true suchness to the utmost, thus falling into mundane karma. After the Jade Emperor relinquished the throne of Prince Miaole, he endured another three thousand two hundred kalpas, his merit and transformation boundless, never regressing, unattached and unpolluted. As the Dharma King of Great Awakening, he encompassed heaven and earth, perfectly nurturing all beings without excess or omission. Those who fully embody and return to this truth transcend all others—this is the meaning of *Tathāgata*.

Through such great cultivation over a hundred thousand kalpas, he finally attained the position of Jade Emperor, Lord of the Ten Thousand Heavens. When the Celestial Venerable of Original Beginning had finished speaking, the pure assembly unanimously exclaimed in wonder, declaring they had never before witnessed such sacred and wondrous conduct.

I humbly observe: Human life embodies yin and yang, thoughts encompass principle and desire. Yin and yang are mutually rooted, alternately waxing and waning; principle and desire cannot coexist in dominance. When desire stirs, yin congeals; when principle prevails, yang flourishes. Flourishing to the point of transformation, one wondrously enters the divine.

Only what is enacted proves ever fitting; nothing applied is ever amiss. The primordial purity of yang is the highest good—yet how few the indolent who can sustain it.

Moved by this, the Jade Emperor expounded the wondrous meaning in full: relinquishing not one but countless royal thrones, he endured eight hundred kalpas to renounce his kingdom for all beings, severing bonds of love to study the Great Dao—this is the boundless pinnacle of sublime conduct. Moreover, the original spirit governs the numinous terrace, commands the five senses, and directs the hundred ministries. Among the six desires and seven emotions, love is the weightiest. To exhaust desire and restore principle, to gather emotions and return to nature, to strip away all embellishments and unite with the profound mystery—this is the Heavenly Lord’s abandonment of rank to study the Dao.

Refining the elixir to save lives, he granted them peace and joy—thus the Jade Emperor endured another eight hundred kalpas to deliver the world. Mortals, deluded by toil and illusion, carve away their true intent, content to age and die without awakening—this is the world’s gravest affliction. Yet by congealing the three treasures of original spirit, essence, and qi into a secret, numinous fusion, reversing yang to transform the bones, one lives without delusion and dies without perishing—this is the inner vision of refining the elixir to save lives.

Expounding scriptures to aid the nation, benefiting both the hidden and the manifest, the Emperor endured yet another eight hundred kalpas. Mortals who comprehend the profound and penetrate the secret, wondrously transmuting yin and yang, ascend as immortals to succor spirits and beings—this embodies the silent transmission of true scriptures to benefit both the unseen and the seen. Sacrificing life and body, forsaking flesh and blood, the Emperor endured another eight hundred kalpas. Mortals whose hearts remain unmoved, who relinquish their impure forms—this too embodies the resolve to endure humiliation and surrender flesh and blood.

From kalpa to kalpa, his reverent cultivation never wavered, pure and unstained, wondrously transforming by nature. Enabling all to awaken, his merit knows no bounds—just as the Jade Emperor, from over three thousand kalpas to a hundred million kalpas, has never ceased such unparalleled wonder.

**Chapter Twenty-One: Divine Powers**

At that moment, among the assembly stood a Jade Maiden named Night Radiance. Rising from her seat, she adjusted her robes and crown with solemn grace, stepped forward with measured elegance, and knelt long before the Dao. She addressed the Celestial Venerable:

“By what past merit, O Ancient One, did I once gain the fortune to attend in Your presence, personally offering reverent service for a hundred million kalpas? In the Three Clarities’ realm, the Golden Gates and Jade Capital, serene and untroubled, I roam carefree in bliss, wandering the sacred precincts, feasting on the sounds of the Dao, savoring their ineffable flavor. Yet never have I witnessed such a rare and wondrous event.”

*As Master Guiguzi said:* When the pure assembly praised the Jade Emperor, among those in attendance stood a Jade Maiden named Night Radiance. Rising from her seat, she straightened her robes and crown—though already immaculate while seated, her dignity only deepened upon standing. With measured, graceful steps, she knelt long before the Dao Ancestor and addressed the Celestial Venerable of Original Beginning: “By what past cause, O Lord, did I, Night Radiance, merit the fortune to gaze upon and attend You in the presence of the Heavenly Emperor? Some suppose Night Radiance refers to one in the Three Clarities’ realm, or inquires about the Jade Emperor’s divine radiance—this is mistaken. The Heavenly Emperor often attends the Three Clarities’ realm; when scriptures are expounded, the Jade Emperor’s great light is not always visible. Thus the Jade Maiden speaks thus, leaving no doubt she is the Heavenly Emperor’s attendant.

Not once but countless times have I served in Your presence, personally offering reverent service for a hundred million kalpas. In the Three Clarities’ mysterious realm, the Golden Gates and Jade Capital, utterly serene and untroubled, I wander carefree in boundless joy, delighting in the sacred precincts, nourishing myself on the sounds of the supreme Dao. As for ‘feasting,’ the sacred tones of the Clear and Subtle Heavenly Perfected contain the highest, most wondrous principles, their flavor inexhaustible and not easily discerned. Though a divine being, I am but newly among the sacred ranks—how could I fully comprehend? Thus I listen to the Dharma’s sounds and savor them deeply, as one savors fine food. This refers to my past experience, not today’s hearing of the Celestial Venerable’s words. To interpret it as today’s hearing would miss the text’s original intent.

Night Radiance has long dwelled in the sacred realm, serving in the Emperor’s presence in boundless joy. Hearing the Dharma’s sounds, she witnesses all wonders, comprehending them all, just as the Jade Emperor universally radiates his compassionate light, manifesting and gathering at will, creating and transforming with auspicious marvels. Through kalpas of cultivation, his merit is immeasurable, teaching and perfecting the sacred ranks, awakening them to the highest truth. Surveying the kalpas, gazing into the distant past, never have I witnessed such a rare and unparalleled event.

*Humbly observed:* The yin within the human body is the immortal maiden. Jade-like bones, icy purity, radiant bearing, and refined demeanor—these are her innate qualities. Yet sullied by worldly dust and defilement, long obscured by grime, the true yin of Brahmanic qi sinks into impure thoughts and evil deeds; the six ding spirits of yin invert into hungry ghosts of impermanence. Endless thoughts churn ceaselessly, day and night restless, eating and sleeping without constancy. Flustered in movement, unable to attend the Supreme Emperor or serve the Mysterious Origin. Indulging in frivolity, craving splendor and finery, bound by fame and profit, burdened by worldly toil, she knows no carefree joy, rising and falling in the wheel of rebirth, endlessly descending into the mortal world. Unaware of the Dao’s wondrous Dharma, she daily indulges in passions and desires, stirred by demonic hordes, obstructed from wondrous transformations, making such encounters rare indeed.

Yet when the pure yang secretly transmutes, hatching the yin essence; when the luminous moon reveals its wondrous radiance without end, and the jade-like form displays its divine transformations without exhaustion; when all within the body becomes utterly numinous, the mechanism of transformation moves with ease, its wondrous mysteries revealed in crystalline clarity—then, in stillness, she pays homage to the Celestial Venerable and silently attends the Heavenly Emperor. Her nature and Dao remain ever luminous, and the human heart obeys her command.”

Within the realm of the Cinnabar Terrace and the Purple Palace, amid palaces of seven treasures and five luminances, all is serene, empty, and radiant—spacious, carefree, and blissful. The spirit roams the mysterious realm, the ears savor the sound of jade-like resonance. This is a rare spectacle of the world, a supreme event never before witnessed.

Then the Moonlight Jade Maiden rose from her seat, adjusted her robes and headdress, and with graceful steps knelt before the Dao. She addressed the Heavenly Venerable, inquired about past causes, and entreated him to clarify the wondrous and rare transformations of the Jade Emperor.

Now, the principles of yin and yang and the regulation of qi are common to all people. Those who attain the Dao employ the yin mechanism to manifest the divine powers of the Jade Maiden; those who do not revert to karmic destinies. Thus, the matter of cultivating the true cannot but be made clear.

**Chapter Twenty-Two on Divine Powers**

Yet I do not understand: in the radiant light seen earlier, the ten directions of all heavens manifested sacred realms, wherein the responsive and transformative Dharma-bodies of the Jade Emperor appeared, attended by Heavenly Perfected Great Sages, Wondrous Practice Perfected Ones, and Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens. These Jade Maidens possessed dignified and majestic countenances, exquisitely beautiful forms, and emitted wondrous fragrances unmatched by any. By the Jade Emperor’s divine power of wondrous translocation, they have now all gathered in the Heaven of Pure Tenuity.

I do not know by what karmic conditions this Jade Maiden has attained such a supreme physical form. I humbly beseech the sagely compassion to reveal what I have yet to comprehend.

The Lord of Southern Florescence said: The Moonlight Jade Maiden herself has declared that though she has long dwelled in the heavens and listened to profound discourses, she has never before witnessed the Jade Emperor’s wondrous transformations. Yet today, she speaks of the great radiant light that manifested the ten directions of all heavens, revealing sacred and true realms. (The character *bian* may also be read as *traverse*, and the meaning remains coherent.) Within these realms, the responsive and transformative Dharma-bodies of the Jade Emperor appeared, attended by the divine and immortal Perfected Great Sages of all heavens, Wondrous Practice Perfected Ones, and Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens as guardians and protectors.

These Jade Maidens possess dignified and majestic countenances, exquisitely beautiful and wondrous forms, and emit divine and marvelous fragrances unmatched by any. By the Jade Emperor’s great divine power of wondrous translocation and compassionate reception, all the attendants followed the Emperor’s light and have now universally gathered in the Heaven of Pure Tenuity.

I do not know by what wondrous causes and excellent conditions these attendant Jade Maidens have attained such a supreme physical form. A *supreme physical form* refers to the wondrously transformed body of the Jade Maiden, which surpasses all and admits no comparison.

Now, the world comprises six destinies: the three evil destinies of hell, hungry ghosts, and animals, which possess no beauty. The human body is but an aggregation of essence and blood; when qi scatters and spirit departs, its filth is indescribable. Moreover, in life, there is decline, old age, sickness, and suffering—thus, all beauty is but a dream’s illusion. Therefore, the body is called *illusory* and cannot be termed a *supreme physical form*. Beyond this, in the demonic destiny, all demonic maidens, though possessing extraordinary beauty, the five supernatural powers, and the ability to transform, ultimately bring calamity upon themselves when their karmic retribution matures. How then can they be called *supreme physical forms*?

Only these Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens possess peerless countenances and surpassing demeanor, transcending the Three Realms. Their celestial fragrance and wondrous transformations neither decline nor remain ordinary—such sights are unattainable in the mortal world. This is the *supreme physical form*, the nature of which even the Moonlight Jade Maiden cannot fathom.

I humbly beseech the utmost sagely compassion to reveal the meaning of what I have yet to comprehend, that the Moonlight Jade Maiden may understand the principles behind the dignified beauty, wondrous fragrance, and exquisite forms of the Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens.

In my humble opinion: the blessings and karma of the world are all created by the mind. The mind governs nature and emotions; nature encompasses all. The wondrous transformations of yin and yang are inherently possessed by all. Without cultivating the Dao, one remains with yin as a dark destiny, a rotting corpse, the root of karmic rebirth. Through awakening to the Dao and cultivating the true, yin becomes the body’s upright qi, the Six Dings manifest wondrously, and celestial radiance shines in stillness. The true fragrance of the Jade Maiden is the marvelous function of the body.

With the entire body pervaded by mysterious communion, the Cinnabar Terrace and Jade Towers, the six yang secret realms, and the true king’s timely dominion—this Dharma-body broadly transforms, subjugating tigers and commanding dragons. Refining jade liquid within the Mysterious Palace, arraying the Azure Maidens to the right; gathering the secret treasures of the cinnabar spirit, floating the pure fragrance of the imperial consorts. This too is the manifestation of the Emperor’s light across the ten directions of heavenly realms, where the responsive and transformative Dharma-bodies of the Jade Emperor appear, attended by Perfected Jade Maidens, translocated by divine power to dwell in the Heaven of Pure Tenuity.

Every person possesses nature, encompasses yin and yang, and contains all wondrous potentials—body and heaven are one. The divine powers and wondrous models of the Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens should be known to all who hear and see them. How is it that the Moonlight Jade Maiden, having attained sagehood and become an attendant of the Emperor, has yet to comprehend this?

Now, cultivation and realization have ranks of nobility and humility, and the sagely body arises from the transformations of the Dao’s source. The fruit attained determines the rank of divine powers—only sages know sages, only the worthy know the worthy, with no room for pretense. The Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens, through their celestial perfection, transform and save beings; thus, their luminous demeanor, wondrous countenance, and true fragrance are rightfully unknown to the Moonlight Jade Maiden. Her lack of knowledge stems from her recent attainment of the sagely body and differing rank, not from evasion or falsehood.

Alas! If even the Divine Consorts and Jade Maidens are not easily known, how then can the divine transformations of the Emperor’s light be fathomed? If the Moonlight Jade Maiden cannot know them, how can others? Sage and mortal share one nature; humans stand shoulder to shoulder with the Jade Emperor. Yet if even knowledge is unattainable, how can one attain sagehood? Let all ponder this and strive.

**Chapter Twenty-Three on Divine Powers**

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable addressed the Moonlight Jade Maiden, saying: You have only recently entered the sagely stream. Though you possess wisdom, you have yet to attain full clarity. These Jade Maidens, from immeasurable kalpas past, have cultivated wondrous practices, attained the gates of liberation, and shared in pure faith, pure understanding, pure mindfulness, pure conduct, pure bodies, pure minds, pure intentions, pure fruits, and pure retributions. They share in great compassion and great mercy, sheltering and protecting sentient beings as a mother cherishes and loves her infant child.

Upholding the precepts with single-minded devotion, they inwardly align with the Great Dao, observe pure fasts, and uphold vast vows. Through myriad kalpas, they have revered the Jade Emperor with utmost devotion.

The Sovereign of Primordial Emptiness declared: When you, Moonlight, first beseeched the sagely compassion to dispel your unenlightened state, the Primordial Heavenly Venerable addressed you, saying: You have only recently entered the sagely stream. *You*—that is, *you*. *Sagely stream* means to stand in the same rank and company as the sages, forming one category with them. Having become a sage, one should know all things. Yet, having only newly entered the sagely stream, though possessing keen wisdom and intelligence, you have not yet attained full clarity and thorough understanding.

These Jade Maidens who attend and guard the Jade Emperor did not acquire their divine powers in a single day. Rather, from immeasurable kalpas past, they have cultivated manifold wondrous practices, fully attained the gates of great awakening and liberation, passed through kalpas unstained, and never retreated from the mind of true faith. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in pure faith, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure faith.

Unattached to form and appearance, they have attained great liberation. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in pure understanding, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure understanding.

With true mindfulness of the unborn, they have transcended all destinies. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in pure mindfulness, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure mindfulness.

Their wondrous practices adorn them, forever free from transgression or disturbance. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in pure conduct, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure conduct.

The Dao embodies the physical form, unstained by defilement or impurity. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in a pure body, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure body.

Mind is the Dao, and the Dao is mind—lucid and unattached. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in a pure mind, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure mind.

Without inside or outside, without approach or reception, they have severed intentions and forgotten scheming. The Jade Emperor’s long cultivation has always been in a pure intention, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure intention.

Abiding in the Upper Clarity, they never regress. The Jade Emperor, having attained sagehood, has realized the pure fruit, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure fruit.

Through vast kalpas, their merit is exalted beyond measure. The Jade Emperor, as the Most High, has received the pure retribution, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices in past kalpas are likewise in this pure retribution.

Their benevolence pervades the dust-mote realms, and their kindness extends through boundless kalpas. The Jade Emperor possesses great compassion, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices are likewise in this great compassion.

All myriad beings receive their tender care and pity. The Jade Emperor possesses great mercy, and the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices are likewise in this great mercy.

The Jade Maidens’ great compassion and mercy are one with the Jade Emperor’s. But how is this so? They shelter and protect sentient beings as a loving mother cherishes and tenderly cares for her infant child with a heart of redoubled affection. Moreover, they uphold the mysterious precepts with unwavering sincerity and single-minded devotion. Some say: reverently upholding the mind and strictly observing the precepts, they concentrate with utter purity and unity, thus inwardly and sincerely returning to the Great Dao. The meaning is even more profound.

The Jade Maidens’ return to the Great Dao is not momentary. With pure and solemn devotion, they uphold vast vows, and through myriad kalpas, they have always revered and honored the Jade Emperor.

This foolish one observes: Those who possess the mind of true faith will naturally attain understanding and awakening, sever deluded thoughts, purify their conduct, keep their bodies unstained, their minds clear, and their intentions pure. They will realize the fruit and receive retribution, ultimately attaining the utmost truth. Those who embody great compassion and mercy, strictly uphold wondrous precepts, and reverently serve the Supreme Emperor without wavering through the ages may ascend to the rank of Upper Immortals.

Yet worldly people, deluded by heterodox views, harbor杂念 and perverse conduct. They fail to cultivate their bodies, their minds are disturbed, and their intentions are chaotic. Their karmic retributions entangle them, all because they lack compassion and do not believe in the Dao. Thus, though Moonlight has newly entered the sagely stream, she still cannot fully comprehend the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices. To walk the same path as they do is even more difficult.

The Dao is inherent in all people. If one reflects upon and cultivates it well, the Jade Maidens’ wondrous practices may be realized within oneself.

**Chapter Twenty-Four on Divine Powers**

These Jade Maidens are not truly women; they are celestial perfected beings who, to deliver sentient beings, manifest as Jade Maidens. Therefore, their bodily forms, divine powers, wisdom, and transformations—whether hidden or revealed—are equal to the Emperor’s.

At that time, upon hearing these words, Moonlight attained awakening. She bowed her head in reverence, rejoiced, and silently returned to her place.

Master Guan Yin said: These Jade Maidens who attend the Jade Emperor, having cultivated manifold wondrous practices through immeasurable kalpas past, are not truly female in form. They are celestial immortals and perfected beings who, to transform and guide sentient beings of the Dharma realms into the Dao, manifest as Jade Maidens. Precisely because they are the transformed bodies of perfected beings—whose original forms are not female—their bodily appearance, divine powers, wisdom, and transformations, whether hidden or revealed, are not superficial but equal to the Jade Emperor’s.

All people possess bodies, yet the illusory nature of the physical form cannot divide or transform. Thus, it is difficult to share the same body as the Jade Emperor. As for the shape-shifting demons and ghosts, their bodies are deceptive and illusory, and thus not worth mentioning.

Among the celestial beings above, some may extend five *li*, or several *li*, or one or two *yojanas*, or hundreds of millions of *zhang*. Some reside in heavenly palaces, some perceive the true realm, and some appear among humans. Yet when they manifest in one place, they cannot transform elsewhere. Or, though perceptible to the senses, they cannot skillfully deliver beings, bound as they are to one location or one moment. None of these are the most supreme, wondrous Dharma bodies of transformation.

The transformed bodies of the Jade Maidens appear throughout all worlds, gathering and dispersing at will, surpassing all others. Their bodies are equal to the Jade Emperor’s. All bodies are composed of form, yet if form is not wondrously refined—or if it is beautiful but not enduring—it is not equal to the Emperor’s form. The transformed bodies of the Jade Maidens possess wondrous beauty, majestic and exquisite, fully manifesting wherever they appear, never changing or declining. Their form is equal to the Emperor’s.

The paths of heavenly beings, demons, and humans all possess spiritual penetrations, yet their transformations are limited, their powers not encompassing the six penetrations—such spiritual penetrations are not equal to the Emperor’s. The Jade Maidens’ divine transformations are boundless, fully possessing the six penetrations; thus, their spiritual penetrations are equal to the Emperor’s.

Divine beings all possess wisdom, yet it is obstructed, not fully illuminated, or relies on borrowed perception, unable to achieve wondrous convergence—such wisdom is not equal to the Emperor’s. The Jade Maidens perceive all without omission, their foresight unobstructed; thus, their wisdom is equal to the Emperor’s.

Those who know spiritual penetrations may all conceal themselves, yet concealment leaves traces—this is not equal to the Emperor’s. When the Jade Maidens disperse, they return to the Great Void, not merely containing Mount Sumeru within a mustard seed; their wondrous concealment leaves no trace, their concealment equal to the Emperor’s.

Where there is concealment, there is manifestation, yet manifestation is not the great radiance—this is not equal to the Emperor’s. The Jade Maidens wondrously manifest in the pure and subtle, their divine perception spanning all realms; thus, their manifestation is equal to the Emperor’s.

Possessing spiritual penetrations, wisdom, concealment, and manifestation enables transformation. Yet if transformation is contrived, it is not equal to the Emperor’s. The Jade Maidens’ wondrous transformations arise without intention, their divine transformations spontaneous; thus, their transformations are equal to the Emperor’s.

At that moment, Yeguang, having heard the Primordial Beginning’s discourse on the Jade Maidens’ manifestations and transformations, attained clarity and awakening in his heart. He understood the wondrous causes of the Jade Maidens’ transformations, bowed in reverence, and rejoiced with delight. Silently, he forgot speech and returned to his original position.

A foolish note: The yin and yang of the human body are not two distinctly separate entities but arise from one, becoming two—yin nurtures yang, and yang generates yin, rooted in the utmost origin. Cultivating truth to attain the Dao, the six yin spirits transform and manifest as Jade Maidens, wondrously changing. This marvelous mechanism shares the same function as the primordial spirit and mysterious numen. This yin transformation revealing numinosity is not unique to the earthly quality; it extends to the heavenly body’s nurturing, the transformation of yang’s radiance and Brahman qi. Moreover, the divine immortals of heaven transform without fixed form, teaching and delivering beings according to expedient means. When a male form is needed, they manifest as male; when a female form is required, they transform into female. Through countless kalpas, worlds abound in multiplicity. Those who ought to be delivered by a female form are beyond measure. Thus, the supreme divine immortals of heaven transform into Jade Maidens to deliver multitudes. Their bodily form, spiritual penetrations, wisdom, concealment, manifestation, and transformations surpass all divine beings and are equal to the Jade Emperor’s. Though Yeguang had visited the Three Pure Realms and long heard the Dharma’s sound, he had only recently entered the sacred stream. Such great spiritual penetrations and supreme, wondrous practices were naturally unknown to him. Nevertheless, the sacred and the profane share the same nature, and the Dharma body is universal. With a heart for universal salvation and emulation of the utmost truth, the Jade Maidens’ divine wondrousness equal to the Emperor’s resides within our own bodies. Thus, Yeguang, upon hearing this discourse, attained understanding and rejoiced. Those who comprehend should reflect deeply.

*Commentary on the August Scripture, Volume Three Concluded*
*Commentary on the August Scripture, Volume Four*
*Collated by the Fiftieth-Generation Celestial Master of the Han Succession, the Great Perfected Zhang Guoxiang*
*Reviewed by the Recluse Beyond the Imperial Examinations, Luo Hongxian of Jishui, Jiangxi*
*Compiled by Zhou Xuanchen of Xiaozhao, Jinan, Shandong*
*Chapter on Spiritual Penetrations, Twenty-Five*

At that time, the Lord of the High Void and Pure Brightness Heaven, together with his celestial retinue, rode the eight-scene simurgh chariot, beneath nine-rayed jeweled canopies. They performed the Mysterious Song and wondrous music, chanted the boundless Cavern Chapters, scattered celestial treasure flowers, and sprayed celestial perfected incense. Ascending in flight, they traversed the void and arrived before the Dao.

By the awe-inspiring power and virtue of the Heavenly Worthy and Jade Emperor, these myriad treasure flowers instantly transformed in midair into a single jeweled canopy, shading and covering the great assembly without exception.

The Master Red Pine said: When Yeguang Jade Maiden returned to her position, the Lord of the High Void and Pure Brightness Heaven, along with the celestial kin of his own heaven—or, as some mistakenly claim, the kin of another heaven—arrived. As the Lord of Pure Brightness Heaven and his retinue came, each rode the eight-scene radiant simurgh chariot beneath nine-cloud luminous jeweled canopies. The "eight scenes" are also called the eight treasured wondrous scenes, the eight trigram divine scenes, or the eight-hued luminous scenes. Generally, the divine chariots of heaven gather the scenes of the eight directions and embody the harmony of the eight solar terms, hence the term "eight scenes." They performed the Great Mysterious Song and spirit-wondrous music, chanted the boundless merit of the Three Cavern treasure chapters, scattered celestial treasure flowers in all directions, sprayed celestial perfected incense, and, stepping upon the void, traversed the heavens to arrive respectfully before the Dao.

By the awe-inspiring power, virtue, and divine penetrations of the Primordial Heavenly Worthy and Jade Emperor, these multitude of treasure flowers instantly transformed in the void into a single jeweled canopy, shading and sheltering the great assembly of the Dharma gathering without omission.

This fool observes: When mortals cultivate the truth, pay homage to the Supreme Emperor, revere the Primordial Sovereign, and silently recite the true scriptures, their pure void spirit-light will, upon later audience in the mysterious realm, manifest secret wonders—jade flowers forming canopies, universally covering all wondrous beings. All this is the secret guidance of the Void Sovereign and the compassionate reception of the primordial spirit. Thus, when the Lord of the High Void and Pure Brightness Heaven later arrived at the Dharma banquet, presenting wondrous music and riding the numinous chariot, the celestial flowers he scattered, by the power of the Primordial Heavenly Worthy and Jade Emperor, formed a jeweled canopy covering all without exception. Those of aspiration who contemplate this canon and spiritually comprehend it will find that the wondrous transformations of heaven are fully possessed within their own bodies.

*Chapter on Spiritual Penetrations, Twenty-Six*

At that time, the Lord of the High Void and Pure Brightness Heaven, beholding this rare spectacle, prostrated himself and knelt in reverence, addressing the Heavenly Worthy and Jade Emperor: "This humble servant, indolent and remiss, arrived late to the Dharma assembly. Today, on this auspicious occasion, I have encountered the Dharma Bridge. The hidden and the manifest, the sacred and the profane, all universally partake of the sagely grace. A great radiance shines forth, revealing rare and wondrous signs, illuminating all heavens above. The Four Brahmā Heavens and Six Desire Realms, all the blessed lands and assemblies of perfected sages, beholding this radiance, gather in clouds. Below, it shines upon the boundless worlds of the lower realms, uniting with the Mysterious Capital, closely adjoining the Nine Heavens. Divine winds perform music, harmonizing palace and note, resonating brightly through the cloud courts, all transforming into Cavern Chapters. All beings universally attain the transformation of the Dao.

In the Fengdu Iron Enclosure, the eternal night of the Nine Dark Realms, all suffering beings in the hells, by the power of this light, are reborn in the heavens and enjoy bliss. Today, the scattered celestial treasure flowers swiftly coalesced into a canopy, universally covering the Dharma assembly. All in the great congregation partake of the power and awe-inspiring might of this light. Through a thousand kalpas of good causes and the cyclical movements of the Nine Heavens, the imperial Dao flows boundlessly, and the true Dharma flourishes. Today is most auspicious, as we behold and revere the mysterious merit."

The True Lord of Fire said: When the treasure flowers formed a canopy covering all, the Lord of the High Void and Pure Brightness Heaven, witnessing this rare event, prostrated himself and knelt, humbly addressing the Primordial Heavenly Worthy and Jade Emperor. He spoke of himself as a lowly and indolent servant, tardy in attending the Dharma assembly. Today, on this auspicious occasion, he encountered the compassionate salvation of the sagely Dharma Bridge. Bridges in the world are built by mortals to span waterways, sparing them from fording. Yet even the finest worldly bridges, constructed of wood and stone, have limited reach and are prone to decay; they cannot span great rivers, lakes, or seas. But the power of the sagely scriptures and Dharma transcends kalpas, pervades the cosmos, and requires no fabrication or trace. Through subtle transformation and secret divine penetrations, it enables beings to escape the river of love, depart the sea of desire, avoid the blood lake, and dispel great calamities—eternally indestructible, hence called the Dharma Bridge. It spans the hidden paths of darkness and the manifest realms of light. The sagely and the foolish, the wise and the ignorant, all universally partake of its sagely grace.

The Jade Emperor radiates the Great Illuminating Brilliance, manifesting a rare and wondrous divine form. Its light ascends to illumine all heavens of every realm—the Four Brahmā Heavens, the Six Desire Heavens, and every blissful pure land. All the immortals, perfected beings, divine sages, and holy assemblies behold this great radiance and gather like clouds in assembly. The clouds converge in an instant, filling the sky, their origin unknown. The holy hosts swiftly gather like clouds, hence called "cloud assembly." The light descends to illumine the boundless worlds below, all of which become as the Pure Subtlety Heaven’s Mystic Capital, closely linked in spirit to the Nine Celestial Upper Heavens. Within the light, a divine breeze plays celestial melodies, harmonizing as palace modes and shang tones blend. Though the five notes—palace, shang, and the rest—distinguish clarity and turbidity and correspond to the Five Phases, their natural wonder is not easily matched. The Emperor’s divine breeze harmonizes exquisitely of itself, far surpassing mortal music. As palace and shang tones resonate, they stir and resound through the cloud courts, transforming into the precious chapters of the Three Caverns. All beings in the worlds below universally attain the mysterious transformation of the Great Dao.

In the Fengdu prisons, the Iron-Walled Citadel, the eternal night of the Nine Dark Realms, and all the hells, suffering beings look up to receive the power of the Jade Emperor’s great illuminating Dharma. They are all reborn in the heavenly palaces, where they enjoy bliss. Today, the celestial treasures and wondrous flowers I have scattered swirl and weave into a floral canopy, universally covering and sheltering all assembled at this Dharma feast. All look up to receive the majestic power and divine virtue of the Heavenly Worthy Jade Emperor.

We, the Lords of the Pure Clarity Heaven, are not merely fortunate in this single lifetime to encounter such a rarity. Through countless kalpas, we have cultivated good causes, and now we meet the auspicious convergence of the Nine Heavens, where the imperial Dao of Heaven flows vast and level, and the profound and wondrous true Dharma flourishes in full splendor.

One version states: When the Primordial Beginning initiated transformation and expounded the supreme Dharma, the imperial wind was profound and serene, the Great Dao level and even. At that time, no heterodox paths existed, and the true Dharma flourished in its prime. This meaning is also acceptable.

Today’s celebration in the celestial realm is a most auspicious occasion. All divine beings and every living creature universally receive and rely upon the most mysterious transformative power.

Another version states: All desire to look up in hope of the mysterious power and humbly present the essentials of the Dao. This is also acceptable.

In my humble opinion: Though the human body is small, it encompasses Heaven and Earth, contains the myriad existences, and embraces all wonders. The pure, empty, and numinous qi governs the six yang, and there is also the Lord of the High, Empty, Pure Clarity Heaven. If the primordial spirit loses its governance and the mysterious transformation does not manifest, one is drawn into the waves of affection, sunk in the sea of suffering. The vast currents and towering waves surge without end—how can one avoid drowning and rescue those lost in darkness?

When even one person is steeped in delusion, they sink and drag others down with them, leading both astray—a matter not worth discussing. Those who stagnate in the Lesser Vehicle or are deluded by side paths, like flowing water without a source, cannot escape drying up—this, too, is not worth mentioning. Occasionally, one dredges the wellspring of the numinous and connects with the pulse of the Dao, gradually nearing transformation. Yet if one hoards their own richness and fails to let virtue descend, this is not the great accomplishment.

Thus, some attain the fruits of the Four Brahmā or Six Desire Heavens but do not reach the Nine Celestial or Seven Treasures realms. Some receive blessings among humans, or become lords of hells or demon kings. Some even sink into the Three Evil Paths or are lost in the Nine Dark Realms—what sorrow could be greater? When the numinous transformation is not manifest and the wondrous resonance is not revealed, the true scriptures fail to circulate. The jade-like flowers lose their luster because one has not cultivated good causes or believed in the true Dharma. Thus, one cannot hear the vast and level Dao or look up to receive the mysterious power.

If one can concentrate the mysterious spirit, stabilize the Heavenly Lord, and embody the pure, empty, and wondrously numinous, then when the later mechanism is activated, one will penetrate the Cao Creek, drink the entire Western River, merge with the golden liquid, and ascend the shore of the Dao. The sea of suffering and the pit of karma will be forever extinguished. One will transcend the Six Desires, rise above the Four Brahmā, universally unite with the myriad spirits, and illumine the dark realms. The divine breeze stirs the true, the wondrous resonance is peerless, and the true scriptures silently circulate without cease. The myriad existences receive boundless grace. Fengdu’s walls are breached, the Nine Dark Realms are illuminated, hells transform into heavens, and sinful beings become pure lands. The yin turbidity of the body entirely shifts to yang clarity; jade-like flowers radiate rosy hues, sheltering all wonders. This is truly the numinous power of the August Emperor and the force of the primordial spirit. Without accumulating cultivation and nurturing the true Dharma with unwavering faith, how could one hear the auspicious wind of the imperial Dao or look up to receive the mysterious power?

Alas! The wondrous truth of this body is revealed when we, the Lords of the Pure Clarity Heaven, arrive late at the Dharma feast and celebrate the encounter with the Dharma Bridge. To praise the sagely transformation and extol the mysterious power is to say that the Dao universally saves the dark and the manifest alike. Yet to cultivate good causes, broaden wondrous practices, not seek hasty transformation, and let the wondrous root arise naturally—this is the secret of attaining sagely perfection. Those who study the Dao should savor this and realize it for themselves.

**Chapter on Spiritual Penetrations, Verse 27**

At this time, as the holy assembly all look up to receive the mysterious power, the Lord of the High, Empty, Pure Clarity Heaven—explained previously—praises the Jade Emperor in verse:

The Lord of the Pure Clarity Heaven praises the Jade Emperor in verse:

Golden Portal, Mystic Vault Ancestor,
*(Ancestor: One version reads "Lord." Considering the scripture’s meaning, the Jade Emperor is the Lord of Heaven, teacher of all buddhas, and ruler of the Golden Portal, the venerable elder of the Mystic Capital’s vaulted heavens, hence called "Ancestor." If rendered as "Lord," it refers only to the Heavenly Emperor.)*

Supreme Jade Emperor Worthy,
*(Explained previously.)*

Wondrous form crowns all heavens,
*(All divine beings in the heavens possess fine forms, but some may decline or be limited in their transformations. Each resides in their own heaven and cannot assume all forms; their appearances and countenances are not supremely transcendent. The Jade Emperor’s form is wondrously excellent without limit, his appearance and countenance uniquely surpassing all heavens.)*

Compassionate light illumines the Three Realms.
*(His great compassionate radiance illumines the heavens above, the earth below, and the human realm in between, hence called "universally illumines the Three Realms.")*

True Sage, Wondrous Dao’s Master.

One tradition states: The Jade Emperor’s conduct is truly sagely and mystically wondrous—he is the revered master of the Dao’s lineage. Heavenly and mortal beings rely upon this master. The Jade Emperor serves as the teaching lord of heaven and humanity, sovereign of all spirits, and supreme divine sage of the heavens. All people in the world revere and depend upon him, drawing upon his transformative power; thus, he is the teacher of heaven and humanity.

He expounds the Great Vehicle’s teachings,
*(The Dao’s teachings are divided into three vehicles: upper, middle, and lower. There is also a supreme vehicle, which transcends all ranks, surpassing the three grades and encompassing all without omission—this is the Great Vehicle. The teachings of various spirits follow their own wisdom and insight; the Great Vehicle is rarely heard. The Jade Emperor’s dispensation of the Dao clarifies and reveals the true essence, penetrating from highest to lowest, encompassing all grades. All beings who receive his instruction attain liberation—this is the Great Vehicle’s expounding of the Dharma.)*

He points out the true One to those lost on the path.
*(The Jade Emperor employs the true essence and the mystic principle of the One to illuminate and awaken those who have strayed, offering direct transmission without deviation, preventing them from falling into lesser or misguided teachings. It is like pointing someone toward the main road, ensuring they do not stray onto crooked paths.)*

His virtue and power are like the emptiness of space.
*(All things in the world have limits and come to an end. Only the emptiness of space remains unchanged through kalpas, never altering. The Jade Emperor’s vast merit and supreme virtue are boundless, like the emptiness of space, impossible to fathom. While other divine sages possess merit and virtue, whether great or small, near or distant, they may be compared within their own measure. The Jade Emperor’s virtue and power defy comparison—thus, they are like the emptiness of space.)*

His praises are inexhaustible.
*(The Jade Emperor’s virtue and power are like the emptiness of space; his praises cannot be fully expressed, and devotion to him knows no end. His praises are boundless, and his sublime power cannot be named. As Huang Shigong said: Though the Lord of the High Void and Pure Clarity later attended the Dharma assembly, upon truly witnessing the Jade Emperor’s wondrous transformations and divine splendor, he was filled with endless admiration. Thus, he composed sublime verses to extol the Jade Emperor. In ancient times, Zai Wo, Zigong, and You Ruo excelled in praising and revering Confucius, for their wisdom was sufficient to recognize a sage. Now, the Lord of Pure Clarity praises the Jade Emperor’s virtue and power as boundless as the emptiness of space, his praises inexhaustible—no other eulogy has been so thorough and complete. This is akin to the wisdom of Zai Wo, Zigong, and You Ruo in recognizing Confucius. These verses may truly be called "words of insight.")

My humble observation: The primordial spirit of the human body remains unchanged through kalpas; the true master of the four limbs is the origin of all existence. It wondrously crowns the six yang, compassionately protects the three origins, and serves as the true teacher of the self, upon which the spirit and qi depend. Its numinous illumination shines brightly, its Dharma voice is supreme, directly shattering delusion and revealing the all-encompassing path. Its wondrous essence and mysterious power—wherever its virtue extends, it is equal to the emptiness of space. How could praises ever be exhausted? Yet people fail to turn inward and reflect, to comprehend this true essence. They do not recognize the supreme virtue within themselves, nor the Jade Emperor’s virtue and power—how then could they grasp the benefits of this scripture’s merit? No wonder they do not awaken to the true reality.

The Lord of Pure Clarity, gazing upon the Jade Emperor’s virtue and power, composed sublime verses in praise, not only to extol the blessings of heaven but also to instruct people to turn their light inward.
