If one can align with their original true nature, understand the power of the Dao, and emulate heaven’s impartiality, sharing the same merit as the Emperor, they will not be misled by other paths, nor lose their celestial treasure. Thus may they aspire to sagehood. Let those of resolve take heed.

**Chapter on Spiritual Powers, Twenty-Eighth**

He is the Lord of the Vault of Heaven, honored through kalpas without end. His wondrous vision and wondrous knowledge are peerless and unmatched. Profoundly still and truly pure, he is neither gone nor present, yet both gone and present. Supreme sage, supreme spirit, great in spiritual power, repository of radiance, mighty hero—he enlightens humans and heavens, teaching without end. Vast in compassion, vast in mercy, he turns the wheel of the Dharma, delivering all beings. Thus is he named the Jade Emperor, the true elder of the vault of heaven, wondrously perfect, pure, and serene. His wisdom and eloquence, his Dao and his honor, are supreme. To liberate all beings, he emits this light.

At that time, the Lord of the High Void and Pure Clarity, having spoken his verses in praise, sat in silent meditation.

Wei Boyang said: The Lord of the High Void and Pure Clarity, in extolling the Jade Emperor’s virtue and power, not only composed ten verses of praise but also declared: This Jade Emperor is the sagely lord of the vaulted and boundless heavens, the supreme honor through kalpas without measure. *(Ordinary kalpas have numbers—whether hundreds of millions or trillions—but none can be called "vast." The Jade Emperor has served as the teaching lord of the ten thousand heavens through kalpas beyond count, vast and profound, impossible to fathom. Hence, he is called "honored through kalpas without end.")* His far-reaching illumination leaves nothing unlit; his spiritual powers and wondrous vision penetrate all without obstruction. His great awakening and mystic knowledge have no equal, no peer for comparison. Radiant and translucent, profoundly still, majestic and unshaken, he is without duality, without cessation. His Dao is utterly true; his virtue utterly pure, unstained and unsullied.

Vast as if gone—yet not truly gone, for it is the natural state of emptiness. Vast as if present—yet not clinging to presence, for it is the wondrous existence of non-attachment. Whether vast as gone or vast as present, it cannot be clearly seen or measured. All immortals, buddhas, and spirits revere the Jade Emperor as the most supreme among sages. Among all divine beings, none possess spiritual powers like his. He is the most exalted and mysterious spirit, his transformations sixfold and transcendent, surpassing all. Truly, his great spiritual power illumines eternally, his radiance pure and undimmed, ever emerging, never extinguished or obscured. He is the true repository of radiance, containing boundless great light.

None is more honored than the Dao. The Jade Emperor embodies the Dao’s spontaneity, vast beyond measure, without limit. Rightly is he called the mighty hero. *(Worldly worthies perfect body and nature, rectify themselves and others, and encompass heaven and earth—this is the mighty hero. The Jade Emperor transforms heaven and earth, gives rise to people and things, without beginning or end. Among sages, he is the most honored; among spirits, the greatest. What hero could surpass him?)* He enlightens and transforms all humans and heavens, teaching and guiding the Dao without end. He covers and loves all existence, pitying and mindful of all beings, without limit.

Great in faith, vast in compassion, he turns the radiant Dharma-wheel, ensuring it neither stagnates nor conceals. *(The character "fades" (焕) might also be rendered as "turns," but this would be overly restrictive.)* To transform and deliver all beings, he is thus titled the Jade Emperor.

The true primordial elder of the vaulted heavens, most venerable, wondrously all-pervasive and perfectly attuned—truly pure, truly pristine—possessing boundless wisdom and infinite discernment, his subtle eloquence inexhaustible, his talents ever-flowing, his supreme Dao immeasurable, his honor unmatched. Now, to enlighten and uplift all beings, he radiates this great compassionate light, universally illuminating.

At that moment, the Lord of the High Void and Luminous Heavens spoke this gāthā in praise, then fell silent and resumed his seat.

*(My humble note: The primordial spirit within the human body is none other than the Jade Emperor of the heavens, known as the Primordial Sovereign, the True Lord, the Mysterious Origin, the Ancestral Perfected, the Celestial Monarch, the Nature School, the True Ancestral Origin, the Dharma-nature, the Wondrous Luminous True Mind, the Right Nature, the Mysterious Numinous, the True Master, the Mysterious Radiance, the Great Pillar, the Dharma King, the Wondrous Treasure, the True Root, the Buddha-nature, the True Seed, and the Cinnabar Primordial.)*

The true lord of the body, uniquely wondrous and peerless, holds infinite luminous potential, transforming yin and yang, his divine wisdom unfathomable. Compassionate toward all subtleties, his responses are all-encompassing and luminously attuned. Most honored and most noble, his transformative power knows no end. Silently merging essence and qi, he nurtures the true numinous. Thus, the true light reveals itself at times, and the wondrous mechanism perpetually arises. Those who embody this naturally give birth to the divine infant, sharing the Jade Emperor’s merit and virtue, their Dao-transformations endless.

Only when one truly grasps the gāthā of the Lord of the Luminous Heavens in praise of the Emperor does genuine knowledge and realization arise. Otherwise, the true mystery remains unattained, and the Emperor’s transformations go unrecognized. The verses of the Luminous Gāthā, when recited, may seem like a dream—how then can one attain the merit of the scripture or reap its true benefits?

Alas! The nature of the Dao resides within us, its true mystery self-sufficient. To comprehend the wondrous luminous true mechanism is to truly respond to and extol the Jade Emperor’s glorious radiance.

**Chapter Twenty-Nine: Divine Powers**

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the four assemblies, saying: This Emperor’s body is the Dao-body, no ordinary form. It is the body of boundless merit and virtue, the body of true purity and spontaneity, the indestructible true emptiness of divine luminosity, the supreme Dharma-body.

His majestic spirit vast and expansive, his renown all-pervading, no darkness escapes his illumination. His divine subtlety towering and sublime, beyond all description.

The Barefoot Great Immortal said: After the Lord of the Luminous Heavens recited the gāthā in praise of the Jade Emperor, he resumed his seat in silence.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Beginning again addressed the four assemblies at the Dharma assembly, saying: This wondrous transformative body of the Jade Emperor is the great Dao-body, no ordinary form.

The Dao is originally formless—how then can one speak of a "body"? Though the Dao is void and boundless, infinite and inexhaustible, it transforms the ten thousand things, completes beginnings and ends, animates yin and yang without cease. Truly empty yet possessing substance, it is not mere nothingness. The Jade Emperor’s merit and virtue are like the vastness of empty space, his spirit one with the Dao. Thus it is said: the Emperor’s body is the Dao-body, no ordinary form.

It is the body of inexhaustible great merit and virtue, the body of true purity, true clarity, and spontaneity, unbound. Merit has limits, virtue may be exhausted—how can one speak of boundlessness? The Jade Emperor transforms all worlds, unchanged since time immemorial—how could he be limited?

To be attached to form or constrained by appearances is not true purity or spontaneity. The Jade Emperor, forever free from defilement, attains great freedom—is this not spontaneity?

It is the body of divine luminosity, firm and enduring, the indestructible true emptiness, the supreme and incomparable wondrous Dharma-body. All things in the world possessing form are subject to decay—only emptiness endures. That which decays is neither firm nor divine. Since the great void abides, emptiness is the ultimate truth.

The Jade Emperor’s divine power persists through the ages undiminished, his mysterious radiance endures through kalpas unvanquished. Not only is he supremely divine and luminous, but his firmness is unassailable, his solidity unbreakable, forever immune to destruction or decay. It is the ever-abiding true emptiness, the indestructible wondrous body, the supreme and peerless Dharma-body.

Who could easily fathom his majestic virtue and divine radiance? Vast and boundless, expansive beyond measure, his inconceivable names and titles overflow, pervading the ten directions. His light reaches every mote of dust, no darkness escapes his illumination. His divine powers and mysteries towering and immeasurable, vast and indescribable—how could one ever fully extol them?

*(My humble note: The human nature is inherently luminous and divinely subtle, self-so. With the three bodies complete and the four wisdoms perfected, the vast qi of integrity, the essence of true unity, the myriad virtues and wondrous qualities—what is lacking? Yet in this fleeting body, one bears the responsibilities of the three realms, with no respite. It is no ordinary form, but the Dao-body, the body of boundless merit and virtue, the body of true purity and spontaneity, the indestructible true emptiness of divine luminosity, the supreme Dharma-body. How then do worldly people indulge themselves, squandering this body, their minds burdened and spirits scattered, essence depleted and qi dispersed, their nature and Dao obscured? Who attends to the mandate of destiny? The essentials of the Dao remain elusive. The illusory body vanishes in emptiness, this life passes in vain, existence and extinction like a dream—utterly unaware. How then can one attain transformation?)*

Some may possess luminous virtue and fulfill their nature, yet fail to preserve their attainment to the end. Thus, people cannot exhaust the divine and attain transformation, return to emptiness and become immortals, or merge with the Dao as one.

Only the Jade Emperor, whose body is the Dao, whose merit and virtue are boundless, whose purity and spontaneity are innate, whose divine luminosity is firm and indestructible, whose true emptiness is unassailable, and whose Dharma-body is supreme—his name remains imperishable.

For those newly entering the sagely stream, even a single gap remains unbridged. Gazing upon him, they cannot penetrate his mystery; speaking of him, they fail to awaken. Their minds have not yet grasped the workings of nature and destiny, nor do they understand the divine source of the divine. Their learning has not yet unified heaven and humanity, nor do they comprehend the transformative power of transformation. They resign themselves to the unfathomability of the heavenly Dao, yearning to encounter the transcendent sages who have attained the profound.

The Primordial Beginning took pity on sentient beings’ prolonged delusion and extolled the Emperor’s virtue as vast and far-reaching, fully awakening those deaf and blind through kalpas past to witness the wondrous efficacy of divine transformation. In true great compassion and profound benevolence, he desired all beings to enter the sublime, expanding his majestic numen and pervading his renown, illuminating the hidden and subtle, divine and wondrous, towering and boundless—his virtue defying all names. Such is the Heavenly Worthy’s great vow.

Yet the world drifts and founders, human hearts sink and drown, unable to follow the Emperor’s principles or uphold the Primordial Beginning’s teachings. Alas! Heaven and humanity share one principle, sage and mortal share one heart—failing to emulate the sage and aspire to heaven, the Dao’s law is natural, and one truly falls short before the true scriptures, the great Dao, parents, and the body of life. Such is the plight of those with resolve.

The thirty chapters on *Divine Transformations* declare: This Emperor is not one whose merit arises from cultivated deeds. Though in the past he descended to be born among humans, traversing many kalpas to enact transformation, demonstrating great divine transformations, his body remained pure and undefiled. Never did he cease residing in the Golden Palace, manifesting in myriad forms, responding to all directions, aiding and delivering sentient beings, elevating them to the Dao’s shore, universally bestowing teachings, awakening later generations. Those who follow and uphold his teachings ascend to truth and attain the Dao. Through such merit and virtue, his adornment is such that his radiance perpetually fills all heavens, his divine wisdom wondrously penetrating, beyond all measure.

The Perfected of Wondrous Conduct said: This towering, divinely wondrous Jade Emperor, whose virtues defy full enumeration, does not rely on contrived deeds or forced merit for cultivation and realization. In kalpas past, though he descended to be born among humans, traversing many kalpas to broadly enact teachings and display great divine transformations—renouncing kingship to cultivate the Dao, severing love to study the Way, administering medicines to heal illness, expounding the Dao to propagate transformation, enduring insult with joyful renunciation, attaining the rank of Golden Immortal, teaching and delivering bodhisattvas through kalpas—thus do the Buddhist scriptures record the causes of buddhas’ births, speaking of descending from Tuṣita Heaven upon a fragrant elephant into the womb of Queen Māyā, whence the Buddha of Literature was born. This, too, is but one manifestation of the Jade Emperor’s teachings, adapted to circumstances.

Elsewhere, he attended the Assembly of Floating Radiance, the Assembly of the Jeweled Pearl, assuming the forms of commoners and Daoists, wherever he encountered the numinous, universally delivering without cease. As Lord of all Heavenly Worthies, his divine transformations are immeasurable. Through many kalpas of enacting transformation and displaying great divine transformations, his Dharma-body remained pure and undefiled, towering and unshaken, never absent from the Golden Palace of Yellow and Gold.

When the Primordial Beginning was about to expound the *Jade Scripture*, the Emperor emitted a great light, instantly dividing his body to pervade the great heavenly palaces of the ten directions. In every world—above in heaven, below on earth, among humans—all beheld the radiance, each receiving benefit and joy, together hearing the Great Vehicle. Such was his division of body, transformation, and response to all directions, aiding and delivering sentient beings, elevating them to the Dao’s shore. The merit thus accrued was not confined to one time or place but universally bestowed teachings, opening and awakening later generations. Those who reverently follow the scriptures and honor the Emperor’s command may ascend to the rank of highest perfected and fulfill the great Dao.

The Emperor’s adornment with this supreme, wondrous merit is why his emitted radiance perpetually fills all heavens, his divine and great wisdom spiritually wondrous and penetrating, beyond all measurement and reckoning. His divine wisdom wondrously penetrating, his great radiance is no mere transient light—his virtue flourishes, and his light is wondrous. Beyond all measure, his divine wisdom wondrously penetrating is no fleeting attainment—his Dao is wondrous, and his divinity manifest. Thus is it ever clearer that the Emperor’s merit does not rely on cultivated deeds.

This fool observes: The primordial spirit of humans endures through kalpas unchanged; its great divine radiance and wondrousness defy easy description. How could it be achieved through intentional action? In hearing and seeing, awareness and knowing, movement and stillness, sitting and lying, eating and resting, speech and silence, responding to stimuli and reciprocating—though manifesting wondrously according to conditions, the pure original substance never departs the cinnabar palace, instantly congealing the mysterious and wondrous to produce the divine infant, while the true and real remains ever unseparated. In a hundred billion transformations, aiding and delivering according to direction, guiding beings to the Dao’s shore, broadly proclaiming the numinous essence, enlightening those of later times—guarding the secret and upholding the true, transcending the mortal and attaining the sage, all transformations reach fulfillment, no fruit left unripened. Through such wondrous conduct as adornment, a single gleam of mysterious radiance pervades all without obstruction, the marvelous efficacy of nature and Dao defying all measurement and reckoning. Behold the Jade Emperor’s sagely virtue and divine efficacy, untainted by contrivance and beyond all measure—are they not of one accord?

Though the nature of inherent perfection is shared, the reckless and abandoned are many, allowing their pure and upright nature to be obscured by lust and delusion, like a bright mirror buried in dust, its radiance unseen. Thus beauty and ugliness remain hidden, and the wondrous intent unmanifest. Yet if one scrapes away the grime and polishes the light, renewing day by day and growing month by month, responding without intention, the true and real is naturally at ease. The Golden Palace and Purple Mansion eternally house the primordial spirit, constantly responding yet constantly still, undisturbed in the least. In wondrous discernment, the one pervades the myriad; in manifest conduct, it responds without attachment. In great compassion and vast vows, it never regresses; in myriad wondrous adornments, it defies enumeration. Through boundless cultivation, true radiance naturally pervades—his merit and virtue are inconceivable.

Alas! This Dao is inherently possessed by humans, neither reliant on cultivated deeds nor attainable through stubborn emptiness, neither existent nor nonexistent. Those of discernment embody it.

The thirty-first chapter on *Divine Transformations* states: The radiance of this body bears wondrous names. They are called: Great Divine Transformation Light, Great Compassion Light, Great Joyful Renunciation Light, Great Forbearance Light, Great Equanimity Light, Great Gentleness Light, Great Freedom Light, Great Benefit Light, Great Wish-Fulfilling Light, Great Wisdom Light, Great Auspiciousness Light, Great Liberation Light, Great Refuge Light, Great Merit Light, Great Perfection Light, Great Unobstructed Light, and Invincible Light.

The Perfected of Great Wisdom said: The great radiance emitted by the Jade Emperor’s body bears these supreme and wondrous names.

What are these radiant names? They refer to the seventeen great lights, beginning with Great Divine Transformation Light. The Jade Emperor universally bestows illumination and embrace; through wondrous practices and accumulated realizations, he possesses great numinous power and is endowed with the six divine penetrations. His Divine Transformation Light adorns and illumines all things—this is the first of the radiant names.

Next, the Emperor embodies great compassion, great mercy; his boundless compassion and mercy manifest in wondrous, vast radiance. Great Compassion Light is the second.

Further, the Emperor truly embodies joyful renunciation; his boundless joy and renunciation shine with wondrous, universal brightness. Great Joyful Renunciation Light is the third.

Through kalpas uncounted, the Emperor has cultivated great forbearance; his limitless forbearance emits an unstoppable radiance. Great Forbearance Light is the fourth.

In former cultivations, the Emperor practiced great equanimity; his ceaseless equanimity shines with an irresistible light. Great Equanimity Light is the fifth.

In past kalpas, the Emperor also embodied great gentleness; his tender harmony remains unchanged through vast eons, universally manifesting an inexhaustible radiance. Great Gentleness Light is the sixth.

The Emperor’s virtue is tranquil and serene, transcendent and free; his expansive, luminous radiance knows no end. Great Freedom Light is the seventh.

The Emperor’s benevolence is vast and boundless, eternally benefiting all; his unceasing beneficence shines with dharma-splendor. Great Benefit Light is the eighth.

The Emperor’s universal body has realized wondrous awakening; pure and spontaneous, he is the Dharma King, the Tathāgata. After countless kalpas, he attained the imperial throne, his supreme merit transcending thought, his numinous transformations perfectly responsive. His Wish-Fulfilling Light endures without limit. Great Wish-Fulfilling Light is the ninth.

The Emperor possesses great wisdom, great discernment; his wisdom surpasses all, his radiance peerless. Great Wisdom Light is the tenth.

The Emperor is fundamentally perfectly good, eternally supremely auspicious; his radiance shines ceaselessly. Great Auspiciousness Light is the eleventh.

The Emperor, having long awakened, attained great liberation; spontaneously released, his golden light shines forever. Great Liberation Light is the twelfth.

The Emperor is one with the great Dao, the wondrous dharma spontaneous; through endless kalpas, his true faith never wavers. All in the ten directions and future ages eternally revere and uphold him, turning their spirits to the Dao, their radiance ever bright and undimmed. Great Refuge Light is the thirteenth.

The Emperor universally delivers boundless beings, perfectly accomplishing all without omission; his merit is supreme, his radiance ever resplendent. Great Merit Light is the fourteenth.

With merit perfected and the Dao complete, the Emperor’s virtue is perfectly fulfilled; his universal light shines eternally, signifying his accomplishment. Great Perfection Light is the fifteenth.

From dust and defilement long purified, his wondrous penetration is perfectly luminous; his numinous transformations unobstructed, the Emperor’s light shines forever. Great Unobstructed Light is the sixteenth.

Noblest among spirits, most revered among sages, Lord of the Myriad Heavens, Teacher of all Buddhas—throughout the vast kalpas and dharma realms, none surpass the Jade Emperor. Thus, his radiance perpetually fills all realms, his numinous transformations immeasurable. Invincible Light—is this not the seventeenth of the great lights?

These seventeen great lights, with their wondrous and numinous meanings, are now manifested by the Jade Emperor—how could his divine transformations be measured?

This humble observer notes: In the realm of human existence, the cultivation of true nature is paramount. Thus, the *Biographies of Immortals* regard this as the seed of great radiance. Though the true seed is fully possessed, none preserve it; thus, in the realm of delusion, one must undertake the work of purification. Therefore, to each supreme good cause corresponds a wondrous, divine light. The Jade Emperor’s accumulated cultivation is immeasurable, his wondrous practices inexhaustible—why only seventeen great lights? For the faculties of beings are many and difficult to awaken, and the transformations of the Dao are profound. The Emperor’s seventeen lights are like the Buddha manifesting his thirty-two-foot form while emitting great auspicious light from his crown. Moreover, the Emperor’s light is supremely wondrous, transcending all comparison—who could trace his wondrous practices or comprehend the seventeen great meanings? Alas, this is difficult to attain, yet it may be hoped for. The Dao resides within oneself: negligence dims it, diligence brightens it. Cultivate effortless practice without seeking swift transformation, and the Dao will naturally be attained.

**Chapter Thirty-Two: Divine Transformations**

Thus, those among you who desire to behold the Emperor yet cannot do so are hindered because you remain attached to body and speech, unable to relinquish habitual tendencies, afflictive actions, and karmic deeds. Due to these obstructions, you cannot gaze upon the Emperor’s compassionate countenance. I shall now proclaim for this assembly the method to sever these hindrances; all of you should each uphold and practice it.

At that time, the great assembly was overcome with joy, each bowing their heads before the Most Revered, desiring to hear the teaching.

Master Lei, the Radiant Elder, said: The Jade Emperor emits seventeen great lights, his divine transformations immeasurable. Thus, even the Heavenly Lords of the Lofty Void and Pure Brightness, though desiring to truly behold the Jade Emperor, cannot do so. The reason is this: though you are free from dust and defilement, having realized the station of Heavenly Emperor, the supreme Mahāyāna has not been fully penetrated. You remain attached to body and speech, unable to relinquish the habitual tendencies of countless kalpas—ignorance, afflictions, and the transgressions of mundane actions. Due to these obstructions, you cannot behold the Jade Emperor’s compassionate countenance.

Habitual tendencies arise from worldly desires and defilements. All delusive entanglements must not be coveted; yet, due to insufficient wisdom and excessive attachment, thoughts arise, gradually leading to contamination. Entangled by external objects, the bonds deepen, forming toxic habits like ropes tightly knotted, difficult to untie in an instant. Long-ingrained defilements are not easily removed; the roots of evil karma remain unpurified. Habitual tendencies toward worldly desires may accumulate afflictions, transgressive actions, or karmic conditions—endless distractions, unceasing disturbances, and the burdens of past deeds obscure and obstruct. Though you now govern the Brahmā heavens, your realization remains incomplete, the profound mystery not fully grasped. How then could you behold the Most Supreme? Thus, you cannot immediately see the Jade Emperor.

Here now do I, for this assembly of disciples, clearly expound and reveal the method to sever and dissolve all obstructions. Let each among you uphold and practice it with utmost devotion.

At that moment, the great assembly overflowed with joy and exultation, each prostrating before the Jade Table of the Primordial Beginning, bowing their heads in reverence, eager to hear the esoteric discourse on severing obstructions.

I—this is the self-designation of the Primordial Beginning. *Table*—a desk or stand.

I observe: since birth, each person carries karmic conditions from former lives. Though the kalpas renew and the qi of Great Harmony prevails, the cultivation of past eons is not easily forgotten at once. Thus, the scriptures compare the latent karmic affinities to accumulated toxins—truly an insightful analogy. Those bound by auspicious affinities may meet as kindred spirits across distant lands, while those entangled in malevolent affinities may remain as strangers though face-to-face. Do not dismiss the records of the *Daoist Canon* or the annals of Buddhist teachings as heterodox doctrines; even within Confucian texts, Yan Ying’s opposition to Confucius was attributed to fate, and the great scholars Cheng and Su were divided into the factions of Shu and Luo—such too is the misfortune of ill-matched affinities. Yet those who ought to be close may grow distant over time, a lament shared across ages. How then can the doctrine of karmic conditions be entirely abandoned?

Thus, the ten perceptions are not easily exhausted, the five aggregates not easily fathomed. The thirteen kinds of disciples, the twenty-five demonic seeds, the seven illusions and three unions—all these mechanisms and snares, who can easily escape? The Lord of the Pure Bright Heaven, though enthroned as a supreme deity and freed from worldly defilements, has not yet transcended the accumulated karma of countless kalpas, lingering in the lofty void, styled the Pure and Bright. Past virtuous causes have not yet shed the trappings of emptiness. How then could one such as the Jade Emperor, who embodies the wondrous existence of empty luminosity, be readily perceived?

In examining the sutras and the bodhisattva path, even those who beheld the face of Śākyamuni Tathāgata did not truly see him. When the Buddha of Measureless Light expounded the supreme truth, the bodhisattvas listened in silence—such is the meaning here. How easily can the Most Sagely be seen? How easily can the obstructions of bodily and verbal habits be dissolved?

Yet this principle is most difficult to perceive: to *see* the Emperor is not to see with the eyes; to fully comprehend the Emperor’s conduct is to thoroughly align with his virtue. As among Confucius’ disciples, only those who truly received the Master’s transmission of the heart-mind attained the one mechanism. When the heart is sincere, though times and worlds differ, the principle remains the same. Only through spiritual communion and heart-mind resonance is true vision attained. Even the wise Yan Hui fell short by a single degree; how then should the Lord of the Pure Bright Heaven, unable to behold the Jade Emperor, be doubted?

The method of the Primordial Beginning to sever the demonic array is to illumine past deeds, verify the heart’s essence, and dissolve all barriers. Once inner obstructions are melted away, what external hindrance remains? Then the Jade Emperor may be seen. Thus, the assembly yearned to hear these teachings.

Alas! The arising of obstructions and the breaking of demonic arrays—all proceed from the mind. With great penetration and unimpeded freedom, one’s original spirit responds without negligence. The coarse traces of speech and hearing must not become stagnant obstructions. Is not the Great Dao within me? Strive on!

**Chapter Thirty-Three: The Divine Penetrations**
The Heavenly Worthy spoke:
The method to sever obstructions is to generate great wisdom. Do not arouse doubt, do not arouse greed or anger, do not arouse sensual desire, do not arouse jealousy, do not arouse killing or harm, do not arouse mundane emotions, do not arouse mundane thoughts, do not arouse dullness or defilement, do not arouse sound or form, do not arouse right or wrong, do not arouse love or hatred, do not arouse discrimination, do not arouse arrogance, do not arouse attachment.

Guangchengzi said: When the assembly of the pure requested the Primordial Heavenly Worthy to expound the wondrous principle of obstruction-free vision, he declared: To sever obstructions and behold the wondrous transformation and radiant countenance of the Jade Emperor, there is no other way—one must generate the divine wisdom of the spirit-mind, firmly believe in the true Dao, and not arouse the heart of doubt, duality, or confusion.

The Great Dao is utterly correct, the True One without duality—there is fundamentally nothing to doubt. Yet when clarity is insufficient to perceive the subtleties, one wavers between two extremes, lacking steadfast vision, and demonic knowledge infiltrates. Once you know the Great Dao resides within you, guard this knowing with firmness. Do not divide it into two, do not multiply it into three—what then is there to doubt? Without doubt, there is no confusion, and the Dao may be entered.

Thus, the great wisdom that severs obstructions and dissolves ingrained habits must first be free of doubt. Seekers of the Dao must not calculate merit, nor seek it elsewhere. Anger, resentment, indignation, and discontent—none of these may arise.

Next in severing obstructions: do not arouse greed or anger. With the heart focused on the Dao, its center remains naturally pure. Nurturing private desires and indulging in excess easily gives rise to deluded thoughts; even the slightest inclination toward sensual indulgence or craving greatly disrupts the truth.

Third in severing obstructions: do not arouse sensual desire. The Dao embraces all without exception; the worthy and the unworthy alike are my teachers and friends. Even the slightest envy of the worthy or disdain for the mediocre is a grave error.

Fourth in severing obstructions: do not arouse jealousy. The Great Dao is supremely benevolent, not tolerating even the slightest harm. If, due to adversity or malice, one harbors thoughts of eradication, this is a grave departure from the Dao.

Fifth in severing obstructions: do not arouse killing or harm. Though the *Yinfu Jing* speaks of the mechanism of killing, it refers only to the ability to subdue and restrain demonic forces, whereby true freedom is attained. As in autumn’s solemn withering, when grasses and trees return to their roots, life’s mechanism withdraws—here lies the benevolence of Heaven and Earth, not the killing of the mundane world. It is also said: “Blessing arises from harm.” This too reveals the intent of Heaven and Earth, not the harm of the mundane world.

Sixth in severing obstructions: do not arouse mundane emotions. The Great Dao is without action; worldly perceptions and knowledge are not employed. The slightest activation of mundane intent leads to endless error.

Seventh in severing obstructions: do not arouse mundane thoughts. The mechanism of the Great Dao requires all thoughts to be purified. The slightest trace of worldly thinking brings boundless harm.

Eighth in severing obstructions: do not arouse dullness or defilement. The Dao is fundamentally pure and luminous, free from contamination. The slightest touch of dullness or worldly filth loses one’s utmost truth.

The Dao is without sound or scent. To seek it through sound or form is to distance oneself from the Dao. Those who embody the Dao are not only unobstructed by external sounds and forms, untouched by worldly affairs, but also free from all traces and boundaries of the Dao—nothing is sought, nothing is grasped.

Ninth in severing obstructions: do not arouse sound or form. The Dao is fundamentally all-pervading unity. To cling to right or wrong is to lose the primordial truth of the Great Mystery.

Tenth in severing obstructions: do not arouse judgments of right and wrong. Though Mencius said, "The sense of right and wrong is innate in all people," the profoundly wise appear foolish—why would they engage in such distinctions? The Dao makes no choices. To harbor love or aversion is to obstruct truth.

Eleventh in severing obstructions: regard all with equanimity, without arousing hatred or attachment. Principle is fundamentally undivided; to discriminate with cleverness is to depart from the Dao.

Twelfth in severing obstructions: do not arouse discriminating thoughts. To see the Dao clearly is to rise above the dust of the world, disdaining worldly concerns. Yet to harbor arrogance even once is to greatly deviate from the Dao.

Thirteenth in severing obstructions: do not arouse thoughts of self-importance or disdain. The Great Dao is lively and free, utterly beyond attainment. Sever these thirteen obstructions, and the Dao is attained. Though called "attaining the Dao," in truth there is nothing attained. The slightest grasping or attachment means principle’s obstruction remains unremoved, and one is bound by dharma.

Fourteenth and final in severing obstructions: do not arouse attachment. As this fool observes: the Dao within humans is inherently unobstructed. Only when the world’s affairs and principles obscure it does one lose the Dao. Thus, the Primordial Beginning in compassion revealed this chapter on severing obstructions to the pure assembly, enumerating each point to inspire resolve and unobstructed progress. Shedding the obstructions of worldly affairs and transcending the snares of dharma, one’s luminous countenance before the Jade Emperor will, with one’s wondrous clarity, shine forth in response—what then remains unseen?

Yet severing these two obstructions is but the gateway to the Dao. The profound awakening to divine transformation and the profound mystery shall be discussed later.

**Chapter Thirty-Four: Divine Powers**
Concentrate the spirit and settle the thoughts; all spirits are subdued and harmonized. The mind becomes like the vast emptiness of heaven, inwardly and outwardly pure and unblemished, containing all without exclusion, embracing all without rejection. Let no external deviance disturb this supreme Dao, leading one astray from the true source, corrupting the numinous root, and stealing the supreme treasure. Thus, through countless kalpas, one remains forever mired in the mundane, entangled in the web of the worldly. Myriad demons assail, and for hundreds of thousands of kalpas, one hears not the wondrous dharma. Ghosts and spirits seize the chance to condemn, dragging one from life into death.

Therefore, you must resolve with wholehearted sincerity to guard the true source and prevent its loss. As previously described, you must sever and eliminate all such obstructions. With the body purified, you transcend all difficulties—this is called the treasure of the Dao, the pillar upholding the dharma.

Liu Haichan said: The Primordial Beginning’s teaching on severing obstructions generates great wisdom and cuts off the fourteen karmic tendencies. What is its ultimate aim? When obstructions are severed and obscurations removed, the spirit becomes clear and thoughts serene. One should silently abide in the primordial numinous origin, concentrate the original spirit, and settle all thoughts. All spirits harmonize and subside; the mind becomes like the boundless emptiness of the sky, inwardly and outwardly pure and steadfast. It contains and embraces all beings and phenomena in the dharma realm. With steadfast vision and unwavering resolve, one remains unchanging. Let no external deviance disturb the supreme and perfect Dao, leading one astray from the true and mysterious source, corrupting the wondrous numinous root, and stealing the indestructible and inalienable supreme treasure. Otherwise, through kalpas without end, one remains forever mired in the mundane, thoroughly entangled in the web of worldly dust. Myriad demons of the yin realms assail, and for hundreds of thousands of kalpas, one is deluded by demonic karma, never hearing the most supreme and wondrous dharma. Ghosts and spirits seize the chance to condemn, dragging one from the path of life into the realm of death.

Therefore, all in this dharma assembly must focus with sincere resolve to guard and uphold the original true source, preventing its loss or abandonment. As previously described, you must sever and eliminate all doubts, delusions, and obstructions. The fourteen obstructions, external deviance, life and death—all such matters are encompassed herein. Having severed all obstructions, the body attains true purity, transcending and ascending beyond the three realms, escaping the karmic suffering, disasters, and hardships of cyclic existence. This method of severing obstructions is called the supreme treasure of the Dao, the great pillar upholding the true dharma. Without pillars, pavilions, pagodas, temples, halls, gates, and dwellings cannot be constructed. Without severing obstructions, one cannot complete the Dao, enter sagehood, or transcend the mundane. Severing obstructions prevents ultimate ruin and allows the true dharma to flourish. Thus, the Heavenly Worthy regards severing obstructions as the pillar upholding the dharma.

As this fool observes: the original spirit of human nature is inherently pure and undefiled, indestructible through countless kalpas. Fond of stillness and harmony, it is ever luminous, no different from the sages and perfected ones. If this luminosity persists without cease, how could the wondrous light of the Jade Emperor’s divine transformation not be personally witnessed? Yet thoughts entangle the mind, and habits persist unchanging. Few understand the Dao, and those who do often seek quick results. Thus, ingrained habits are hard to exhaust, afflictions difficult to relinquish, and the Emperor’s light remains unseen.

Only with true clarity, profound penetration, utmost vigor, and resolute decisiveness—recognizing the reality of nature and life, discerning the illusory nature of all phenomena—can one first see the Dao and forget things, then practice the Dao and forget people, then attain the Dao and forget the self, then perfect the Dao and forget the mind, then delight in the Dao and forget pursuits. Further, one forgets even the act of forgetting, merging principle and phenomena, transcending both truth and illusion, and no longer dwelling in the boundaries of sage or mundane. What need is there for the five ranks of host and guest? Attainment is no attainment; preservation is no preservation. Emptiness is not emptiness; the unspiritual is spiritual. Thus, past habits are purified, accumulated karma is severed, subtle defilements are extinguished, and one ascends to the supreme. Without need for silent audience before the Emperor, one shares the Emperor’s spirit. Without clinging to the Dao’s naturalness, one unites with the Dao’s truth. What place is there for the three vehicles, or the various ranks? Among sages, one is the most exalted, with unparalleled merit and virtue.

All can achieve this, but only when the roots and dust are purified, when effort is profound and practice wondrous, when there is non-action and no seeking.

Those who feign attainment surely cannot transcend; when fusion remains incomplete and transformation lacks spiritual power, one’s entry into sagehood is still imperfect—such as earthbound immortals of the Daoist tradition, bodhisattvas of the Buddhist teachings, or the great worthies of the Confucian school. Now, those who seek the Dao must model themselves on the highest sages and not be content with the Great Vehicle alone.

**Chapter Thirty-Five: Spiritual Powers**
One must further cultivate and revere this scripture, as though drawing near the Emperor, nurturing a heart of reverence and awe. Fix the mind upon the Emperor’s august countenance, extol his sacred name, and only then will you and all others behold his compassionate visage, receive his protection and deliverance, universally hear the wondrous Dharma, personally offer devotion and veneration, and forever escape the cycles of rebirth.

The Eastern Flower Lord of Wood declared: The Primordial Beginning revealed to the assembly the method for severing obstacles, proclaiming it the treasure of the Dao and the pillar of the Dharma. He further instructed the assembly on the meaning of enduring devotion, saying: "You, the pure assembly, having heard the true Dharma today, must further cultivate, revere, and uphold this *Scripture of the Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct*. To recite this scripture is to draw near the August Jade Emperor, fostering a heart of reverence, awe, and devotion. Knowing the scripture’s sanctity prevents disrespect toward Heaven’s Dao; recognizing its weight prevents disregard for Heaven’s treasures. Perpetual reverence ensures no defiance or irreverence, and the Great Dao is naturally attained—just as the *Analects* speaks of awe for Heaven’s mandate and awe for the words of sages. Though drawing near the Emperor is not the same as truly beholding the Jade Emperor, if one cannot face him even for a moment, one cannot maintain reverence for even that moment. Fixing the mind upon the Jade Emperor’s august countenance and wondrous form is not merely an act of imagination; it is as though he were truly present, serving the Emperor with clarity. Thus, one’s virtue harmonizes with Heaven and Earth, becoming a supreme sage. Extolling and proclaiming the Emperor’s most sacred names will allow you and the great assembly to behold the Jade Emperor’s radiant, compassionate visage, all receiving his protection and deliverance, universally hearing the supreme, most true, and wondrous Dharma. You will personally offer devotion and veneration to the Emperor and this scripture, forever free from the loss of rebirth and transmigration.

Another passage states: To see this scripture, hear this wondrous Dharma, and behold the Emperor’s visage, then personally and earnestly revere, venerate, and make offerings, is to forever depart the dust of the mundane and escape the suffering of rebirth and transmigration. Another interpretation holds that the heart will never regress, and further exploration deepens this understanding.

A query arises: The Confucian texts say, "The spiritual cannot be attained through thought." The Daoist scriptures say, "Spiritual transformation arises without intention, following naturalness." The Buddhist scriptures say, "One who seeks the Tathāgata through form or sound walks the wrong path and cannot see the Thus-Come One." Yet here it is said, "Fix the mind upon the august countenance, extol the sacred name, and only then will you behold the compassionate visage." Could the words of the Primordial Beginning and Mysterious Ancestor deceive us? This is not mere mental contemplation or fixation on words and sounds. One’s virtue harmonizes with Heaven, and one’s spirit resonates with the Emperor, merging and forgetting all distinctions. Thus, the ancients said, "Heaven’s majesty does not depart from the space before one’s face." Through reverence and transformation, praise and extolling arise unconsciously—just as the Confucian texts say, "Speak the words of Yao, act as Yao acted, and you are Yao." The Buddhist teachings say, "The Dharmakāya enters my nature, and my nature unites with the Tathāgata." The Daoist scriptures say, "When spirit unites with the Dao, the Dao and the self become one." Only thus can one hear the wondrous Dharma, make offerings, and escape rebirth. If one merely contemplates in the heart or extols with the mouth, failing to return the body, spirit, and life to the Dao, merging the mind with its truth, this cannot be called true veneration—how then can one escape rebirth? To attain ultimate freedom from descent and unchanging permanence, the acts of fixing the mind, extolling, and making offerings must transcend worldly understanding.

The foolish observe: Human life and nature are endowed by Heaven, and none are without them. Yet, mired in the mundane stream, one sinks into the cycles of rebirth. If one can master the great principles of the world, fully realizing one’s nature, this is true cultivation and reverence for the Jade Emperor’s scripture. To face and serve Heaven is to draw near the Emperor. With utmost care and reverence, serving without transgression, one nurtures a heart of devotion. The body acts as Heaven’s agent, the mouth speaks Heaven’s words, following Heaven without partiality—this is the Emperor’s true governance. Thus, contemplating the Jade Emperor’s countenance, extolling his name, one receives the blessing of beholding his visage. Virtue is one, and every action is auspicious. Fully realizing oneself, others, and all things, participating in transformation and nurturance, returning life and sincerity, embodying form with utmost likeness, utmost sincerity without cease, enduring without end—this is to receive protection and deliverance, universally hear the wondrous Dharma, personally offer devotion and veneration, and forever escape rebirth.

Alas! The Dao within humanity must be sought without departure. The scriptures of the Dao are like paths for the traveler; to tread the great way, how can one not follow this path? This is what Confucius meant by "How could one not follow the Dao?" The Primordial Beginning said that the common cannot see the Emperor. Yet those who truly savor this scripture’s meaning will naturally stand shoulder to shoulder with the Jade Emperor.

**Chapter Thirty-Six: Spiritual Powers**
At that time, the four assemblies, having heard this teaching, rejoiced and leapt with joy, exclaiming that such wonders had never been before. The Heavenly Official Great Emperor declared: At this moment of expounding the Jade Scripture, the four assemblies of the Dharma gathering heard the Primordial Beginning Dao Ancestor complete the *Scripture of the Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct: Spiritual Powers Chapter* in the Heaven of Subtle Light. They heard of the Emperor’s wondrous birth and growth, his many lifetimes of cultivation, his boundless transformations, his unfathomable merit and virtue, his natural spiritual responses, and the supreme greatness of his Dharma. The jade maidens attending him were transformed from celestial beings. The vast kalpas of the sand realms all depend on this scriptural Dharma. It clarifies the causes of sin and fortune, and one hears the wondrous principles of severing obstacles. The seventeen great radiant lights have their foundation; the cultivation of truth through billions of kalpas has its essentials. Taking the Dharma as one’s model, entering sagehood is effortless. Rejoicing in the shedding of karmic dust and the ease of entering the seven abodes, all were filled with joy and delight, leaping and exulting in unison, praising with one voice.

Here at this Dharma assembly, the most excellent karmic conditions converge—this rare encounter is no mere coincidence. This assembly, this hearing, this Emperor, this scripture, this moment, this teaching—such has never been seen across kalpas past. Some may say that upon hearing this discourse, one should focus solely on the methods of severing demonic obstructions, taking it too narrowly. When the Primordial Dao Ancestor expounded the scripture, the *Divine Transformations Chapter* was concluded—not that after finishing, He spoke again. Though divided into three scrolls and five chapters, it was out of compassionate instruction that the celestial perfected arranged the teachings into three scrolls. To regard the concluding praises of the final scroll as identical to other laudations would be to miss the deeper meaning. Thus, upon hearing this discourse, one must also bear in mind what precedes it. Let the reader examine this carefully.

In my humble view: The spirit, qi, and blood of the human body obey the celestial sovereign within; the wondrous mind is luminously clear, the celestial melody resounds, harmony flows naturally, and supreme harmony arises spontaneously. Hands dance and feet leap, boundless joy unfolds, and in attaining the Dao, one forgets all scheming—nothing in the world surpasses this. Even the four assemblies who hear this teaching rejoice and exult, marveling at what has never before existed. Yet the world is drowned in profit and desire, few awaken to truth, and those who enter sagehood and achieve perfection are rarely seen. If one hears the scripture and inwardly comprehends it, embodying supreme harmony while mind and spirit merge with transformation, is the Emperor’s work not already within me?

**Examination of Chapter Divisions in the First Scroll**
When the Primordial Heavenly Worthy expounded the *Collected Scripture of the Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct*, the celestial perfected inquired about the origins of the Emperor’s transformations. Though their words differed, all occurred in a single moment—why then was the first scroll divided into thirty-six chapters? The scripture’s exposition unfolded in one instant, but questions and answers varied. Later, unable to fully grasp the scripture’s purport, the profound and mysterious teachings of the supreme sage, the celestial emperors, gods, and perfected—along with the Five Elder Emperor Lords—collated the text, while the Heavenly Strategist continued the compilation afterward. The Wenchang Emperor and the Celestial Pivot Minister each, in their time, offered critical assessments and corrections, designating the first section as *The Divine Transformations Chapter of the Clear Subtlety Heavenly Palace*—no other chapter was so distinguished, for the Emperor’s divine transformations are peerless, His station supreme. This teaching of the Primordial Ancestor is beyond the speech of all immortals and buddhas.

During the Han, Wei Boyang; in the Tang, Lü Chunyang; in the Yuan, Qiu Changchun; and in the Ming, Luo Nian’an—all discussed this in great detail, dividing it into chapter annotations. The first scroll’s *Divine Transformations Chapter* thus comprises thirty-six chapters, not arbitrarily dissecting the true words but aligning with the meaning of the thirty-six heavens to establish the divisions. Each demarcation carries intent, the ideas interconnected, preventing fragmentation. If those who recite and study this scripture purify their minds and still their thoughts, embodying the supreme sage’s intent in expounding the scripture and the perfected’s purpose in dividing the chapters, their spirits will resonate with the sagely and true. When the scripture’s vital essence flows uninterrupted, what need is there to distinguish thirty-six chapters? And how could the scripture’s purport remain unattainable?

Yet those who cling to the text are many, while those who inwardly comprehend without tiring are few. Some dismiss the scripture as useless, others seize upon a single phrase as extraordinary, or fixate on a single character as flawed. They distinguish between *Lingbao* and *Gaoshang* in name only, failing to listen with the heart and grasp the wondrous communion of the spirit. Thus, through the scripture, they cannot awaken to the Dao, instead becoming ensnared by the obstacle of words—this is the gravest delusion.

Alas! The ultimate teachings of all scriptures are the seal of the mind. Through words, one perceives the Dao; having attained the Dao, one forgets words. The profound and hidden discourses are all the inherent principles within us—why doubt their difficulty or, worse, disparage them lightly? A single moment of attainment should not breed complacency. These prefatory and concluding remarks are appended as a warning to scholars.

**Commentary on the Imperial Scripture, Scroll Four**
*End of the First Scroll’s Thirty-Six Chapters*

**Collected Commentaries on the Imperial Scripture, Scroll Five**

**The Orthodox Transmission of the Daoist Canon, Continued Daoist Canon**

**The Highest Emperor’s Original Acts Scripture, Scroll Two**

From the preceding scroll’s *Divine Powers Chapter* to the sacred transformations of the Heavenly Officials. The sagely and true of the Three Teachings are all beyond easy attainment, hence this is listed first to show the origin of the divine transformations in this true scripture.

This section begins with the *Divine Incantations Chapter*, for the scripture contains secret dharma-words. They can deliver humans and record immortals, restrain stars, subdue demons, govern waters, pacify the five directions, and succor the dharma-realm—thus they are called "divine incantations." Following the divine powers with their secret dharma-words and esoteric texts, such benefits place this as the second chapter.

**The Great Illuminating Perfect Radiance Divine Incantations Chapter, Second**
*Divine Incantations Chapter, First Section*

At that time, the Primordial Ancestor of Heaven and Earth, the Five Elder Thearchs, bowed their heads and knelt in reverence, addressing the Heavenly Venerable:

"We have heard that the Highest Jade Emperor, in great compassion for sentient beings, universally emits divine radiance, illuminating the dharma-realm. The six realms of the ordinary and the four ranks of the sagely all partake of the blessings of the Dao’s shelter.

We humbly consider that the lifespan of ordinary beings is brief, and the kalpa’s destiny nears its end. The true Dao ought to be propagated to deliver the multitudes, allowing those who cultivate reality to have a time for light ascent, and the people of the latter age to all attain longevity.

At that time, when the Primordial Heavenly Venerable had finished expounding the *Divine Powers Chapter*, the Primordial Ancestor of Heaven and Earth’s inception, the Five Directions’ Five Spirits, and the Five Elder Thearchs bowed their heads in obeisance, prostrated in reverence, and addressed the Primordial Heavenly Venerable:

'We have heard that the Highest Jade Emperor, in great mercy, pities the sentient beings of the world, universally emitting the great divine powers of boundless true radiance, illuminating the three thousand great thousand worlds, all heavens and earths, and every dharma-realm. The six kinds of ordinary beings—heavenly, human, demonic, hellish, hungry ghosts, and animals—as well as the four ranks of the sagely—those of the supreme vehicle, and the upper, middle, and lower vehicles, the immortals, buddhas, spirits, and aspirants—all universally partake of the blessings of the great Dao’s compassionate radiance.

We humbly consider that ordinary beings are short-lived, the world’s span is fleeting, and the kalpa’s destiny in the dharma-realm nears its end. The true Dao of immortals ought to be transmitted and practiced to deliver the billions of people, allowing those who aspire to immortality and cultivate reality to have a time for liberation, attaining lightness of body and ascension, while the people of the latter age suffer no premature death and all attain longevity.

Yet human life in the world has a fixed destiny, and the sages of the Three Teachings all shed their bones in the dust. Yanzi, the great worthy, died at thirty-two. Though the *August Scripture* brings benefits, how can it defy the great workings of creation and grant humans immortality?'

This is not so. The human body may die, but the principle of human life does not perish. If the Dao is not understood, though one lives in the world, the heart is already dead—merely clinging to life in cowardice, how can this be called longevity? If one comprehends the Dao, awakens thoroughly, and completes practice, returning to emptiness and transcending transformation, then to hear the Dao in the morning and die by evening leaves no regret—this is true longevity.

Thus the *Dao De Jing* states: 'That which dies yet does not perish is longevity.' Confucius said: 'Human life is upright.' He also said: 'The humane are long-lived.' The Buddhist scriptures say: 'If one fully realizes nirvana, one sees the Tathagata—this is called the indestructible vajra.'

The perfected of the Three Teachings do not regard death as death, but ignorance of the Dao as death; they do not regard life as life, but realization of the Dao as life. Though the workings of creation make birth and death inescapable, they may bind ordinary people but cannot bind the sages.

The *August Scripture of the Jade Emperor* was expounded by the Primordial Heavenly Venerable as the supreme vehicle’s wondrous dharma, the true essence of the Three Teachings, the profound secret of the myriad methods, the compassionate vessel of the dharma-realm, the crucial gate of life and death, the esoteric meaning of formation, duration, decay, and emptiness, the pivot of kalpas’ turning, the broad path of transcendence and realization, the wondrous means of delivering the world, and the bridge for untying knots and removing transgressions.

If the Most Venerable compassionately expounds this scripture, once the multitudes receive the sagely grace and rely on the power of divine radiance, all may return to the true dharma, avoid deviant paths, and face life and death without shame. It can grant short-lived beings long life—such is the divine efficacy of this scripture."

*Seal of the sound, yin.* (蒸 is interchangeable with 烝.)

At the kalpa’s end when the final age draws near,
the *Divine Incantations* chapter two:

From of old, the *Primordial Beginning’s Cavernous Mystery Numinous Treasure Vermilion Script Jade Chapters True Writ* arose before the Primordial Beginning, within the empty void—ere heaven and earth took root, ere sun and moon shone forth, in profound obscurity, without ancestor or lineage, without qi or image, without color or name, without form or trace, without sound or voice, in the chaos of the Great Nonbeing. The numinous writ, veiled in dim haze, flickered in and out of existence, now present, now absent. Yet when the numinous diagram unfolded and transformation began, when the mysterious signs shifted and qi congealed to float in the void, riding the turning of the mechanism to meet its destined moment, the *Jade Emperor’s True Teachings*, the *Numinous Treasure Secret Scripts*, and the inconceivable, supreme divine incantations came into being.

The Five Venerable Lords, Ancestors of Heaven and Earth, declared that the true Dao of the *August Emperor’s Venerable Scripture* could grant longevity to the multitudes of the final age—how did it come to possess such vast efficacy?

From of old, the *Primordial Beginning’s Cavernous Mystery Numinous Treasure Great Vermilion Celestial Writ*’s true writ of azure jade and jasper chapters arose before the dharma-realm was established, before the Primordial Beginning’s original inception, within the vast emptiness of the Great Void—ere the Two Modes had divided, ere the Supreme Ultimate or Non-Ultimate, ere heaven and earth had laid their foundations, ere yin and yang, water and fire had begun their gestation, ere sun and moon had cast their light. Vast and indistinct, how could one discern its divisions? Only profound obscurity reigned. The myriad forms had not yet arisen—what could precede them? The origin of creation was unseen; it was without ancestor or lineage. In the mysterious emptiness of the Great Void, no qi was visible, no forms or images existed, no colors to be perceived, no names to be uttered, no shapes or shadows, no beginnings or ends, no echoes or traces. Silent and desolate, what sounds or voices could there be? Boundless and infinite, it was the chaos of the Great Nonbeing.

The true writ of the *Primordial Beginning’s Cavernous Mystery Numinous Treasure Vermilion Script Jade Chapters*, its numinous and secret radiance, though veiled in dimness and not clearly seen, yet faintly revealed its traces—now present, now absent, neither existent nor nonexistent, neither being nor nonbeing, existing yet never truly existing, nonexistent yet never truly nonexistent.

The Primordial Beginning’s numinous workings unfolded the mysterious diagram, opening the myriad transformations. The wondrous signs of the mysterious origin shifted and turned, congealing the subtle qi of Brahma to pervade the empty void, riding the mechanism of the mysterious workings to meet the destined moment when the true Dao should spread its blessings upon heaven and humankind. The *Jade Emperor’s Precious Teachings*, the *Numinous Treasure’s Secret Celestial Scripts*, and their immeasurable, inconceivable supreme virtues—these divine incantations then manifested their secrets and took form, and the wondrous dharma came into being.

The Vermilion Script, the true writ of the *Jade Emperor’s Venerable Scripture* and the wondrous existence, was all formed from the primordial Brahma-qi of the heavens. Its characters spanned a *zhang* in length, their crimson light resplendent, written in great vermilion gold upon jade chapters in the Cinnabar Heaven. Above the Nine Heavens, all were azure-jade chapters, the writ of the *Primordial Beginning’s Cavernous Mystery Numinous Treasure*. Their radiance like precious rosy clouds, their luster like jade—hence called the *Jade Chapters*.

They arose before the Primordial Beginning, before the original inception of heaven and earth—not before the Primordial Heavenly Worthy. "Ere heaven and earth took root" does not mean heaven and earth lacked a generative root; rather, heaven and earth were born from the formless. The Primordial Beginning’s true writ existed before the Three Thousand Great Worlds were established, before the beginning of kalpas. Thus, ere the root of heaven and earth’s division was seen, it flickered in and out of existence—present yet its form undefinable, absent yet its truth never extinguished.

The *Jade Emperor’s True Speech* and the *August Scripture’s* wondrous canon bring boundless compassion, enduring through kalpas without measure, pervading the Three Thousand Great Thousand Worlds without end. All heavens uphold it; the Three Teachings revere and follow it—it is the decree of the kalpa-turning dharma-realm.

The *Numinous Treasure Secret Scripts*, the celestial cloud-script, are not easily encountered or perceived, beyond conception or discourse, beyond the reach of thought or speech. Thus they came into being.

The true writ of the *Jade Scripture* existed before the kalpas—it did not arise only now, nor did it await the destined moment of its revelation. The Dao embraces the Great Void—what form could it have? Who could perceive it? Though present, none knew of its presence. Now, as the true Dao spreads its rightful course, the numinous writ reveals its secrets, its divine radiance shining forth in brilliance. Thus it is said to have come into being at this time. The presence of the true scripture’s wondrous dharma, meeting its destined moment, is a rare and fleeting occasion. Those who encounter this gathering—how could they bear to neglect it and not seek the teachings?

*Divine Incantations* chapter three:

Thus, heaven and earth received it and divided; the Three Luminaries received it and shone forth. The numinous writ flourished in splendor, illuminating the Highest Clarity, emanating from the Celestial Beginning of Azure, its colors unbounded, its patterns intricate and winding, difficult to trace in detail.

The Primordial Beginning refined it in the Cavern of Yang, forged it in the Courtyard of Flowing Fire. The resonant tones preceded its true text, its brilliance gleaming forth. As the Cavern of Yang’s qi was crimson, it was named the *Vermilion Script*. Once the numinous diagram shone forth, the Five Emperors paid homage to the true, soaring through the void, circling the Upper Palace, burning incense and scattering flowers, chanting the numinous verses.

At that time, heaven manifested twelve mysterious omens, earth produced twenty-four responses. Above, the Nine Heavens’ numinous mysteries were celebrated; the Three Heavens’ precious radiance was praised. The divine winds stirred, and the August Dao flowed unimpeded.

The Primordial Beginning issued the decree; the Perfected of Great Purity took up the brush. The Jade Consort swept the mat; gold was cast into tablets, jade carved into script. The Five Venerable Lords recorded it, sealing it in the Celestial Capital’s numinous palace. Jade maidens tended the incense; the Great Flower held the cloth. Golden lads stood guard; jade steps led to the celestial hall. The Nine Heavens’ jade script was not for ghosts or spirits to hear—only the true writ of the *Jade Scripture* and the *Numinous Treasure Secret Scripts* came into being at this time.

Thus, the Supreme Ultimate gave birth to the Two Modes: the pure floated to become Heaven, the turbid congealed to become Earth. Heaven and earth received it and divided. The sun’s brilliance shone, the moon displayed its splendor, the stars arrayed themselves—the Three Luminaries received it and shone forth.

The true scriptures and numinous writs, dense with their auspicious radiance and luminous qi, shone resplendently, illuminating the Upper Clarity’s realms. They emanated from the Primordial Azure’s supreme heavens, their hues unbound by fixed form or place. The radiant might of these numinous writs filled every winding path, their depths too profound for tracing or fathoming.

The Primordial Heavenly Worthy refined these true writs in the Cavernous Yang’s Double Mystery Hall, smelting this scripture in the Flowing Fire’s Great Brahmā Court. He purified their orthodox text, their brilliance boundless. He clarified their great, correct, wondrous, and existent writs, causing them to gleam and surge with luminous splendor. The Cavernous Yang’s wondrous qi overflowed with cinnabar radiance, purely crimson—thus named the *Crimson Writs*. The numinous destiny’s mysterious charts, now resplendent with light, drew the Five Thearchs to pay homage at the Origin. The Perfected rode clouds and auspicious omens, soaring through empty space, circling the supreme palaces in ritual procession. They burned the pure and spontaneous true incense, scattered celestial blossoms, and chanted the numinous writs’ precious chapters.

At that time, Heaven did not withhold the Dao, and the primal celestial bodies offered auspicious signs—twelve mysterious omens appeared in the heavens. Earth did not withhold its treasures, and the twenty-four qi manifested in their purest form, revealing twenty-four terrestrial responses. Above, the nine heavens’ numinous writs’ profound meanings were celebrated; the three heavens’ precious chapters were extolled. The wondrous canon shone brilliantly, its divine teachings spreading like the wind. The mechanism for delivering the world was set in motion, the imperial Dao flourished universally, and the great Dharma universally bestowed its blessings upon all.

The Primordial Heavenly Worthy ascended his throne and bestowed his mandate. The Supreme Perfected and transcendents held brushes to inscribe it. Jade consorts and numinous consorts swept the ritual mats. Indestructible golden light was cast into mysterious tablets and secret writs; azure jade’s mystic radiance was carved into cinnabar script. The Five Directions’ Five Numinous Ones and Five Venerable Lords recorded and transmitted it, sealing it in the Nine Heavens’ Supreme Numinous Mysterious Capital’s halls. Jade maidens tended the celestial incense; the Great Flower Perfected held the mystic cloth. Golden lads stood in attendance, guarding the jasper steps that led to the celestial halls. The Nine Heavens’ jade graphs and cinnabar script—these were not for any ghost or spirit to hear.

Only after Heaven and Earth existed did written characters come to be, and the scriptures were transmitted. Yet now it is said that the *August Scripture* existed before Heaven and Earth divided. Many who hear this grow doubtful and confused. Yet the Dao’s spontaneity, its ceaseless mutual succession, is what makes it true writ; the Dao’s indestructibility is what makes it true scripture. The Primordial existed before the kalpas’ vastness, and the *August Scripture*’s principle was already present. The true writ has no characters, its wondrous transformations are inexhaustible. Thus, Heaven and Earth divided from this, and the Three Luminaries shone forth from this. This is the true principle—what doubt remains?

The text’s winding structure has led some to misread characters as phonetic loans, but this is incorrect. The phrase "purified their orthodox text" has been misconstrued as "explained their orthodox text," but this is wrong. *Ying* (莹) is pronounced like *ying* (盈), not read as *xun* (巽) or *xin* (信). The mysterious scripture has no form—how could it be called "golden tablets"? Yet the mysterious light’s wondrous image endures beyond kalpas without destruction, hence it is called "golden tablets and jade script." The mysterious writ’s radiant auspiciousness, its lustrous dignity, is thus called "jade script." "Not for any ghost or spirit to hear"—the *August Scripture*’s profound mystery is unknown to ghosts and spirits, for it is not an ordinary hearing, nor an easy hearing, nor a hearing within the capacity of the common.

The *Divine Incantations* in four chapters:
Thus, Heaven treasures it to attain purity, Earth secretes it to attain tranquility, the Five Thearchs wield it to attain numinosity, the Three Luminaries ride it to attain brilliance, the supreme sages uphold it to attain the divine, the lofty spirits revere it to attain the true, the Five Marchmounts follow it to attain stability, the Son of Heaven obtains it to attain governance, and the dynastic mandate relies on it to attain peace. Truly, it is the wondrous power of the *Numinous Treasure*, the mysterious root of Heaven and Earth.

Its majestic numinosity is vast and boundless, universally bestowing its inexhaustible blessings. The great transformation is expansive and unobstructed, the origin of all divine luminaries. Its measure is unfathomable, towering like the great void. At that time, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy transformed the era of primordial chaos. Mystic images unfolded in the numinous charts; the numinous writs flourished in radiant splendor. They distinguished the workings of positions and transformations, manifesting the divine in the Five Directions—east, west, south, north, and center—dividing above as Heaven and below as Earth, opening and transforming the Dharma-realm’s myriad numinous beings and all species. This is the Double Mystery’s true and secret treasure—might one briefly glimpse its numinous essence through the imperial teachings, unfolding the supreme true and secret origin?

Thus, Heaven’s position is above, and by treasuring this true scripture, it attains the True One and achieves eternal purity. Earth’s position is below, and by secretly upholding this true scripture, it attains the True One and achieves eternal tranquility. The Five Directions’ Five Thearchs wield this secret writ to attain divine transformations and become the Five Numinous Ones. The sun, moon, and stars—the Three Luminaries—ride this true scripture’s wondrous Dharma to ascend in lofty brilliance. The supreme sages and perfected ones uphold this true scripture to attain a sageliness beyond comprehension and ascend in divine loftiness. The divine departments revere this true scripture to attain the true and sagely positions. The Five Marchmounts’ sacred thearchs, through this true scripture’s power, remain unshaken and attain secure stability. The Son of Heaven who rules all under Heaven obtains this true scripture’s wondrous Dharma to achieve governance without care. The nation’s mandate and enterprise rely on this true scripture to attain peaceful rule.

Truly, it is the wondrous power of the *Numinous Treasure*’s true origin, the mysterious root of Heaven and Earth’s true origin. This scripture’s celestial majesty and numinous efficacy are vast beyond measure, boundless and without limit. Across the kalpas’ vastness and the Dharma-realm, all benefits are inexhaustible. Universally bestowed without end, its transformations are vast and unobstructed, its merit and influence formless and boundless. Truly, it is the great and immeasurable divine transformation, the true origin of all divine luminaries—its merit and measure are beyond all reckoning. Without form or origin, towering and unattainable like the great void.

At that time, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy transformed the era of primordial chaos. Mystic light’s wondrous images unfolded the numinous charts; the numinous writs flourished in radiant splendor. They distinguished the workings of positions and transformations, manifesting the divine in the Five Directions—east, west, south, north, and center—dividing above as Heaven and below as Earth, opening and transforming the Dharma-realm’s myriad numinous beings and all species. This Double Mystery’s true and secret treasure—might one briefly glimpse its numinous essence through the imperial teachings, unfolding the supreme true and secret origin?

Unfolding—alternatively rendered as "perusing." The imperial scriptures are Daoist parlance, originally for cultivating and verifying immortal ranks, not for governing equitably or achieving universal peace. Yet here it speaks of the Son of Heaven attaining governance through them, and the nation’s fortune relying on them to achieve peace—why? For only when the Dao transforms and completes does governance and peace arise. Awakening to the true origin and illuminating the great Dao, one gains trust without speech, transformation without action, and accomplishment without striving. When virtue flourishes, its transformative power becomes divine, eternally benefiting all without limit. Thus it is said: governance is achieved, and governance is made equitable. Wondrous virtue is fundamentally without attainment, without visible bestowal, yet its transformative efficacy is boundless—hence it is called "wondrous virtue."

As for the Mystic Root: all roots possess form, yet when the Dao generates Heaven and Earth, though it encompasses the Limitless, the Supreme Ultimate’s diagram of the Two Modes (Heaven and Earth) originates from what is itself without form. The true cannot be seen, cannot be spoken, and diagrams are but provisional images to instruct people. What tangible form does the root of Heaven and Earth possess? Though without tangible form, its cyclical revolutions are inexhaustible—thus it is called the Mystic Root. Its numinous might: the sages and deities of the Three Teachings dare not slight it, for its wondrous transformations are boundless—hence it is called "numinous might." The origin of divine luminaries: all sages take it as their foundational method. It is also said: the thousand spirits and myriad sages emerge from this. The great void: its beginning unseen, its end unseen, indistinct and formless—hence it is called the great void. "Revolutionizing the era": some say it refers to the revolution of an ending era, but this is incorrect. This scripture existed before the vast kalpas, and thus it revolutionizes the era of primordial chaos.

"Manifesting the divine in the Five Directions": in primordial chaos, there was no distinction, yet the Dao’s wondrous transformations differentiated positions, distinguishing inner and outer—hence it is said "manifesting the divine in the Five Directions."

**Chapter Five of the Divine Incantations**
Now, as the imperial Dao flourishes and spreads, its blessings extend to the ten directions. Gazing upon the kalpic cycles and cosmic currents, the true wind of the Dao ought to be propagated. Your servant’s heart truly desires that the numinous shade of the Dao may reach the eight farthest reaches, its beneficent breeze perfuming the orchid groves, so that withered branches, long devoid of vitality, may lift their heads in hope of the luxuriance of the Southern Marchmount, and decayed remains may receive the life-giving moisture of the Dao’s profound and arcane teachings. The *Luminous Perfected* sets forth its standards—today, these must be enacted in the world. Looking up to the Primordial Compassion and prostrating below in sincere entreaty, I only pray for Your mercy to turn toward the teeming masses.

I wonder: might the *True Writs of the Numinous Treasure Jade Chapters* be granted for revelation, to be taught to those who have not yet heard? The treasure of the Mystic Origin—I hope to briefly glimpse its numinous essence. Now, as the great Dao spreads and flourishes, its compassionate grace permeates the four cardinal and four intermediate directions, reaching from the highest to the lowest, its blessings extending to the ten directions. Gazing upon the kalpic cycles and cosmic currents, the true wind of the proper Dao ought to be advanced. Your servant’s heart truly desires that the blessings of the Numinous Treasure Dharma may overshadow all worlds in every direction, reaching even the eight farthest reaches. May the Dao’s beneficent breeze and transformative grace bathe the orchid groves and fragrant jewel gardens. May all beings in the world—those mired in stagnation, adherents of heterodox paths, demonic and external cults, the sentient and insentient, those who have not heard the proper Dao—all receive the deliverance of the true scriptures. Like withered branches long devoid of vitality, may they lift their heads in hope of the warmth and moisture of the Southern Marchmount’s luxuriance, their withered forms revived and made flourishing. May decayed remains receive the life-giving moisture of the profound and arcane teachings of the sacred writs.
