Here, only after awakening does one enter the mountains to cultivate authenticity and study the Dao—thus, the gradations of the two traditions may be discerned. At times, those who study the Dao ascend heights and visit waters, traveling through sublime landscapes, gazing in all directions from the mountains. Wherever their eyes alight—whether upon mountains or forests, rivers, streams, ravines, or valleys (valleys being the deep, hollow, and vast gorges of mountains)—all sentient beings, all categories of life imbued with the intent of the great Creator, whether formed or formless (formed being those already born; formless, those not yet born—though some are born yet lack visible form), whether born from womb or egg, from moisture or transformation, crawling, flying, or hidden creatures—all beings stirred by the great Creation, moving or still, soaring high or lurking deep, those that walk between the flying and the hidden, every kind of creature—all their karmic offenses, past and present, are eradicated. Their bodies and minds become pure, free from entanglements, and at death, they all ascend to heaven.

If the mere gaze of a cultivator can deliver and save beings to such an extent, how much more so for one who receives and upholds this scripture? Know that the merit of such a person is boundless, the very treasury of the great Dao, immeasurable in its power—this is the embodiment of great merit and virtue. For those who study the Dao, their hearts are vast with compassion, and their benevolence knows no bounds. Though unseen and unheard, their minds cannot be perceived; yet wherever their gaze falls, all beings, moved by their intent to cherish life and recognize the dharma-nature in all, are silently spiritually delivered and rescued from the world. Thus, all are saved. Such is their merit.

The Confucian classics say: "Achieve the center and harmony, and the myriad things will be nurtured." They also speak of establishing a numinous terrace to observe vapors and omens, discern calamities and blessings, and harmoniously complete the myriad things, aiding and assisting their transformation. Where Heaven and Earth cannot reach, they enable beings to accept their lives and deaths in accord with the correct mandate, returning to the source of transformation—what karmic offenses could remain?

Those who praise Confucius say: "In his lifetime, his learning could not be exhausted; through generations, his depths could not be fathomed." That which is beyond knowing is called the divine. Now, in praising those who cultivate authenticity and study the Dao, we say: "the embodiment of the *Daozang*’s merit and power." This, too, speaks of that which is all-embracing, unfathomably profound, and beyond all praise. Only those who contemplate this scripture and attain realization will understand this meaning.

**Chapter 35 (Continued: Merits of Upholding the Scripture)**

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the Jade Emperor of the Void: "Now, I have briefly spoken, yet have not exhausted its wonders. If I were to expound at length, even after kalpas beyond count, the merits of this scripture for those of deluded views, doubts, and unbelief could not be fully expressed."

At that time—*see previous explanation*. The Heavenly Worthy is the Most High, the Primordial Beginning. *Addressed*—to speak to; the Primordial Beginning spoke to the Jade Emperor of the Luminous Void of Heaven. Another name is the Jade Emperor of the Mysterious Void of the Jade Clarity. *Now I have briefly spoken*—here, the Primordial Beginning refers to the time of expounding the scripture. *I*—the Primordial Beginning’s self-reference. *Briefly spoken*—to speak in broad strokes. *Not exhausted its wonders*—not fully expressed the essential wonders of the Dao and the supreme merits and virtues.

"Were I to expound at length, this scripture’s discourse on the merits of upholding it would extend to benefiting people and all beings, the living and the deceased, the formed and the formless, oneself and others, heaven and earth—truly vast in scope. Yet even so, were I to expound at length, the deluded and unbelieving would remain.

What is spoken of here encompasses the beings of this world, past and present, the enduring and the perished of heaven and earth, the three thousand great thousandfold worlds without measure, from kalpa to kalpa, kalpas beyond count, this future age, all future ages, from the beginning without beginning to the end without end—whether sentient or insentient, whether perceiving or unperceiving, whether conceivable or inconceivable, whether finite or infinite. All virtues reside within this scripture and those who uphold it. Were one to widely propagate and expound its wonders, still the deluded, those of perverse views, doubts, and unbelief—ordinary worldly folk and the vulgar masses—would persist."

As flowing water cannot rise above its source,
so too do perverse views—
views that are biased and crooked, not upright and grand.
Doubt arises when wisdom’s vision is incomplete,
when the mind wavers between two possibilities, undecided.
Delusion stirs from self-serving thoughts,
entangling the mind in confusion,
unable to discern right from wrong,
disordered and without fixed principle—
hence they do not believe this scripture holds boundless benefit.

The virtues of this scripture are beyond expression even across kalpas,
beyond enumeration even through measureless kalpas.
One might say its virtues are inexpressible even after exhausting all kalpas.
In essence, the Primordial Beginning endures eternally,
kalpas are without end,
the scripture’s merits are unfathomable,
and the Great Dao is immeasurable—
in the end, words cannot exhaust it.

The Great Dao is wordless,
the wondrous Dharma is imageless,
the true scripture is characterless.
What can be bestowed or received,
seen or heard,
spoken or attained—
these are but secondary meanings.

Thus, the Most High has transformed and given birth across measureless kalpas,
preached to the twelve thousand heavens,
traversed distant lands,
composed millions of scriptures.
In one transformation, a thousand seven hundred years,
he expounded the scripture over ninety thousand times,
yet still declared, “I know not its name,”
and only by force called it the Dao.

Confucius, who carried forward the past and inaugurated the future,
enlightening ten thousand ages,
said only, “I know nothing.”
Śākyamuni Buddha preached for forty-nine years,
held over three hundred assemblies,
composed the Tripitaka of scriptures, vinaya, and treatises,
yet said, “What I have now briefly expounded,
I lack the power to exhaust.”

Yan Hui, standing in noble solitude,
practiced fasting of the mind and sitting in forgetfulness,
and still said, “Though I wish to follow it,
I know not the way.”

This scripture is the root of the ten thousand Dharmas,
its virtues indeed inexpressible—
the supreme merit.
To speak of it is impossible.
Even if spoken,
people cannot comprehend it.

Thus, the Confucians’ governance through non-action,
the Daoists’ true and mysterious virtues,
the Buddhists’ offering of body and life,
the essential meaning of the Western teachings—
none can be transmitted through words.

How wondrous is the mastery of the wheelwright,
where the mind responds to the hand.
Zhuangzi, master of the Three Teachings,
thus left what lies beyond the six directions unspoken,
and did not discuss what lies within them—
not because he could not speak,
but because words easily give rise to delusion,
and silence is better.

This is the meaning behind the Master’s rare words on fate,
and why the nature of the Dao cannot be heard.

The Buddha spoke of many worlds and their appearances,
dividing matters and principles—
setting aside whether such claims are vast and baseless,
even if grounded in evidence,
much remains inexpressible.

Those who follow his teachings assume the Buddha spoke what others cannot,
mistakenly deeming it profound.
Yet the Buddha was born in foreign lands,
among strange customs and different peoples,
in remote and petty regions,
surrounded by multitudes.
The Śākya clan spoke of what they saw,
but China knew nothing of it.
Falsely, they claim the Buddha’s vision was vast.

Observe China:
within a hundred *li*, customs differ.
From Yan to Yue, from Tai to Qi,
the mountains, rivers, and winds of north and south—
those who have not traversed them cannot know.
How much less can the distant Western Regions be thoroughly examined?
Even with historical records,
they are but hearsay and miscellaneous notes—
who can guarantee their accuracy?

Many love the strange,
not investigating right from wrong.
If the Buddha truly knew all,
why did the scriptures he composed not originally enter China in Tang language,
but required three translations to become coherent?
Since he did not know the Tang language or script,
what he spoke must have been for his neighboring lands.
Perhaps, like Zhuangzi, he used parables to expound the Dao—
this too is possible.

Yet people, without careful examination,
erroneously judge high and low—
how excessive is their love of the strange!

Alas, to not speak of all realms
is to avoid deluding people.
To briefly speak of its transformative power
is to enlighten their ignorance,
reveal the true intent,
and manifest the true Dharma—
this is how the Dao brings real benefit.

Scholars must diligently investigate it.

*Chapter on Virtues, Continuation of the Thirty-Sixth*

At that time, the Jade Sovereign of the Void, having heard these words, was filled with joy and exultation beyond measure. Gazing upon the compassionate countenance of the Heavenly Worthy, he bowed in reverence and offered praise, reciting these verses:

Above the Nine Heavens lies the Great Veil,
Where jade capital and golden palaces stand,
Cloud-layers towering, majestic and grand.

Within resides the Heavenly Emperor,
Boundless in kindness, grace, and harmony,
Whose Way is matchless, subduing all demons.
Celestial treasures and sacred talismans,
Jade statutes and golden canons,
Countless immortals and divine banners.

Those who hear this name shall have their sins erased,
Forever freed from the river of desire.
He is called the Jade Emperor,
The True Ancient of the Vaulted Sky,
Perfect in subtlety, pure and clear,
Wisdom vast and eloquence profound.
The Way most supreme, the Honored One,
Teacher of the Three Realms,
Primal Ancestor of the Undifferentiated,
Unsurpassed Lord,
Compassionate Father of the Four Modes of Birth,
Exalted Sage of the Highest Heaven,
Greatly Kind and Benevolent One.

His ten titles complete,
Myriad virtues suffuse his being,
Limitless in delivering beings,
Lifting them from the suffering of birth and death.

When the Jade Sovereign of the Void had recited these verses and the ten titles, all the sages and divine hosts of the heavens, with one voice, marveled at what they had never before encountered. This speaks to the reverence and joy of receiving the scripture.

At the moment when the Heavenly Worthy concluded the chapter on the divine incantation’s virtues, the Jade Sovereign of the Void, having heard these words, was overcome with joy and exultation, his heart leaping with boundless delight. Gazing upon the compassionate countenance of the Jade Emperor, he bowed in reverence and offered verses of praise:

Above the Nine Heavens lies the Great Veil,
Where jade capital and golden palaces stand—
as previously described.
Cloud-layers towering, towering,
lofty and grand indeed.
The Great Veil’s golden palaces,
dharma-clouds and auspicious radiance,
layer upon boundless layer,
majestic and towering,
their vastness immeasurable.

Amidst rosy clouds, the jade capital’s palaces rise high and steep.
Within dwells the Heavenly Emperor,
the Jade Emperor, Lord of the Myriad Heavens.
Boundless in kindness, grace, and harmony—
his kindness is not mere favoritism,
but through kalpas of creation,
all beings are endowed,
nothing withheld, hence called kindness.
His Way and virtue are invincible,
subduing all demons.
Celestial treasures and sacred talismans—
the wondrous, mysterious talismans of the heavens.
Jade statutes and golden canons—
the celestial precepts and golden codes.
Countless immortals,
the divine hosts attending the throne,
hundreds of thousands of myriads,
with dharma-banners and jeweled standards as their retinue,
their numbers beyond measure.

Those who hear his name and the sound of the Dharma
shall have their sins wholly extinguished,
forever freed from the river of desire.
Of all karmic bonds of sentient beings,
none are harder to sever than attachment.
Through kalpas they drift and sink,
unable to escape at once.
To be forever freed from the river of desire
is to sever the roots of karma.

He is called the Jade Emperor—
as previously described.
The True Ancient of the Vaulted Sky—
the boundless vault of heaven,
the immeasurable azure expanse,
the True Ancient without beginning.
Perfect in subtlety, pure and clear—
wondrously complete, truly pure.
Wisdom vast and eloquence profound—
great wisdom, great discernment,
subtle eloquence, vast talent.
The Way most supreme, the Honored One—
the Way without limit, the Honored One without peer.
Teacher of the Three Realms—
the master of the realms of heaven, earth, and humanity.
Primal Ancestor of the Undifferentiated—
before the beginning, before heaven and earth divided,
before the world existed,
the Emperor’s true essence endured,
the true source through kalpas,
hence called the Primal Ancestor of the Undifferentiated.
Unsurpassed Lord—
of the Three Teachings and myriad Dharmas,
no sage can compare,
all acknowledge him as Lord,
hence called the Unsurpassed.
Compassionate Father of the Four Modes of Birth—
the four modes: womb-born, egg-born, moisture-born, and transformation-born.
All rely on the Emperor’s virtue to be born and to mature,
to have a good beginning and a good end,
all aided by the Dao,
hence called the Compassionate Father of the Four Modes of Birth.
Exalted Sage of the Highest Heaven—
among all heavens, none is higher than the Great Veil Heaven,
among all immortals and buddhas, none is more exalted than the Jade Emperor,
hence called the Exalted Sage of the Highest Heaven.
Greatly Kind and Benevolent One—
boundless in great kindness and great benevolence.

His ten titles complete—
from the Vaulted Sky to the Benevolent One, ten titles in all.
The Jade Emperor’s virtues and divine works
are thus perfectly complete and fulfilled.
Myriad virtues suffuse his being—
the Emperor’s virtues are boundless,
this is called "myriad virtues suffuse his being" as a concise expression.
Limitless in delivering beings,
lifting them from the suffering of birth and death.

At that time, when the Jade Sovereign of the Void had recited these verses and the ten titles, all the sages and divine hosts of the heavens, with one voice, marveled at what they had never before encountered. Having heard this wondrous Dharma and the sacred titles of supreme virtue—rarely met even through kalpas—the divine hosts together voiced their joy, for they had never witnessed such a marvel. Some say: in the world, nothing like this has ever been seen.

Such are the virtues and merits of the Emperor. Those who study this scripture shall awaken to true cultivation and not feel ashamed.

*Collected Annotations on the August Scripture, Volume Seven Concluded*
*Collected Annotations on the August Scripture, Volume Eight*
*Highest Scripture of the Jade Emperor’s Original Deeds, Volume Three*
*Chapter Four: Protection by Heavenly Perfected Ones*
*Chapter One of the Protection Section*

At that moment, the August Emperor of the Vast Heaven, having heard the scriptural Dharma expounded, rose from his seat and knelt reverently before the Jade Emperor, addressing him thus: "May the sagely compassion extend universally to the great assembly, to all the devas and humans, and to those who uphold this scripture, that the benefits of this teaching be proclaimed."

Thereupon, the Jade Emperor of the Most High, moved by expedient intent, opened the gate of beneficence, proclaimed the jade-casket precepts, and transmitted the numinous-treasure Dharma. He addressed the August Emperor of the Vast Heaven, saying: "Now listen carefully, and I shall expound for you the merits of receiving and upholding this scripture—the wondrous matters of aiding the imperiled, delivering the suffering, and benefiting both the living and the deceased."

The assembled Perfected Ones bowed their heads and spoke in unison: "Today, we are fortunate to hear the Dharma of serene and ever-abiding truth. Through its power, blessings shall ascend to all the heavens, pervade the Three Realms, and the sufferings of the Three Paths and Five Torments shall all be extinguished. We beseech your compassion to expound these wondrous principles for our sake."

After the divine hosts had extolled the merits of the divine incantations and the virtues of the Emperor’s sacred titles, the August Emperor of the Vast Heaven—also known as the August Emperor of the Vast, Lofty, and Mysterious Heaven (not merely the Vast Heaven of ordinary times)—heard the Heavenly Worthy expound the scriptural Dharma. Rising from his own seat, he knelt before the Jade Emperor and petitioned: "May the supreme sagely compassion extend universally to all in the great assembly"—or, as some say, to all the divine hosts who hear this scripture, or to the vast multitudes of the world (for though the heavens contain no mortals, this scripture broadly delivers the Three Realms through kalpas of tribulation; both interpretations are valid)—"and to all the devas and humans who uphold this scripture, that the benefits of this teaching be proclaimed in full."

Thereupon, the Jade Emperor of the Most High, moved by the sublime intent to deliver all beings, opened the gate of eternal and boundless beneficence, proclaimed the jade-casket precepts—this scripture being enshrined in jade tablets and precious caskets, treasured in the heavens—and transmitted the great Dharma of the Mysterious Numinous Treasure. He addressed the August Emperor of the Vast Heaven, saying: "Now listen carefully"—"you" refers to the August Emperor of the Vast Heaven, and "listen carefully" means to attend with single-minded clarity—"and I shall expound for you the merits of receiving and upholding this scripture: how it upholds all in peril, rescues all from suffering, and brings wondrous benefits to both the living and the dead."

The assembled Perfected Ones bowed their heads and spoke in unison: "Today, we are fortunate to hear the Dharma of serene and ever-abiding truth. The nature of humanity is inherently luminous, neither defiled nor pure, neither formed nor destroyed, neither ascending nor sinking, fundamentally serene and ever-abiding. Yet deluded by worldly entanglements, beings bring about their own ruin, drifting and sinking in the cycle of rebirth, blind and ignorant, unable to abide in serenity. Ghosts and spirits, though endowed with consciousness, when their retribution is exhausted, are reborn in turn and likewise cannot abide in serenity. Now, through the merits and benefits of hearing this scripture, our original nature is restored, the roots and dust are purified, karmic consciousness is uprooted, sins and obstacles are eradicated, and firmness and perfection are attained. To hear the Dharma of serene and ever-abiding truth is a rare encounter across ages—how could we not count ourselves fortunate? The power of this Dharma bestows blessings upon all the heavens and realms, pervading the Three Realms." (See previous explanations.)

The Three Paths: the celestial path, the terrestrial path, and the aquatic path. The Five Sufferings: suffering of the mind from the burden of form, suffering of the spirit from the burden of attachment, suffering of the body from the burden of greed, suffering of the soul from the burden of the self, and suffering of the essence from the allure of sensory realms—all are dissolved and extinguished.

We only pray that the Most Venerable One, in compassion and pity, may take mercy upon us. *Pity: to show compassion, sympathy, and care.* Expound these wondrous principles.

This scripture is the most sublime and wondrous Dharma, and thus possesses such merit and virtue. The August Heavenly Thearch, though not seeking its profound essence, requests its blessings—not to drink from another’s cup of grace. Every word and stroke of this scripture is an immeasurable Dharma treasure. To know its efficacy and uphold it with a true heart is to not betray the compassion of those who preach the scripture.

**Chapter Two of the Protective Upholding**

The Jade Emperor proclaimed: Should any being honor and support their parents, revere the Three Treasures, devote loyalty to their sovereign, refrain from killing or stealing, avoid licentiousness and jealousy, forsake anger and resentment, abandon arrogance and deceit, observe precepts and maintain purity, contemplate the Great Dao with a tranquil mind, and hold this scripture in reverence, I shall command the following:

Dispatch throughout the Dharma realms and transmit across the boundless worlds in the ten directions. Command the Eastern Emperor Lord of Azure Radiance, the Azure Rider, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Southeastern Great Emperor of Fusang, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Southern Great Emperor of Vermilion Mound, the Crimson Rider, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Southwestern Primordial Elder of Great Flower, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Western August Numinous Sovereign Elder, the White Rider, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Northwestern August Heavenly Thearch, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Northern Emperor Lord of Purple Tenuity, the Black Rider, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Northeastern Heavenly Lord of Impenetrable Void, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Supreme Heavenly Thearch of the Upper Realm, the Yellow Rider of Kunlun’s Ancient One, with his divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command the Heavenly Lord of Harmonious Advent from the Lower Realm, with the divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts of the famous mountains and grotto-heavens, to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

The Jade Emperor proclaimed: Upholding the scripture is not merely reciting it with the mouth. If any being in the world honors and serves their parents, reveres the Dao, scriptures, and masters of the Three Treasures, exhausts their strength and whole heart in utmost loyalty to their sovereign, refrains from killing, stealing, or licentiousness, forsakes jealousy, anger, resentment, arrogance, and deceit, receives and observes the pure and mysterious precepts of the Daoist canon, maintains true and proper fasting, avoids negligence and impatience, abides in tranquility and equanimity, silently follows nature, nurtures the spirit in stillness, models themselves after Heaven to solidify their true nature, contemplates the Great Dao with a profound mind, reveres the August Heaven as if it were present, and holds the Dao and its scriptures in esteem and veneration—

It is also said: One must cultivate strict reverence without carelessness, uphold, recite, and chant this scripture.

*I, the Jade Emperor, speak of myself. Read as "We."*

Then command the dispatch throughout all worlds and Dharma realms, transmitting across the boundless worlds in the ten directions. Command the Eastern Emperor Lord of Azure Radiance, the Azure Rider; the Southern Great Emperor of Vermilion Mound, the Crimson Rider; the Western August Numinous Sovereign Elder, the White Rider; the Northern Emperor Lord of Purple Tenuity, the Black Rider; and their divine immortals and celestial troops.

The Southeastern Great Emperor of Fusang, the Southwestern Primordial Elder of Great Flower, and the Northwestern August Heavenly Thearch belong to the Qian direction. The Northeastern Heavenly Lord of Impenetrable Void and the Supreme Heavenly Thearch of the Upper Realm—this is not the Celestial Thearch of the Curved Array, but the deity who governs Heaven. *The Buddha calls him the Heavenly Lord Śakra.* The Yellow Rider of Kunlun’s Ancient One and the Heavenly Lord of Harmonious Advent from the Lower Realm, along with the divine immortals, celestial troops, and innumerable hosts of the famous mountains and grotto-heavens, are all commanded to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

*To shield: to protect, cherish, and uphold.* Those who uphold the scripture respect and honor the words of the Emperor and the Dao, aligning their virtue with Heaven and the Dao to merge with the true. They embody the Great Dao. Where the Dao resides, both gods and humans revere it; thus, the Emperor commands the sacred hosts of the ten directions to shield them. Yet this applies only to those who are loyal, filial, reverent, and observe the precepts against killing, stealing, licentiousness, and deceit.

Upholding the scripture is rooted in virtuous conduct. Contemplate the Dao with a profound mind, and the Dao will naturally return to you. Some say that Daoists who leave the household do not draw near to sovereign or kin, deeming them disloyal and unfilial. Yet they do not understand that the mysterious precepts of the Daoist gate are most strict—those who observe and cultivate them dare not violate the precepts, lest they harm their bodies and shame their kin. With utmost sincerity and firmness, they first repay the Four Gratitudes. How could they ever forget their sovereign or kin, or fail in loyalty and filial piety? Thus, the Perfected Lord Xu permitted the *Scripture of Pure Brightness on Loyalty and Filial Piety* to reveal the true loyalty and filial piety of the Dao.

**Chapter Three of the Protective Upholding**

Command all Golden Immortals of the ten directions, the Four Assemblies, the Eight Divisions, and all their retinues to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command all Heavenly Perfected Great Sages, Flying Heavenly Divine Kings, the Three Officials, the Four Saints, the Two Luminaries, the Nine Stars, the Northern Dipper, the Southern Dipper, the Eastern Dipper, the Western Dipper, the Central Dipper, the Twenty-Eight Constellations, all the stars of the celestial sphere, the Vajra Warriors, the Divine Kings, and their respective hosts to descend and shield those who uphold this scripture.

Command all Golden Immortals of the ten directions across the worlds. The Golden Immortals are the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas. The Four Assemblies are not the Four Assemblies of the mundane world, but the Four Assemblies of yin-yang spirits, divine generals, and soldiers. The Eight Divisions are explained in the second fascicle. And their retinues refer to the kin and followers of the Four Assemblies and Eight Divisions. The Heavenly Perfected Great Sages of the ten directions are the Great Sages among the hosts of Perfected Ones in the ten directions. The Flying Heavenly Divine Kings are explained previously. The Three Officials are Heaven, Earth, and Water. The Four Saints are Heavenly Marshal Peng, Heavenly Marshal You, the Illustrious Sage, and the Protective Sage. The Two Luminaries are the sun and moon. The Nine Stars are Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, Earth, Moon Comet, Purple Qi, Rāhu, and Ketu. The Northern, Southern, Eastern, Western, and Central Dippers are the Five Dippers. The Twenty-Eight Constellations are Horn, Neck, Root, Chamber, Heart, Tail, Winnowing Basket, Dipper, Ox, Girl, Emptiness, Rooftop, Encampment, Wall, Straddler, Bond, Stomach, Mane, Net, Turtle Beak, Orion, Well, Ghost, Willow, Star, Spread, Wings, and Chariot, along with all the stars of the celestial sphere. The Vajra Warriors, Divine Kings, and their respective hosts are all the generals and their divisions. Each with their respective subordinates. Verification:

By imperial decree, this scripture is promulgated by the court’s command. The Three Dukes, Four Ministers, officials of the Two Capitals and Nine Courts, all functionaries and attendants, noble kinsmen and foreign clans, the myriad multitudes of black-haired people—none fail to revere and uphold it. Those who receive and maintain this Jade Scripture under the shelter of the host of spirits do so by imperial mandate to honor the worthy and assist the virtuous.

Within the human body reside the Three Origins, Four Symbols, Two Qi, Nine Palaces, Five Phases, and the degrees of the Twenty-Eight Constellations. The warp and weft of the celestial sphere, the waters and fires of true resolve, great wisdom, cultivation of conduct, vigorous practice, wondrous Dharma, and meritorious deeds—together with the host of spirits—constitute the entirety of a person. From the body’s hair and skin to its flesh, blood, and marrow; from its sinews and bones to its spirit and qi; from its essence and radiance to its meridians and collaterals, all serve to sustain our true qi of correct nature, wherein the treasure of life is preserved.

This true qi of correct nature is none other than the imperial true scripture. The thirty-six thousand spirits and qi, the eighty-four thousand luminous pores—these are the immortals and perfected beings of the ten directions, the Vajra Warriors, stellar deities, and divine kings with their legions. As the *Scripture of Disaster Dispelling* states: “There are hundreds of millions of celestial perfected beings and Vajra Warriors who guard and protect this scripture”—such is its meaning.

The scripture does not reside in words or written signs; its true import lies within our hearts. The spirits do not dwell in the ten-directional worlds but within our very selves.

To cultivate the heart and refine the body does not lie in recitation or perusal, but in silent operation with utmost sincerity, free from self-interest. When spirit, essence, and qi are whole, sageliness may be learned, Heaven may be aspired to, and the Dao may be entered—every movement shall be auspicious, and the spirits will surely protect one. If the Three Treasures are depleted and the One True [Nature] is lost, one’s own spirits wane and qi weakens, essence fails to flourish, and one falls into opposition with Heaven—how could the spirits protect such a one?

Alas, all are human: the noble one cultivates and meets with fortune, while the petty one rebels and meets with misfortune. Thus the scripture states: those who uphold and protect this scripture shall know that Heaven bestows blessings upon the virtuous. The imperial virtue is boundless, and the scripture’s benefits are supreme—it depends solely on how one reveres and receives it.

**Chapter on Protection and Upholding (IV)**
By imperial decree, the Vajra Warriors of Subduing Demons, the Four Heavenly Gate Kings, the deities of the Five Marchmounts and Four Waterways, all renowned mountains, the Four Seas and Nine Rivers, the Twelve River Sources, mountains and forests, rivers and marshes—all their lords and retinues—are commanded to shelter and protect those who receive and uphold this scripture, ensuring their safety in all perilous places.

By imperial decree, all local earth spirits, ditch and canal deities, and all mighty ghost kings are commanded to shelter and protect those who receive and uphold this scripture.

The Twelve River Sources are here recorded as thirteen names, for two waters share a single source—hence they are called the Twelve River Sources.

By imperial decree, the Demon-Subduing Kings and Heavenly Ding Warriors are commanded.

The Four Heavenly Gate Kings are the kings of the eastern, southern, western, and northern heavenly gates. The Five Marchmounts are Mount Tai in the east, Mount Heng in the south, Mount Hua in the west, Mount Heng in the north, and Mount Song in the center. The Four Waterways are the deities of the Yangtze, Yellow, Huai, and Ji Rivers. All renowned mountains in the world are included. The Four Seas are the eastern, western, southern, and northern seas. The Nine Rivers are the Yangzi, Qiantang, Hanshui, Xunyang, Huntong, Jinjiang, Xiangjiang, Wulong, and Yalu, along with all other rivers. The Twelve River Sources refer to the Yellow River as the world’s pulse—its origins include Kunlun, Yumen, Star Constellation Sea, Huodunnao’er, Weilu, and the sources of the Faxie River. Another account states that the Yellow River’s source at Kunlun has nine wells and seven springs, not merely twelve. The Twelve River Sources refer to Yu’s dredging of the Nine Rivers, along with the Ru, Han, Huai, and Si Rivers, totaling twelve. The Nine Rivers are the Tuhai, Taishi, Majia, Fufu, Husu, Jianjie, Goupan, Gejin, Ru, Han, Huai, and Si—these are the Twelve River Sources. The Yellow River is the general spirit of all rivers. Rivers such as the Jing, Wei, Yi, Wen, Zhen, Wei, Hutuo, Xingqia, Weak Water, and all others are its tributaries.

Mountains and forests encompass all in the world. Rivers and marshes encompass all in the world. Flowing waters are called *chuan*; marshes are watery expanses. "All lords" refers to the spirits presiding over mountains, forests, rivers, and marshes, along with their retinues, who shelter and protect those who receive and uphold this scripture. In all dangerous and treacherous places, they ensure safety and stability for those who uphold the scripture.

Wherever the imperial decree reaches, all local earth spirits and responsive numina, along with ditch and canal deities—where a ditch is a waterless channel, whether in mountains or earth, and a canal is a water-filled channel—and all other minor spirits, as well as all mighty ghost kings, are commanded to shelter and protect those who receive and uphold this scripture.

The scripture’s dharma decree is revered by all immortals, upheld by all buddhas, practiced by all heavens, venerated by all spirits, and recited by all people—even demonic forces submit of their own accord. Truly, mountains are thus stilled, waters thus flow long, and protection is thus strict. Since those who uphold the scripture are guarded by all spirits, how could they dare be negligent? A single lapse brings profound transgression and grave offense.

How well Confucius said: "The petty person does not know the Mandate of Heaven and thus does not stand in awe of it." To treat the great with familiarity, to mock the words of sages—such is the petty person. In viewing this scripture, one must still take warning and exert oneself.

**Chapter on Protection and Upholding (V)**

Let all demonic heresies be utterly subdued, their forms concealed and traces hidden, soaring high beyond the seas or fleeing far to other lands. Thus shall the spirits of mountains and forests, altars of the earth, and temple deities that partake of blood offerings all vanish of their own accord. The plague-bearing demon marshals of the five directions, all malevolent spirits, wind kings and water monsters, sinful dragons of karmic clamor, earth sprites and water specters—all shall dissolve away. The fivefold emptiness and sixfold depletion, disturbances in dreams, wild curses, hexes, and poisons—all shall dissipate on their own. For those who uphold this scripture, every desire of the heart shall be fulfilled, every wish granted in full.

*[Note: 慑 is pronounced "nie."]*

"Let all demonic heresies" refers to the command to subdue and eradicate them. "Demonic heresies" include heavenly demons, earthly demons, demon kings, demon folk, and demon women. "Heresies" encompass lewd doctrines, heterodox teachings, deviant practices, miscellaneous arts, and lesser techniques—such as the three thousand six hundred private methods, the ninety-six schools, and the thirty-six thousand varieties. "Let" signifies the imperial decree to suppress and eliminate them, ensuring all are thoroughly subdued.

All—this means entirely. *Nie* (慑) signifies awe and reverent submission. *Fu* (伏) denotes restraint and yielding compliance. They conceal their forms and flee their traces. *Qian* (潜) means to hide, concealing their shapes so they dare not appear. *Dun* (遁) means to evade, escaping their shadows so they dare not linger. Though the forms of these demons may outwardly seem enchanting, their illusions strangely beautiful, their true nature is obstructive and cannot be shown to others. The true methods of this scripture shatter the courage of ghosts and crush the hearts of demons; no demon can escape its scrutiny. Fearing the profound power of its divine teachings, they dare not remain, lest their foul essence be exposed. The words of heterodox teachings seek to confuse the truth. Yet when the true Dao is practiced, deviant doctrines fade; when the great Way is revered, lesser paths are abandoned. Once the imperial decree is proclaimed, none dare harbor them. They soar beyond the seas, their demonic ways leaving no trace—this may be described as "flying." But how can heterodox teachings "fly" upon entering the ear? They transform the heart and alter thoughts, turning toward the Dao and forgetting self-interest. "Soaring beyond the seas" is a common expression, akin to "the soul flying beyond the heavens" or "the spirit scattering to the nine skies." They flee to distant lands, daring not remain in their former abodes.

Thus, all spirits of mountains and forests, altars to earth and grain, shrines and temples, and those who partake of blood sacrifices shall dissipate on their own. *Mountains and forests*—explained previously. *She* (社) is the earth deity; *ji* (稷) is the grain deity. *Ci* (祠) means to administer or to sacrifice, where the spirit presides and is invoked in prayer. *Miao* (庙) means to attend, where spirits are honored in the temple with morning rites—those who receive offerings of blood and sacrificial wine. These are all spirits deemed worthy of worship, yet how can they be made to dissipate on their own? Spirits that demand sacrifices must be unjust; people who flatter spirits must be unrighteous.

Thus, Master Sa the Perfected subdued Marshal Wang Lingguan and reformed the forbidden city gods; when Ximen Bao governed Jizhou, he cast the witches into the river to restrain the river deity. How much more, then, when evil spirits falsely assume divine forms to delude people, and people revere such evil to deceive the world? When Hu Ying administered Guangdong, he destroyed illusory Buddhas, slew the serpent demon, and beat the monks to liberate the foolish masses from their delusions. Now, it is said that all ghosts and spirits shall dissipate on their own—those who uphold this scripture’s decree shall neither invite misfortune nor fortune, and shall dwell in peace, free from threats or clamor.

The plague-spreading demon marshals of the five directions, all malevolent ghosts and spirits—whether the fierce ghosts and overbearing deities of the world, the wind-controlling kings, the aquatic monsters, the violent dragons, the perverse and inauspicious spirits, the earth spirits and tree specters—shall all vanish of their own accord. The five deficiencies and six depletions—where the five viscera (spirit, qi, blood, and body) grow weak, and the six pulses decline—shall cease, along with disordered dreams and restless souls. Alternatively, the five deficiencies and six depletions refer to celestial omens like Heaven’s Wailing and Ruin, along with baleful stars such as Sangmen, Tai Sui, Great Depletion, Lesser Depletion, Fei Kang, Kong Wang, Yellow Pennant, Leopard’s Tail, Nine Fruits, Red Mouth, White Tongue, and the malevolent spirits of curses, oaths, hexes, and poisons—all such base practices, heterodox ways, incantations, and demonic speech, whether cursed or sworn, shall likewise dissipate.

For those who uphold this scripture with sincere devotion, all desires and aspirations shall be fulfilled as their hearts wish, without hindrance or opposition. The virtuous and those who walk the Dao command the reverence of ghosts and spirits, while all inauspicious and perverse forces are dispelled. Witness the death of the ominous mulberry, the expulsion of pestilence by the catalpa staff, the subduing of the flood dragon by Zheng Yang, the vanquishing of demons by the Celestial Master, and the binding of ghosts by the Sa Patriarch—all these bear clear testament. Alas, Wang Yanfang was a man of valor; even bandits, when sentenced to execution, dared not let Yanfang learn of their heterodox ways, for his virtue was as resounding as a bell.

Yet the three corpses, five burdens, seven emotions, six desires, and nine consciousnesses within a person—when these lower evils wreak havoc, they deceive one into failing to correct oneself, allowing perverse forces to persist and inauspicious influences to linger. If one can rectify their path, sever the three corpses, eliminate the five burdens, purge the emotions and desires, and expel the nine consciousnesses’ evils, then their personal aspirations shall be fulfilled, external perils shall vanish, and misfortune shall scatter while fortune arrives.

**Chapter on Upholding the Six Precepts**
Even those who cannot yet follow the ritual codes and observe fasts or jiao offerings may still uphold purity and precepts, maintain unwavering faith, and revere this scripture with devotion—such persons are equal to those who perform the fasts. Those who uphold pure precepts shall find their merit unimpeded, their virtue unobstructed, and they shall be called sages among men, their wisdom and power ever-renewed, akin to the perfected immortals.

For those who receive and uphold this scripture in accordance with the Dao, their merit shall be immeasurable. Even if one cannot yet follow the profound ritual codes and perform grand jiao offerings, so long as they maintain purity without defilement, uphold the precepts with single-minded devotion, and observe the Daoist commandments—whether the Five Precepts, Eight Precepts, Twelve Precepts (as appropriate), Eighteen Precepts, Twenty-Four Precepts, Thirty-Six Precepts, Seventy-Two Precepts, One Hundred Twenty Precepts, One Hundred Eighty Precepts, Three Hundred Great Precepts, or the Six Hundred Pure Precepts for female Daoists—if they focus their will, uphold these precepts with unwavering resolve, and revere this scripture with sincere faith, they shall be counted among those who perform the fasts. Those who uphold pure precepts in this way shall find their merit unimpeded.

Even those who cannot yet follow the ritual codes, perform fasts or jiao offerings, or maintain purity while revering the scriptures—if they can uphold purity, maintain single-minded faith, and revere this scripture with devotion—are all equal to those who perform the fasts and uphold pure precepts. The merit of those who cannot yet follow the ritual codes but perform fasts or jiao offerings, or those who revere the scriptures with purity, is the same. The gods shall respect and protect those who uphold these pure precepts.

Alternatively, if one maintains purity and single-minded devotion in upholding their precepts, their merit shall be unimpeded. "Unimpeded" means level and vast. If the heart is divided, merit cannot be genuine. If precepts are not upheld, merit is tarnished. When body and mind are pure, precepts are upheld with devotion, faith is sincere, the scripture is revered, the heart is undefiled, and resolve is unwavering—without deficiency or hindrance—then merit is true and naturally unimpeded. What obstacle could remain? They shall dwell in freedom and ease.

Human nature is born free and unconfined. Yet beset by worldly cares and material burdens, one toils in ceaseless hardship, no longer at ease—how can there be joy? With purity and right faith, free from material burdens, one attains great freedom, ever joyful and carefree. Such a one is called a sage among men—not merely a carefree person. With purity and right faith, rising above the common throng, they are called a sage among men. Their virtue and wisdom ever renew, cultivated with growing insight; transformation aligns with the heart, perception is true and wisdom profound, worldly burdens fade and true nature abides in clarity. Virtue daily renews, wisdom daily brightens—this is virtue and wisdom ever new. Together with the perfected ones—those of pure and right faith who uphold the scriptures and attain the Dao, the celestial perfected—such is the meaning of purity, precept-holding, single-minded devotion, reverence, and unwavering respect. Without thought of merit or intent to impress, one acts without ulterior motive, utterly free from pretense or interruption. This is what Confucius meant by "even in haste or during a meal, never deviating," and what the *Doctrine of the Mean* describes as "finding fulfillment in every circumstance." Zhuangzi expounded the essence of *carefree wandering*, Hai Chan composed the *Song of Joy*, Buddhism speaks of *great freedom*, and the Confucian classics speak of *daily renewal*—all are natural effects. How could they be borrowed or forced?

Alas! Purity and right faith, even without relying on ritual codes or performing fasts and jiao offerings, possess this natural merit. Thus, the profound teachings of the Dao lie in truly embodying the scriptures' meaning. Ritual codes and jiao offerings merely propagate the Dharma to spread the Dao’s transformation. Chen Tuan chanted the *Scripture of Salvation* and attained the Dao—this was truly upholding the scripture’s essence. Today’s jiao offerings lack evident efficacy because they possess grand rituals but no true cultivation. If purity and right faith are combined with jiao offerings, their merit is greatly enhanced. Without jiao offerings, true sincerity alone still yields divine merit. But without true sincerity, jiao offerings become mere formalities—how could they avoid fault?

**Chapter on Upholding the Sevenfold Merit**

At that time, the August Heavenly Emperor, having heard these words, bowed before the Emperor and chanted:

Great is the Supreme Dao, formless and nameless.
Vast through countless eons, the Yellow Dao opens in clarity.
Divine clarity shines radiant, the Nine Qi emit their essence.
Jade Void gleams pure, the Great Rosy Clouds rise in brilliance.
The Jade Emperor unfolds transformation, universally delivering heaven and humanity.
The Three Origins nurture the Dao, the Two Images embrace life.
Rotten trees and dead roots, once withered, are made to flourish.
All creatures that creep and breathe attain long life and transformed forms.
Those with child or in gestation all achieve birth and completion.
The dead, their fate expired, souls return to the Three Clarities;
their po spirits refined and delivered, ascend to the Southern Palace.
Today is most auspicious—all attain luminosity.
The Five Emperors reflect and illumine, universally proclaiming to the myriad spirits.
Heavenly gods and earthly deities, all river sources,
the Five Peaks and Four Waterways, all famous mountains,
Caverns of Mystery, Void, Emptiness, and Immortality—
the boundless Great Sage, the Most Perfect Honored Deities,
limitless and infinite, universally oversee deliverance.
Evil roots severed, names recorded in the Mystic Capital.
The assembled perfected array, heed the Emperor’s words.
This scripture is the Emperor’s decree: those who recite and uphold it
shall reach the Dao’s shore, untouched by calamity.
By the Emperor’s command, all shall obey.

At that time—referring to the aforementioned merits of upholding—
the August Heavenly Emperor, having heard these words, bowed before the Jade Emperor and chanted in praise:

Great is the Supreme Dao, measureless and unattainable.
Formless and nameless, unseen and unheard—even its name is but a forced designation.
Vast through countless eons, without beginning or end,
through innumerable kalpas—"a hundred thousand" is called *yi*, but this merely denotes vast numbers, for in truth they are without count.
The Yellow Dao opens in clarity, an auspicious time of celestial harmony.
Divine clarity shines radiant, the divine wind eternally pure, luminous and bright.
The Nine Qi emit their essence—the Nine Qi of Fusion, Flame, Evolution, Vastness, Radiance, Dao, Chaos, Cavern, and Vastness.
As the Yellow Dao opens and inauspicious omens dissolve, the Nine Qi display their brilliance, emitting their essence in wondrous splendor.
Jade Void gleams pure—jade light, empty and bright, serene in its clarity (or: the Heaven of Jade Void shines radiant).
The Great Rosy Clouds rise in brilliance, the Great Mystery’s rosy glow, supremely high and luminous.
The Jade Emperor unfolds transformation, opening and delivering through teaching.
Universally delivering heaven and humanity—*pu* means "all-encompassing," delivering all beings between heaven and earth.
The Three Origins nurture the Dao—heaven’s birth, earth’s completion, and humanity’s cultivation are the Three Origins’ nurturing of the Dao.
The Two Images embrace life—Qian and Kun’s creation, the generation of all things.
From beginning to end, they govern and shape—thus called the Two Images embracing life.
(Alternatively: Yin and Yang’s molding is the Two Images embracing life—both are correct.)
Rotten trees and dead roots—*xiu* means "decayed," *gu* means "dead."
Once withered, made to flourish—*ku* means "dried up," once desiccated, made to bloom anew.
All creatures that creep and breathe, long life and transformed forms—
flying, crawling, and creeping beings, none die prematurely, all transcend their original forms.
Those with child or in gestation all achieve birth and completion—
all beings in gestation, unharmed and unfallen, all attain peaceful growth and fulfillment.
The dead, their fate expired, souls return to the Three Clarities—
the deceased, spared the underworld, all return to heaven.
Their po spirits refined and delivered, ascend to the Southern Palace—
the seven po of the dead refined by the Great Compassionate Perfected, their souls and spirits ascend to the Southern Palace.
Today is most auspicious—referring to the time of the scripture’s recitation.
All attain luminosity—all beings are saved, darkness dispelled by light.
The Five Emperors reflect and illumine—the Five Emperors of the Five Directions observe and shine.
Universally proclaiming to the myriad spirits—
heavenly gods and earthly deities, all river sources,
the Five Peaks and Four Waterways, all famous mountains,
Caverns of Mystery, Void, Emptiness, and Immortality—
the vast and empty caverns, all immortal emperors, gods, and buddhas, and ghostly generals.

The Boundless Great Sage, the Most Perfect and Revered Divinity—
limitless, boundless, measureless in extent.
Universally overseeing the salvation of beings, pervading all to observe and descend,
transforming and delivering the multitudes of living things.
Severing the roots of evil, forever eradicating the wicked roots of humans and all beings.
Inscribed in the Mystic Capital, on the Cinnabar Terrace of the Mystic Capital, recording merits and virtuous names.
The assembled perfected ones arrayed in ranks, attending in ordered rows.
All heed the words of the Jade Emperor—these are the words of the Jade Emperor.
This scripture is the Jade Emperor’s decree.
Protecting those who recite and uphold it, safeguarding those who recite and maintain the scriptural dharma.
Attaining the shore of the Dao, ascending to the shore of the Dao.
Preventing all calamities from encroaching, ensuring no disasters assail.
I bear the Emperor’s mandate, carrying out the Jade Emperor’s command.
All heed in reverence—all humans, beings, ghosts, and spirits obey.
Herein lies the merit of the entire scripture.

**Chapter Eight: Protection and Upholding**

At that time, the August Heavenly Thearch, having spoken these verses, addressed the great assembly, saying: These are the wondrous dharma-words of the Jade Emperor, the secret and arcane utterances of all the sages. The path is severed, the Dao cut off—subtle and profound beyond thought, majestic and vast in scope, the foundation of all divine luminaries. It safeguards and stabilizes the realm, delivering beings from birth and death.

When the August Heavenly Thearch had finished speaking these words, the pure assembly of the dharma gathering all gazed upward toward the Dao’s discourse, universally attaining enlightenment.

At that time, the August Heavenly Thearch bowed in reverence and extolled the Jade Emperor. Having recited the verses, he addressed the assembled host of celestial immortals, perfected beings, divine generals, and all others, saying: These are the wondrous dharma-words of the Jade Emperor.

All the immortal sages possess their own dharma-words—vast yet measurable, transmitted within limits. Some may know their beginning and end; some benefit the living but neglect the dead; some aid humans but forsake other beings; some are recognized by ghosts and spirits, while others fail to subdue demons and malevolent forces. Some remain formless and unknowing, unable to universally deliver—none are wondrous or sublime.

Yet the transformative power of this scripture is infinite, its majesty and benefit immeasurable. All receive its blessings—it is no ordinary teaching. These are the wondrous dharma-words of the Jade Emperor, the secret and arcane utterances of all the perfected sages.

When the Primordial Beginning expounded this scripture, how could it be said that all the sages and most perfected ones who heard and received it did not treasure it, daring not to lightly disclose it? Thus it is called the "secret of all the sages," the "arcane words." The path is severed, the Dao cut off—this is the supreme vehicle. The dharma is rarely heard, the essential path of cultivating the real, the circuit of entering sagehood. Illusory desires and false thoughts—here, their roots are plucked. Love, attachments, and mundane thoughts—no longer sprout or spread. The cycles of rebirth and transmigration—severed in one stroke. Thus it is said: the path is severed, the Dao cut off. Another version states: the Seven Sages are all deluded, and this is a path humans find difficult to tread—this is also true.

Subtle and profound beyond thought—deep, mysterious, and wondrous. The divine cannot be grasped by thought, nor entered through contemplation. The human mind’s reflections cannot easily reach it. Majestic and towering, the wondrous model of immortal verses, the true seal of the divine luminaries’ hearts. Another interpretation: the Jade Emperor’s Dao is the model, the ancestral teacher of all divine luminaries. This is too restrictive.

It safeguards and stabilizes the realm, delivering beings from birth and death.

At that time, the August Heavenly Thearch, having spoken these wondrous dharma-words up to the phrase "delivering from birth and death,"—the dharma gathering, the flower-adorned assembly; the pure assembly, the assembly of pure and sacred beings—all gazed upward toward the Dao’s discourse. Or, some take it as gazing upward toward the wondrous dharma-words of the August Heavenly Thearch. Universally attaining enlightenment, all achieved awakening.

**Verification:**
The Master’s words on human nature and the Dao of Heaven cannot be heard. The *Wenshi Jing* states: "Sages and the wise create delusion; even ghosts and spirits do not comprehend." When the Buddha expounded the dharma on Vulture Peak, the bodhisattvas listened with rapt attention. The Jade Emperor’s dharma-words—severed path, cut-off Dao, subtle and profound beyond thought—what doubt can there be? As the foundation of all divine luminaries, stabilizing the realm and delivering beings from birth and death—these are its natural effects.

**Resolving Doubts:**
There are no people beyond the Dao in the world, nor is there a Dao beyond people. Humans, beings, the hidden and the manifest—all are the Dao. Human nature is wholly real; all things are complete within it. All transformations and nurturing, the world’s beginning and end—all are the reality of our nature. The Jade Emperor is the embodiment of the Dao; the scripture is the Dao’s intent. Only the Dao achieves complete spiritual transformation, its wondrous essence naturally so. Humans share the same nature—how could they not uphold this scripture? Knowing the Dao resides within, embodying the Dao with a single heart, generation after generation without duality—then the perfected sages are within me.

**Chapter Nine: Protection and Upholding**

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy spoke in verse:

The Jade Emperor’s merit is vast,
the profound principle most abstruse.
Born before the kalpas’ expanse,
its transformations span past and present.

I now expound this wondrous scripture,
compassionately mindful of all sentient beings.
This is the most sublime dharma,
the merit among merits.

Its name is the supreme vehicle,
incomparable, the first of all.
The Great Radiant King of Light,
whose majesty and virtue are rare in the world.

It can shatter violent demons,
subduing all their hearts.
It can eradicate the gravest sins,
rendering all pure and immaculate.

If one hears this scripture,
or hears the Jade Emperor’s wondrous name,
bows in reverence with devotion,
all sins are extinguished.

The ten evils and four grave offenses,
the five rebellions against parents—
with sincere faith, upon uttering the name,
all vanish with the sound.

It protects the hosts of humans and devas,
the four signs and five declines,
the extreme sufferings of the three paths,
the mundane calamities of humans—
famine, plague, and bereavement in inauspicious years,
poisons, nightmares, and malevolent spirits,
imprisonment, enmity, and grudges,
the agonies of war and battle,
perils in mountains and forests, on treacherous paths,
among tigers, leopards, jackals, and wolves,
the venomous dragons of the crimson sea,
fierce thunder, wind, rain, and hail,
fire, flood, and bandits,
gu poison gnawing at the heart and belly,
loss of reason, madness, and delirium,
snakes, scorpions, and noxious creatures,
malevolent spirits and monstrous demons,
those lurking to exploit human weakness—
by upholding this true scripture,
all scatter and vanish of themselves.

Vexing illnesses, long-entrenched,
disturbing dreams and restless sleep,
unjust desires that waste life,
annihilation without misfortune—
through encountering this scripture,
one attains peace, stability, and freedom.

All cherished wishes—
wealth, treasure, and prosperity—
through the merit of this scripture,
are fulfilled as desired.

The immortals of divine might and freedom,
the Eleven Luminaries of the heavens,
the lords of the Thirty-Two Heavens,
the stars of the Twenty-Eight Constellations,
the spirit maidens and jade women,
the celestial deities and earthly spirits,
the gods of the Three Realms and empty space,
the dragon kings of rivers and seas,
the spirits of water, fire, and wind,
the guardians of palaces and dwellings,
the deities of mountains, forests, and trees,
the gods of ditches, wells, and springs—
by upholding this scripture,
all gather to protect and shield.

Clothing and food come naturally,
descendants attain wealth and nobility.
One’s words are rare to hear,
and wherever one goes, all show reverence.

Should one seek sons or daughters,
by reciting this true scripture,
an imperial decree descends from the celestial courts,
and a celestial immortal, demoted from heaven,
is born into the household
as a son or daughter.

They bring honor and esteem to the family,
and the seven generations of ancestors ascend.
The household shines with glory,
extending to father and mother.
Auspiciousness ever flourishes,
and calamities cannot intrude.

Therefore, I now proclaim—
let all listen attentively.
With compassion, I ferry all beings,
that they may reach the Supreme Clarity.

The sound of the ordinary concludes.
Thus, the Dharma assembly awakens the pure multitude,
and the Primordial Heavenly Worthy of Origin spoke in verse:

The Jade Emperor’s virtue is vast,
his profound principles exceedingly deep.
Born before the great kalpas,
he transforms through past and present.

I, the Primordial Origin, now expound this wondrous scripture,
moved by compassion for all sentient beings.
Among all meritorious deeds, this is the supreme merit,
an unparalleled wondrous Dharma,
the foremost mystery.

The Venerable King of Great Luminosity,
boundless in radiance,
the Awakened King, most exalted.
His awe-inspiring virtue is rare in the world,
his mysterious power and wondrous virtue
unmatched in the realm of existence.

The Ten Evils and Four Grave Offenses—
the Four Grave Offenses are:
first, demon, hell, ghost, and beast;
second, struck by lightning, plague, bandits, and imprisonment;
third, the Five Acts of Betrayal against parents.
Mencius spoke of the Five Unfilial Acts:
laziness of the four limbs, gambling and drinking,
coveting wealth, favoring wife and children,
following the desires of the ears and eyes,
bringing disgrace to parents,
pursuing bravery and violence,
endangering parents.
Fourth, irreverence, lack of faith, disobedience, and disregard for ritual—these are the Five Transgressions.
With a single invocation of the Emperor’s name,
sins vanish with the sound.

The Five Decays:
the pearl crown shatters, the body bends,
the head bows, the eyes weep,
the nose drips, the body loses its light,
heavenly robes fray, the shadow is exposed,
and the spirit’s movement is no longer free.
These are the encounters of fate’s cycles.
*Ke-jia*: the meeting of past karmic conditions.
*Xun*: swift as thunder.
*Hao*: hail, the icy rain.
*Si*: lurking in darkness to exploit human weakness.
Those who harm themselves through irrational desires—
annihilation and cessation, yet no misfortune befalls.
The lords of the Thirty-Two Heavens of the four directions—east, west, south, and north.
The words of the scripture’s upholder are profound and wondrous, rare to hear,
and wherever they go, people revere them wholeheartedly.
The Seven Ancestors: father, grandfather, great-grandfather, great-great-grandfather,
the ancestor of the lineage branch, the ancestor who founded the grove, and the ancestor who established the surname.
*Chi-sheng*: great brilliance and glory.
With compassion, I ferry all beings,
that they may reach the Supreme Clarity, the Great Luo Realm.

This verse by the Primordial Origin extols the merits of the Jade Emperor’s Jade Scripture,
urging all to revere and uphold it.

**Chapter Ten: Protection and Upholding**

Then, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the four assemblies:
All who uphold and recite this scripture,
who receive and chant the Emperor’s name,
possess deep roots in the Dao and heavy karmic affinities from past lives.
This scripture is exalted and wondrous,
universally ferrying gods and humans.
Simply devote the heart with reverence,
and the household and nation will know peace,
life will be preserved, disasters averted,
and inauspiciousness swept away.
Should emperors, kings, or nobles embrace it,
their lands will know great peace,
hostile foes will submit,
borderlands will know no strife,
the people will sing in joy,
and all under heaven will prosper.
As fate’s cycles turn, the true Dao shall prevail.
Those who attain it are revered by celestial immortals.
Treasure it, keep it secret.

Then, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy addressed the four assemblies:
All in the world who uphold and recite this scripture,
who receive and chant the precious name of the Jade Emperor,
possess deep roots in the Dao—what the Confucians call "clear and abundant endowment,"
what the Buddhists call "excellent karmic capacity."
They bear heavy affinities from past lives,
having broadly cultivated hidden virtue in former kalpas,
and thus possess good predestined connections.
For the supreme Dao is rarely heard,
Dharma assemblies are rarely encountered,
and auspicious kalpas are rarely met.
Some pass through lifetimes without hearing the true Dharma;
others hear but do not believe or awaken,
failing to fully comprehend or receive its true benefits.
All this stems from shallow karmic capacity and thin predestined affinity.
Now, having encountered this Dharma assembly,
hearing the true Dharma and receiving its true benefits,
they have cultivated through kalpas,
possessing deep roots in the Dao and heavy affinities from past lives.
This scripture is exalted and wondrous,
universally ferrying gods and humans.
Simply devote the heart to its reverent veneration,
and with utmost sincerity and respect,
upholding this scripture,
the household and nation will know peace,
life will be preserved, disasters averted,
life prolonged, and calamities dispelled.
Since ancient times, sages and worthies have been born and have died,
disasters and misfortunes ever present—
how then can one speak of preserving life and averting disaster?
It means preserving the Mandate of Heaven and maintaining the upright qi,
remaining composed amid long-standing trials,
living in accord and dying in peace,
unmoved by fortune or misfortune—
such is the preservation of life and averting of disaster through upholding the scripture.
Sweeping away inauspiciousness,
where the scripture’s Dharma abides,
misfortunes silently vanish;
the virtuous receive celestial aid,
disasters are forever dispelled,
and nothing inauspicious remains.
Emperors, kings, and nobles—
the ruler of all under heaven is called the Son of Heaven, the August, the Emperor;
in the Zhou, he was called the King.
In recent times, those enfeoffed as lords of a state are called kings,
while those granted hereditary office are called nobles.
In ancient times, nobles were enfeoffed with a hundred *li*.
Those who receive and uphold this scripture
will bring their nations to enjoy great peace,
and hostile foes will be subdued.
"Subdued" means pacified.
When a state is well-governed,
internally ordered and externally majestic,
evildoers and bandits do not arise,
naturally subdued and pacified.
The four barbarians come to submit,
all under heaven is at peace,
and borderlands do not wage war.
The multitudes of the people
sing and rejoice in the peace.
All under heaven prospers,
abundant and secure.
As fate’s cycles turn,
the era of the True Origin unfolds,
the reckoning of time completes a full cycle,
and the true Dao shall prevail in the world.
Those who attain the scripture’s Dharma
and the wondrously transformative Dao
are revered by celestial immortals.
Treasure it, keep it secret.
This scripture is exalted and sacred—
treasuring it is fitting.
Yet if it universally ferries gods and humans,
why speak of keeping it secret?
Would this not privatize the Heavenly Dao?
Though the great Dao universally saves,
it must not be lightly transmitted to the faithless.
The Buddha’s Treasury of the True Dharma Eye
is not indiscriminately shown to others.
Confucius said:
"Those below the middle cannot be spoken to of higher things."
True understanding must arise from inner awakening.
To treat it lightly is to profane the Heavenly.
The scripture says to keep it secret—
readers, take heed and comprehend its meaning.

---

**Fifth Chapter: Responses and Verifications**
**Eleven Additional Verses on Verifications**

At that time, the Perceiver of Misery’s Cries Who Delivers from Calamity,
the Seeker of Voices Who Rescues from Suffering,
the Life-Saving Death-Transcending Perfected,
and the Myriad Blessings Body-Protecting Perfected
all rose from their seats, stepped beyond their ranks, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy:
If in the latter ages, ordinary beings,
though possessing good affinities from past lives
and encountering this scripture,
are obstructed by various demonic hindrances,
doubting its origins and ends,
and do not believe in the scripture’s power—
what karmic retribution will such persons receive
in the present and future,
in the hells of all realms?

At that time, the Perceiver of Misery’s Cries Who Delivers from Calamity,
the Seeker of Voices Who Rescues from Suffering,
the Life-Saving Death-Transcending Perfected,
and the Myriad Blessings Body-Protecting Perfected
all rose from their seats, stepped beyond the ranks of the divine assembly,
and addressed the Primordial Heavenly Worthy:
If in the latter ages, ordinary beings,
though possessing good affinities from past lives
and encountering this scripture,
are obstructed by various demonic hindrances—
their own perverse views, others’ misleading teachings,
stubborn and deluded natures,
obstacles of circumstance and principle,
all manner of obstructions—
doubting its origins and ends,
initially unable to believe,
later unable to awaken,
clashing above and below,
unable to harmonize,
failing to fully comprehend from beginning to end,
doubting the scripture’s power—
what karmic retribution will such persons receive
in the present and future,
in this life and the next,
in the hells of all realms?
We beseech the Heavenly Worthy of Sagely Compassion
to expound the sufferings of their karmic retribution in the evil destinies.

Beings’ karmic consciousnesses
each follow their own inclinations.
Some good, some evil,
they sink in the wheel, difficult to escape.
The Great Sage and Perfect Truth
dissolves past habits,
uproots the dust of the senses,
purifies karmic consciousness,
severs all destinies,
dispels all obstructions and attachments,
and is not subject to rebirth,
free from all karmic retribution.
Great worthies, bodhisattvas,
lesser immortals and sages,
divine generals and spirits—
the good take cultivating blessings as their path,
the evil take creating karma as their path.
The good need not be discussed;
the evil sink into karmic prisons,
their retributions manifold,
with no way out, no means of escape.
When their retribution is exhausted, they are reborn,
leaving one state to enter another,
entangled by karmic affinities,
again deluded and unawakened,
endlessly cycling through kalpas,
perpetually repeating.
Such karmic destinies
are truly pitiable.
The four Perfected beseech the Heavenly Worthy
to expound the sufferings of their karmic retribution in the evil destinies—
so earnest is their compassionate desire to deliver the world.

Both teachings speak of karmic retribution,
though Confucians deem it otherwise.
*Tai Jia* says:
"Heaven’s calamities may yet be avoided;
self-inflicted calamities cannot be lived through."
The *Commentary* states:
"Virtue brings blessing, excess brings misfortune."
It also says:
"The response between heaven and humans
is swifter than an echo."
How could they not speak of karmic retribution?
The Master said:
"The noble person is mindful of punishment."
He also said:
"Revere the Mandate of Heaven."
Thus, one naturally refrains from evil.
Delighting in the Dao and virtue,
one is free from other destinies.
Through the ages, in village drinking ceremonies and archery rites,
laws and ordinances were read aloud,
instructing the multitudes—
only to correct their conduct, not their hearts,
and guide them toward goodness.

The two teachings speak of karmic retribution and penal suffering for no other purpose than to extricate beings from their karmic destinies and guide them toward supreme goodness. Alas! Only the sage, through the numinous Way of education, brings the multitudes to submission. The Jade Emperor’s virtue and power are supreme, and thus the scriptures clearly reveal karmic retribution to deliver beings from evil destinies—not to deceive the masses. If one does not cultivate the truth but merely dazzles others with talk of fortune and misfortune, this is deceit.

Those who study the scriptures must sever desire to attain the real, escape the personal hell of evil, and only then may they save the world and deliver others.

**Chapter on Verification of Responses, Continued (Chapter Twelve)**

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the Four Perfected Ones, saying: "Among all the beings of the world—those who are stubborn, violent, and evil, the unvirtuous—who spend their days and nights before the images of the Dao, yet harbor no reverence in their hearts and utter slanderous words, such sins condemn them to the Five Uninterrupted Hells. If, however, they encounter one who upholds this scripture and employ various expedient means to guide and instruct them, such persons may extinguish their evil minds, believe in and turn toward this scripture, and their karmic offenses will be entirely purified without remainder."

At that time, the Most High Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Beginning addressed the Four Perfected Ones—Compassionate Deliverance from Suffering and the others—saying: "Among all the beings of the world—those who are stubborn, violent, and fierce, whose nature is bold and conduct coarse, the unvirtuous, whose words and deeds are wicked—who spend their days and nights (here, *jing* means ‘end,’ ‘exhaust’; they exhaust day and exhaust night) before the images of the Dao and the sacred likenesses of the gods, yet harbor no reverence in their hearts and utter slanderous words (*fei*: to criticize with words; *bang*: to defame with words), thus showing disrespect to the images of the Dao and slandering the sacred—such sins condemn them to the Five Uninterrupted Hells, the great hells of the netherworld. Without the methods of the sage, they inevitably fall into this retribution. Observe the laws of the world that punish those who slander heretical teachings, and you will understand the gravity of slandering the gods.

"If they encounter one who upholds this scripture (here, *zhi yu* means that at that time, they happen to meet), who employs various expedient methods of salvation to guide and instruct them—those who slander the gods and revile the Dharma, whose karmic roots are deep and heavy, who are obstinately deluded and lack faith—the upholder of the scripture, with great compassion and expedient means, awakens, guides, and transforms them, revealing their innate goodness and arousing their virtuous thoughts. Thus, those who slander the gods and revile the Dharma may extinguish all their evil minds, believe in and turn toward this scripture, take refuge with sincere faith, and devote themselves to it. Their karmic offenses (here, *bi* refers to those who slander the gods and revile the Dharma) will be entirely purified without remainder. As their karma dissolves and their sins vanish, all retribution is exhausted, and they are forever freed from transgression, never to return. Constantly pure and clean, their evil retribution is permanently removed, and no unresolved karma remains. Even in the Uninterrupted Hell, where karma is difficult to dissolve, if one wholeheartedly believes in and turns toward the true scripture, evil roots are severed at once, all defilements are extinguished, and what fetters remain? With roots and defilements instantly eradicated, karma is purified without remainder.

The virtue of the gods and the merit of the scriptures bring the greatest benefit. Both teachings emphatically speak of sin and blessing, earnestly revealing the gravity of the sin of disrespecting the gods and slandering the Dharma. Confucians likewise warn against flattery and irreverence toward the spirits—how could Confucians fail to revere the gods or honor the scriptures? The *Book of Songs* says: *"Do not disgrace those who gave you life."* Master Zhang said: *"To feel no shame in the solitude of one’s chamber is to not disgrace one’s origins."* He also said: *"To preserve the mind and nurture one’s nature is to be unwavering."* Both teachings speak of revering the gods and honoring the scriptures to cultivate the mind and practice the Dao, feeling no shame before heaven, earth, and the gods, believing in the words of the Dharma, and embodying the Dao to attain the real.

Confucians speak of not flattering the gods to caution against seeking blessings through irreverence. Serving Heaven, revering Heaven, aspiring to Heaven, honoring the words of the former kings, responding with reverent haste—Confucianism and the two teachings are one in this. If sacrifices bring no benefit and reverence is not practiced, if the Mandate of Heaven is not feared, these are corrupt words. Confucians also sternly reprove such views—how could this apply only to the two teachings?

Alas! Good and evil, reverence and negligence—all arise from the mind. If one severs desire, relinquishes cunning knowledge, empties the five aggregates, and removes the five burdens, then one is no longer bound by the five phases. Heaven and earth cannot restrain them, so how could the Five Uninterrupted Hells ensnare them? The Buddha said: *"By reciting the Buddha’s name, fire pits transform into lotus ponds."* Mencius said: *"Recite the words of Yao and practice the deeds of Yao, and you are Yao."* Thus, the true efficacy of goodness is immediately manifest.

*Collected Commentaries on the August Scripture, Volume Eight* concludes.
*Collected Commentaries on the August Scripture, Volume Nine* begins.

**Chapter on Verification, Continuation of Chapter Thirteen**

Moreover, if there are wicked and foolish men of perverse views and obstinate delusion who, upon seeing one upholding this scripture, give rise to all manner of evil and rebellion—casting sidelong, crooked glances, or even harboring a single malicious thought, uttering a single wicked word, and recklessly slandering those who uphold the scripture—their transgression is profoundly grave. After the end of their lives, they shall fall into the great hells, with no hope of escape.

Not only is the sin of disrespecting the gods and slandering the scripture severe. Again, if there are foolish and benighted men of perverse views and obstinate delusion who, upon beholding those who recite and uphold this scripture—*beholding* meaning to see with their own eyes—give rise to all manner of evil and rebellion, lacking faith in their hearts, failing to recognize that the scripture contains the words of the Dao and the teachings of the Dharma, and that upholding it brings benefit, they grow arrogant and dismissive, despising and slandering it. They give rise to all manner of transgressions and rebellious acts, casting sidelong, crooked glances, unwilling to see the scripture or those who uphold it. They lack the proper gaze of settled observation, instead casting biased, perverse glances, treating them with contempt, aversion, and disdain. Even if they harbor a single malicious thought or utter a single wicked word, recklessly slandering those who uphold the scripture—*slander* meaning to praise or defame—their offense is grave. Upholding the scripture is a virtuous act and must not be defamed. Yet these wicked and obstinate men, ignorant of karmic causes, sins, and blessings, unaware of the goodness of upholding the scripture, recklessly generate slanderous, abusive, and reviling speech against those who uphold it. Their transgression is profoundly grave. After the end of their lives—*end* meaning their allotted span is exhausted.
